Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
12 min
The Hadith of Musarrah and Prioritizing Qiyas over Khabar Wahid
Explaining the hadith of musarrah and the ikhtilaf among scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a khabar wahid may be set aside in favor of qiyas when the narrator is not a faqih and accepting the hadith would close the door of qiyas.

Core Idea
A khabar wahid conflicting with qiyas may be abandoned if the narrator lacks fiqh and the hadith would nullify qiyas.

This lesson delves into a key Hanafi usul rule: when a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) contradicts the established method of qiyas, and the narrator is trustworthy but not a jurist (faqih), the Hanafi school may set aside the literal meaning of the hadith. The classic example is the hadith of musarrah, where the Prophet (ﷺ) ordered a sa' of dates as compensation for milk consumed from a misrepresented animal. This ruling appears to conflict with the general principle of damages (daman), which requires an equivalent (mithl) for fungibles and market value (qimah) for non-fungibles. The lesson examines how different schools resolve this conflict and the methodological reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hadith and Its Ruling
Read the hadith of musarrah carefully. Note the ruling: the buyer has the option to keep the animal or return it along with a sa' of dates as compensation for the milk consumed. This is the apparent meaning of the text.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Hurayra, who is known for his vast memory but not particularly for his juristic expertise.
2
Recognize the Conflict with Qiyas
Compare the hadith's ruling with the general legal principle of daman. For fungible goods (mithliyyat) like milk, compensation should be by equivalent (mithl), i.e., milk or its value. A fixed sa' of dates regardless of milk quantity contradicts this principle. Identify this as the point of istihsan or tarjih.
The Hanafi school views this contradiction as significant because qiyas is a primary source (Quran 59:2).
3
Understand the Hanafi Condition on Narrators
The Hanafi usul holds that if a narrator is known for 'adalah (moral integrity) and accuracy (dabt), but not for deep fiqh (understanding of legal implications), then when his hadith contradicts qiyas, there is a possibility that he transmitted the meaning (riwaya bi al-ma'na) and made an error. In such cases, the hadith may be set aside under extreme necessity (e.g., if accepting it would close the door of qiyas entirely).
This is not a reflection on the narrator's integrity but a methodological caution.
4
Apply the Usul Rule to the Dispute
Now apply this rule to the musarrah case. According to Abu Hanifa, because the hadith directly contradicts the clear qiyas principle, and because Abu Hurayra was not a faqih, the hadith is not applied literally. Instead, the buyer keeps the animal and recovers the deficiency (arsh) from the seller. Contrast this with the positions of Malik and al-Shafi'i (literal application) and of Abu Yusuf and Ibn Abi Layla (value of milk).
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is the difference in compensation.
5
Summarize the Thamarah al-Khilaf
List the three outcomes: (1) Malik/Shafi'i: return animal + sa' dates; (2) Abu Yusuf/Ibn Abi Layla: return animal + value of milk; (3) Abu Hanifa: keep animal + claim arsh. Recognize that the Hanafi position is the most restrictive on returning the animal due to the priority of qiyas.
The Hanafi school's approach is consistent with its broader usul: khabar wahid is zanni, and qiyas jaliy can override it in cases of strong contradiction.

اور ذوات القیم ( قیمت والی چیز وانا میں) قیمت سے تاوان دیا جاتا ہے۔ فضمان اللبن المشروب البذا جس دودھ کو پی لیا گیا ہے۔ اس کا تاوان دودھ سے دیا جائے۔ یا اُس کی قیمت سے ادا کیا جائے اور کھجور ہی سے تاوان دینا مقصود ہو تو د دودھ کی کمی و زیادتی کے مطابق دیا جائے۔ قیاس یہ نہیں کہتا کہ کھجور ایک صارع دینا ہو گا۔ خواہ دودھ کی مقدار کم ہو یا اس سے زائد ہو۔ امام مالک اور امام شافعی ظاہر حدیث کی طرف گئے ہیں اور حضرت ابن ابی لیلیٰ اور حضرت ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ دودھ کی قیمت واپس کرے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کا نہ ہب یہ ہے کہ اس کو جانور واپس کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے البتہ اس سے اس کا جو نقصان واقع ہوا ہے وہ لے سکتا ہے مگر جانور اپنے پاس رکھے۔ دوسرے شراح نے بھی امام صاحب کا قول اس طرح نقل فرمایا ہے۔
...and its meaning is that if the buyer falls into this deception, then if he is pleased with it, it is good and fine; if he is displeased, he returns it and returns a sa' of dates as compensation for the milk he consumed on the first day. So this hadith contradicts analogy in every respect, because the guarantee of torts and all sales is determined by the equivalent in fungible things and by value in non-fungibles. Therefore, the guarantee of the milk drunk should be by milk or by value, and if it were by dates, it should be measured by the smallness or abundance of the milk, not that a sa' of dates is obligatory regardless of whether the milk is little or much. So Malik and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on them) followed the apparent meaning of the hadith; Ibn Abi Layla and Abu Yusuf held that the value of the milk should be returned; and Abu Hanifa held that he does not have the right to return [the animal], but he recovers the deficiency from the seller and keeps the animal. This is how some of the commentators have transmitted. And if [the narrator] is known for 'adalah (moral integrity) and accuracy, but not known for fiqh...
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a usul discussion using the hadith of musarrah (tying up an animal's udder to deceive the buyer) as an example of a khabar wahid that contradicts qiyas. The author first explains the hadith: the Prophet (ﷺ) gave the deceived buyer the option to keep or return the animal, and if he returns it, he must give a sa' of dates as compensation for the milk he consumed. The author notes that this ruling contradicts the general principle of damages (daman), which requires an equivalent (mithl) for fungible goods and market value (qimah) for non-fungibles. Milk is normally compensated by its equivalent (milk) or value, not a fixed measure of dates. The author then presents the positions of the schools: Malik and al-Shafi'i follow the hadith literally; Ibn Abi Layla and Abu Yusuf say the buyer returns the value of the milk; Abu Hanifa says the buyer cannot return the animal but may claim the deficiency in price (arsh). The commentary clarifies that this is an example where the Hanafi madhhab prioritizes qiyas over a khabar wahid when the narrator is not a faqih, due to the possibility of error in meaning-based transmission. The Urdu section elaborates on the condition of the narrator: if the narrator is known for 'adalah but not for fiqh (like Anas and Abu Hurayra), then if the hadith agrees with qiyas, it is accepted; if it contradicts qiyas, it may be set aside in cases of extreme necessity (e.g., if accepting the hadith would close the door of qiyas altogether, which would contradict the Quranic command to use analogy). The author stresses that this is not a disrespect to the Companions but a methodological point that the narrator may have misunderstood the meaning of the hadith.

Key Terms
مصراة (musarrah): An animal whose udder has been left unmilked for several days before sale to deceive the buyer into thinking it gives much milk.
ضمان (daman): Legal liability or compensation for damage or loss.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary report that does not reach the level of tawatur; its authenticity (thubut) is considered zanni (speculative).
أرش (arsh): Compensation for a deficiency or loss, particularly in sale transactions (e.g., when an animal has a defect).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the buyer's remedy in the case of a musarrah animal?
A) He must return the animal and give a sa' of dates.
B) He may return the animal and claim the value of the milk.
C) He cannot return the animal but can claim the deficiency (arsh) from the seller and keep the animal.
D) He has no remedy and must keep the animal as is.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes qiyas over a khabar wahid when the narrator is not a faqih and accepting the hadith would abandon the divinely commanded use of analogy.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Dispute on Fiqh al-Rawi: Isa ibn Aban vs al-Karkhi
Usul dispute on narrator's fiqh as condition for khabar wahid over qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on whether a narrator's juristic knowledge (fiqh al-rawi) is a condition for taking a khabar wahid over qiyas, and evaluate the arguments for each view.

Core Idea
A trustworthy narrator's fiqh knowledge determines whether his solitary hadith can set aside qiyas—Isa ibn Aban requires it, al-Karkhi does not.

The Hanafi school does not uniformly accept every solitary hadith (khabar wahid) over qiyas. A key internal dispute concerns the intellectual qualification of the narrator: does the narrator need to be a jurist (faqih) for his hadith to override analogical reasoning? This passage presents the views of two great Hanafi usul scholars—Isa ibn Aban and al-Karkhi—and their respective proofs. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to evaluate how Hanafi usul balances scriptural and rational evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
What exactly is being disputed? Is it about the reliability or the juristic competence of the narrator?
The dispute is about the condition of 'fiqh al-rawi'.
2
Extract the two positions
State Isa ibn Aban’s condition (narrator must be known for fiqh) and al-Karkhi’s counter-position (trustworthiness alone suffices).
Both are Hanafi positions.
3
Analyze the proofs for al-Karkhi’s view
What examples does he give (Hammal ibn Malik, vomiting hadith) and why do they support his position?
These hadiths contradict qiyas but were accepted by 'Umar and the Companions.
4
Consider the implied Hanafi response for Isa ibn Aban
How would Isa ibn Aban counter those examples?
The text does not give it explicitly, but from context: the narrators were either faqihs or the hadith was mutawatir in meaning.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf)
How does this dispute affect actual fatwa? Which hadiths might be accepted or rejected depending on the view adopted?
Isa's view may reject some ahad hadiths, Karkhi's accepts them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ هَذِهِ التَّفْرِقَةُ بَيْنَ المَعْرُوفِ بِالْفِقْهِ وَ الْعَدَالَةِ مَذْهَبُ عِيْسَى بْنِ أَبَانَ وَتَابَعَة أكْثَرُ المُتَاخَرِينَ وَأَمَّا عِنْدَ الْكَرْخِي وَمَنْ تَابَعَهُ مِنْ أَصْحَابِنَا فَلَيْسَ فِتْهُ الرَّاوِى شرطًا لِتَقَدَّمَ الْحَدِيثِ عَلَى الْقِيَاسِ بَلْ خَبَرُ كُلِّ رَاقٍ عَدْلٍ مُقَدَّمَ عَلَى الْقِيَاسِ إذَا لَمْ يَكُن مُخَالِفًا لِلْكِتَابِ والسَّنْةِ المَشْهُورَةِ وَلِهَذَا قُبِلَ عُمَرُ حَدِيثَ حَمْلِ بْنِ مَالِك فِي الْجَنِيْنِ وَأَوْجَبَ الْقُرْةُ فِيهِ مَعَ أَنَّهُ مُخَالِف لِلْقِيَاسِ لأَنَّ الْجَنِيْنَ إِنْ كَانَ حَيًّا وَجَبَتْ الذِيْةُ كَامِلَةً وَأَنْ كَانَتْ مَيْتًا فَلَا شَيْء فِيْهِ وَأَمَّا حَدِيثُ الْوُضُوع عَلى مَنْ قَيْقَةَ في الصلوة فَهُوَ وَأَنْ كَانَ مُخَالِفًا لِلْقَيَاسِ لكِنْ رَوَاهُ عِدَّةٌ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ الْكَبْرَاءِ كَجَابِرٍ وَأَنَسٍ وغَيْرِهِمَا وَلِذَاكَانَ مُقَدِّمًا عَلَى الْقِيَاسِ
Then this differentiation between one known for fiqh and one known for 'adalah is the madhhab of 'Isa ibn Aban, and most of the later scholars followed him. As for al-Karkhi and those of our companions who followed him, the fiqh of the narrator is not a condition for the hadith to take precedence over qiyas; rather, the report of every trustworthy narrator takes precedence over qiyas as long as it does not contradict the Book or the well-known Sunnah. For this reason, 'Umar accepted the hadith of Hammal ibn Malik regarding the fetus and imposed the ghurrah (compensation) in it, even though it contradicts qiyas, because if the fetus had been alive, full blood-money would be due, and if it had been dead, nothing would be due. As for the hadith of vomiting [؟] in prayer, even though it contradicts qiyas, several major Companions like Jabir and Anas and others narrated it, so it is given precedence over qiyas.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is an usul dispute regarding the condition of the narrator's knowledge of fiqh (fiqh al-rawi) for accepting a khabar wahid that contradicts qiyas. The author presents two views within the Hanafi school. First, 'Isa ibn Aban (a Hanafi scholar) and the majority of later Hanafis (mutakhkhirin) hold that if the narrator is known for 'adalah but not for fiqh, then his hadith may be set aside when it contradicts qiyas, because a non-faqih might have misunderstood the meaning of the hadith. However, if the narrator is known for both 'adalah and fiqh, his hadith is accepted even if it contradicts qiyas. Second, al-Karkhi and his followers do not require the narrator to be a faqih; the report of any trustworthy (adl) narrator is given precedence over qiyas, provided it does not conflict with the Quran or widely known Sunnah. Al-Karkhi supports his view with the example of 'Umar accepting the hadith of Hammal ibn Malik about the ghurrah for a fetus. The hadith imposed a ghurrah (a slave or equivalent), which contradicts qiyas because if the fetus was alive, full diyah would be due, and if dead, nothing. Yet 'Umar accepted it because the narrator was trustworthy. Similarly, the hadith about vomiting (al-wudu' min al-qay') in prayer, even though it contradicts qiyas (since vomiting is not like other impurities that invalidate wudu), is accepted because it was narrated by several major Companions. The commentary highlights the methodological difference: for Isa ibn Aban, the intellectual competence of the narrator is crucial; for al-Karkhi, reliability (adalah) suffices.

Key Terms
فقه الراوي (fiqh al-rawi): The narrator's knowledge and understanding of Islamic law, allowing him to accurately transmit the meaning of a hadith without error.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith narrated by one or a few individuals, not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Karkhi, what condition is required for a khabar wahid to take precedence over qiyas?
A) The narrator must be a faqih.
B) The narrator must be trustworthy (adl) and the hadith must not contradict the Quran or well-known Sunnah.
C) The hadith must be narrated by at least two Companions.
D) The hadith must be from the six authentic books.

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, there is a legitimate ikhtilaf on whether a narrator's fiqh knowledge is required for his solitary hadith to set aside qiyas, with Isa ibn Aban requiring it and al-Karkhi not.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Condition for Hadith to Override Qiyas: Isa ibn Aban vs. al-Karkhi
Usul dispute on narrator condition for hadith over qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions (Isa ibn Aban vs. al-Karkhi) on the condition for a narrator's fiqh expertise in preferring hadith over qiyas, and evaluate the proofs for each.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school splits: some require the narrator to be a faqih, others hold that justice alone suffices for his hadith to override qiyas.

In this passage, the author presents a key internal Hanafi dispute: must a narrator be recognized as both a faqih (expert in fiqh) and 'adl (just) for his hadith to be given precedence over analogical reasoning (qiyas)? Isa ibn Aban and later scholars say yes; al-Karkhi and his followers say no. Let's trace the arguments and evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the first few lines of the passage to find and contrast the views of Isa ibn Aban and al-Karkhi on the condition for preferring hadith over qiyas.
Isa ibn Aban requires the narrator to be known for both fiqh and justice; al-Karkhi requires only justice, provided the hadith does not contradict the Quran and well-known Sunnah.
2
Examine the proof from Umar’s acceptance
Consider the example of Umar accepting the hadith of Haml ibn Malik on the ghurra (compensation) for a fetus, despite it contradicting qiyas. How does this support al-Karkhi’s view?
Haml was not necessarily a faqih, yet his hadith was accepted over qiyas.
3
Examine the proof from the laughter-in-prayer hadith
Analyze the second example: the hadith on wudu due to laughter in prayer, narrated by several major Companions. How does this strengthen al-Karkhi’s position?
The multiplicity of narrators may compensate for the lack of fiqh expertise, but the key is that the hadith was accepted despite contradicting qiyas.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference between the two opinions. Under which view would more ahadith be accepted to override qiyas?
Al-Karkhi’s view is more inclusive; Isa ibn Aban’s view is more restrictive.
5
Assess the tarjih in the text
Determine which view the author seems to favor. Look for clues such as the weight of evidence and mention of Imam A‘zam’s general acceptance of hadith.
The author presents more evidence for al-Karkhi’s view and notes that Imam A‘zam accepted all hadith from Allah and His Messenger.

Then this distinction between one known for fiqh and justice is the madhhab of Isa ibn Aban, and most of the later scholars followed him. But according to al-Karkhi and those of our companions who followed him, the condition of the narrator being a faqih is not required for preferring hadith over qiyas; rather, the report of every just narrator is preferred over qiyas, provided it does not contradict the Book and the well-known Sunnah. And for this reason, Umar accepted the hadith of Haml ibn Malik concerning the fetus and imposed the ghurra (compensation) therein, even though it contradicted qiyas, because if the fetus was alive, full blood-money would be due, and if it was dead, nothing would be due. As for the hadith of wudu due to laughter in prayer, although it contradicts qiyas, it was narrated by several major Companions such as Jabir and Anas and others, so it was preferred over qiyas. And if the narrator is unknown (majhul) – i.e., in narrating hadith and justice, not in lineage – such that he is only known through one or two hadith, like Wabisah ibn Ma'bad, then his condition does not go beyond five categories. If the salaf narrated from him, or they differed about him, or they remained silent about criticizing him, then he becomes like a known narrator in all three categories, because the narration of the salaf is evidence of his authenticity, and silence about criticism is equivalent to their acceptance, so it is accepted. As for the disputed one, they gave as an example the narration that Ibn Mas'ud was asked about marrying a woman without naming a mahr until he died, so he made ijtihad for a month and said: 'I have heard nothing from the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) but I will make ijtihad with my opinion: if I am correct, it is from Allah; if I err, it is from me and from Satan. I see for her the mahr of women like her, without excess or deficiency.' Then Ma'qil ibn Sinan stood and said: 'I bear witness that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) judged in the case of Barwa' bint Washiq similarly to your judgment.' So Ibn Mas'ud was extremely pleased that his judgment coincided with the judgment of the Messenger of Allah (PBUH). Translation and explanation: Then this distinction between the one known for fiqh and justice is the madhhab of Isa ibn Aban, and most of the later scholars followed him. According to Imam Karkhi and our companions who followed him, it is not conditional for the narrator to be a faqih for preferring hadith over qiyas; rather, every just narrator's report is preferred over qiyas, as long as it is not contrary to the Book and well-known Sunnah. The research of Imam A'zam is that any hadith that reaches us from Allah and His Messenger is accepted. For this reason, Umar (RA) accepted the hadith of Haml ibn Malik regarding killing a fetus and imposed the ghurra (500 dirhams) despite it being against qiyas, because if the fetus is considered alive, full blood-money would be due, and if dead, nothing. Similarly, the hadith making wudu obligatory due to laughter in prayer, although contrary to qiyas, was narrated by many great Companions like Jabir and Anas, so it is accepted and preferred over qiyas. And if the narrator is unknown in terms of hadith narration and justice (but not in lineage), he is known only through one or two hadith, like Wabisah ibn Ma'bad. The condition of such a narrator is not free from five categories. If the salaf narrated from him, or they differed about him, or they remained silent about criticizing him, then in these three categories his narration is like that of a known narrator, because the salaf's narrating from him is testimony to his authenticity, and silence about criticism is tantamount to acceptance. So it is accepted. As for the disputed one, they gave the example of what is narrated that Ibn Mas'ud was asked about...
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is an usul dispute about the condition for preferring a hadith over qiyas. The text presents two positions. The first, attributed to Isa ibn Aban and followed by later scholars, distinguishes between a narrator known for fiqh and justice and one who is merely just; only the former's hadith overrides qiyas. The second, attributed to al-Karkhi and his followers among the Hanafis, holds that any just narrator's hadith is preferred over qiyas, provided it does not contradict the Quran or well-known Sunnah. The author then provides evidence: Umar's acceptance of Haml ibn Malik's hadith on the ghurra for the fetus, and the hadith on wudu due to laughter, narrated by multiple Companions. The discussion then turns to the case of a majhul (unknown) narrator. The text explains that if the salaf narrated from him, or differed about him, or remained silent about criticizing him, his narration is treated like that of a known narrator. The example of Ibn Mas'ud's ijtihad on the mahr of a woman whose husband died without fixing a dower is given to illustrate a case where a hadith corroborates a judgment. This passage shows the Hanafi internal differences on the conditions for prioritizing hadith over qiyas, and the careful scrutiny of narrator reliability.

Key Terms
معروف بالفقه والعدالة (ma'ruf bi al-fiqh wa al-'adalah): A narrator known for both proficiency in fiqh and upright character (justice).
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that may be overridden by a hadith under certain conditions.
عدل (adl): Just, upright narrator; one whose character is free from major sins and who maintains virtue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Karkhi's view in this passage, what is the primary condition for a hadith to be preferred over qiyas?
A) The narrator must be known for fiqh and justice.
B) The narrator must be a major Companion.
C) The narrator must be just, and the hadith must not contradict the Quran and well-known Sunnah.
D) The hadith must be mutawatir.

Key Takeaway
The condition for a hadith to override qiyas is disputed within the Hanafi school: al-Karkhi requires only justice, while Isa ibn Aban requires both fiqh and justice.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Acceptance of a Majhul Narrator's Hadith to Override Qiyas
Usul classification of majhul narrator acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five categories of a majhul narrator and state which three categories lead to acceptance of his hadith for overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
A majhul narrator's hadith can override qiyas if the salaf narrated from him, differed about him, or remained silent about criticizing him.

This passage continues the discussion on narrator conditions, focusing on the case of a narrator whose reliability is unknown (majhul). The text breaks down the possible scenarios into five categories, three of which make his narration equivalent to that of a known narrator. Let's unpack these categories and see how they apply to a real case from the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Define 'majhul' in this context
Read the definition: a narrator unknown in hadith narration and justice, but known in lineage.
The unknown here is specific to hadith expertise, not general obscurity.
2
List the five categories
The text mentions five categories in total, but only describes three in the source: (1) the salaf narrated from him, (2) they differed about him, (3) they remained silent about criticizing him. The other two are not detailed.
The three described lead to acceptance; the remaining two presumably do not.
3
Understand the logic behind acceptance
Why does narration by the salaf, difference, or silence lead to acceptance? The text says narration is testimony to authenticity, and silence about criticism is equivalent to acceptance.
This is a principle: the practice of the early generations can elevate an unknown narrator's status.
4
Examine the example of Ibn Mas'ud
The passage gives the story of Ibn Mas'ud's ijtihad on a woman's mahr after her husband dies without fixing it. His judgment was later confirmed by a hadith from Ma'qil ibn Sinan. How does this illustrate the acceptance of a majhul narrator?
The story shows that even when a narrator is not widely known, corroboration from a known Companion (Ma'qil) is accepted.
5
Apply the categories to the example
Determine which category Ma'qil ibn Sinan falls into. He was a Companion but not a major narrator; his hadith was accepted because the salaf (including Ibn Mas'ud) acted upon it.
This corresponds to the first category: the salaf narrated from him and acted upon his report.

وَأَنَسٍ وغَيْرِهِمَا وَلِذَاكَانَ مُقَدِّمًا عَلَى الْقِيَاسِ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَجْهُولًاً أَي فِي رِوَايَةِ الْحَدِيْثِ وَالْعَدَالَةِ لَافِي النَّسَبِ بِأَنْ لَمْ يُعْرَف الا بِحَدِيث أَوْ حَدِيثَيْنِ كَوَابِصَةَ مِنْ مَعْبَدٍ فَحَالُهُ لا يَخْلُوْا عَنْ خَمْسَةِ أَقْسَامِ فَإِنْ روَى عَنْهُ السَّلَف أَوْ اخْتَلَفُوا فِيْهِ أَوْ سَكَتُوا عَنِ الطَّعْن صَارَ كَالْمَعْرُوفِ فِي كُلر من الأقسام الظُّلقَةِ لأَنْ رِوَايَةَ السَّلْفِ شَاهِدَةً بَصَحَتِهِ وَالسَّكُوتُ عَنْ الطِّعْنِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ قُبُوْلِهِمْ فَإِذَا يُقْبَلُ وَأَمَّا الْمُخْتَلَفَ مِنْهُ فَاوْرَدُوا فِي مِثَالِهِ مَارُوِيَ أَنَّ ابْنَاشرف الانوار شرح اردو ۱۴ نور الانوار جلد سوم شیر مَسْعُودٍ سُبُلَ عَنْ تَزَوجِ اِمْرَاةٍ وَلَمْ يُسمُ لَهَا مَهْرًا حَتى مَاتِ عَنْهَا فَاجْتَهَدَ شهْرًا وَقالَ بَعْدَ ذلِكَ مَا سَمِعْتُ مِنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ شَيْئًا وَلَكِنْ أَجْتِهِدُ بَرَاثَى فَإِنْ أَصَبُتُ فَمِنَ اللهِ وَإِنْ اِخْطَأْتُ فَمِنِّى وَمِنَ الشَّيْطَانِ أَرَى لَهَا مَهْرَ مَثْلِ نِسائِهَا لأَوَكَسَ وَلَا شَطَطَ فَقَامَ مَعْقَلُ بُن سِنَانٍ وَقَالَ أَشْهَدُ اَنْ رَسُوْلَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَى آلِهِ وَعَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَضِي فِي بِرُدَعُ بِئْتِ وَاشِقٍ مِثْلَ قَضائِكَ فَسَرُ أَبْنُ مَسْعُودٍ سُرُوْرًا لَمْ يُرْمِثْلَهُ قَطُّ لِمُوَافَقَةِ قَضَائِهِ قَضَاءَ رسول الله صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّم. ترجم و تشريح ثم هذه التفرقة بين المعروف بالفقه والعدالة پر معروف بالفقة و معروف بالعدالة کے درمیان فرق و امتیاز پیدا کرنا عیسی ابن ابان کا مذہب ہے اور اکثر متاخرین نے اُن کا اتباع فرمایا ہے۔ اور بہر حال امام کرخی اور ہمارے اصحاب کس سے جنھوں نے اُن کا اتباع فرمایا ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ حدیث کو قیاس پر مقدم کرنے اور ترجیح دینے کے لئے کمی کا فقیہ ہو نا مشروط نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ ہر راد بی عادل کی خبر قیاس پر مقدم ہے۔ جب کہ کتاب اللہ اور سنت مشہورہ کے خلاف نہ واقع ہو اس باب میں تحقیقی بات امام اعظم کی ہے آپ نے فرمایا خدا اور رسول کی طرف سے جو حدیث ہم تک پہونچے وہ ہمارے سر آنکھوں پر ہے۔ ولهذا قيل عمر رضى الله عنه - اس وجہ سے حضرت عمر فاروق رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے حمل بن مالک کی حدیث کو قتل جنین کے بارے میں قبول فرمالیا تھا اور تاوان و ا جنب قرار دیا تھا۔ غر پانچ سو در نیم) باوجودیکہ وہ قیاس کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ جنین اگر زیرہ شمار کیا جاتا ہے تو کامل دیت واجب ہونی چاہئے اور اگر وہ مردہ ہے تو کوئی دیت واجب نہ ہونا چاہیے۔ اور بہر حال بحالت صلوۃ قہقہہ سرزد ہونے کی صوورت میں وضو کے واجب کرنے والی حدیث یعنی الوضوع على من قهقه فی الصلوة - اگر چہ مخالف قیاس ہے مگر اس روایت کے متعدد بڑے بڑے اگرچہ صحابہ جیسے حضرت جابر رضی اللہ عنہ اور حضرت انس رضی اللہ عنہ اور اُن کے علاوہ دوسرے صحابہ نے روایت فرمایا ہے اس کو قبول کیا گیا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے قیاس پر مقدم ہو گی۔ و ان كان مجهولاً ۔ اور راوی اگر مجہول ہو یعنی روایت حدیث اور عدالت میں نہ نسب میں جان لم يعرف الا يحدیث او حدیثین بایں طور کے وہ علاوہ ایک دو حدیث روایت کرنے کے معروف نہ ہو۔ جیسے حضرت والبہ بن معید تو ایسے راوی کی حالت پانچ اقسام سے خالی نہیں ہے۔ فان روى عنه السلف الخ اگر اُس سے سلف نے باتفاق روایت کی یا اُس سے روایت کرنے میں باہم مختلف ہو گئے۔ یا سب نے اس راوی کو مطعون کرنے سے خاموشی اختیار کرلی تو اُن تینوں قسموں میں اس مجہول الحال راوی کی روایت معروف راوی کی طرح ہوگی یعنی ان تینوں حالتوں میں کیونکہ سلف کارواہمت کر لینا اس کے صحیح ہونے کی شہادت ہے اور طعن و
Then this distinction between one known for fiqh and justice is the madhhab of Isa ibn Aban, and most of the later scholars followed him. But according to al-Karkhi and those of our companions who followed him, the condition of the narrator being a faqih is not required for preferring hadith over qiyas; rather, the report of every just narrator is preferred over qiyas, provided it does not contradict the Book and the well-known Sunnah. And for this reason, Umar accepted the hadith of Haml ibn Malik concerning the fetus and imposed the ghurra (compensation) therein, even though it contradicted qiyas, because if the fetus was alive, full blood-money would be due, and if it was dead, nothing would be due. As for the hadith of wudu due to laughter in prayer, although it contradicts qiyas, it was narrated by several major Companions such as Jabir and Anas and others, so it was preferred over qiyas. And if the narrator is unknown (majhul) – i.e., in narrating hadith and justice, not in lineage – such that he is only known through one or two hadith, like Wabisah ibn Ma'bad, then his condition does not go beyond five categories. If the salaf narrated from him, or they differed about him, or they remained silent about criticizing him, then he becomes like a known narrator in all three categories, because the narration of the salaf is evidence of his authenticity, and silence about criticism is equivalent to their acceptance, so it is accepted. As for the disputed one, they gave as an example the narration that Ibn Mas'ud was asked about marrying a woman without naming a mahr until he died, so he made ijtihad for a month and said: 'I have heard nothing from the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) but I will make ijtihad with my opinion: if I am correct, it is from Allah; if I err, it is from me and from Satan. I see for her the mahr of women like her, without excess or deficiency.' Then Ma'qil ibn Sinan stood and said: 'I bear witness that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) judged in the case of Barwa' bint Washiq similarly to your judgment.' So Ibn Mas'ud was extremely pleased that his judgment coincided with the judgment of the Messenger of Allah (PBUH). Translation and explanation: Then this distinction between the one known for fiqh and justice is the madhhab of Isa ibn Aban, and most of the later scholars followed him. According to Imam Karkhi and our companions who followed him, it is not conditional for the narrator to be a faqih for preferring hadith over qiyas; rather, every just narrator's report is preferred over qiyas, as long as it is not contrary to the Book and well-known Sunnah. The research of Imam A'zam is that any hadith that reaches us from Allah and His Messenger is accepted. For this reason, Umar (RA) accepted the hadith of Haml ibn Malik regarding killing a fetus and imposed the ghurra (500 dirhams) despite it being against qiyas, because if the fetus is considered alive, full blood-money would be due, and if dead, nothing. Similarly, the hadith making wudu obligatory due to laughter in prayer, although contrary to qiyas, was narrated by many great Companions like Jabir and Anas, so it is accepted and preferred over qiyas. And if the narrator is unknown in terms of hadith narration and justice (but not in lineage), he is known only through one or two hadith, like Wabisah ibn Ma'bad. The condition of such a narrator is not free from five categories. If the salaf narrated from him, or they differed about him, or they remained silent about criticizing him, then in these three categories his narration is like that of a known narrator, because the salaf's narrating from him is testimony to his authenticity, and silence about criticism is tantamount to acceptance. So it is accepted. As for the disputed one, they gave the example of what is narrated that Ibn Mas'ud was asked about...
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is an usul dispute about the condition for preferring a hadith over qiyas. The text presents two positions. The first, attributed to Isa ibn Aban and followed by later scholars, distinguishes between a narrator known for fiqh and justice and one who is merely just; only the former's hadith overrides qiyas. The second, attributed to al-Karkhi and his followers among the Hanafis, holds that any just narrator's hadith is preferred over qiyas, provided it does not contradict the Quran or well-known Sunnah. The author then provides evidence: Umar's acceptance of Haml ibn Malik's hadith on the ghurra for the fetus, and the hadith on wudu due to laughter, narrated by multiple Companions. The discussion then turns to the case of a majhul (unknown) narrator. The text explains that if the salaf narrated from him, or differed about him, or remained silent about criticizing him, his narration is treated like that of a known narrator. The example of Ibn Mas'ud's ijtihad on the mahr of a woman whose husband died without fixing a dower is given to illustrate a case where a hadith corroborates a judgment. This passage shows the Hanafi internal differences on the conditions for prioritizing hadith over qiyas, and the careful scrutiny of narrator reliability.

Key Terms
مجهول (majhul): An unknown narrator, specifically one not well-known in hadith narration and justice, but known in lineage.
سلف (salaf): The early generations of Muslims, especially the Companions, Followers, and early scholars.
اختلفوا فيه (ikhtalafu fihi): They differed about him – i.e., some scholars accepted his narration, others rejected it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three categories that make a majhul narrator's hadith accepted to override qiyas?
A) The salaf narrated from him.
B) A later scholar praised him.
C) The salaf differed about him.
D) The salaf remained silent about criticizing him.

Key Takeaway
A majhul narrator's hadith can be accepted to override qiyas if the salaf narrated from him, differed about him, or remained silent about criticizing him.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
12 min
Rules of Ta'n: When Hadith Loses Its Evidentiary Value in Hanafi Usul
Expansion on rules of ta'n in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five types of ta'n (criticism) that affect a hadith's evidentiary value and apply the Hanafi rule that a narrator's certain contradiction voids the hadith as evidence.

Core Idea
A narrator's certain contradiction of his own narration proves abrogation or unreliability, voiding the hadith as evidence.

In this lesson, we examine the rules of ta'n (criticism) of hadith from the Hanafi usul perspective. The passage from Ashraf al-Anwar explains five scenarios where a hadith loses its binding authority due to the action or stance of the narrator or the companion. We will analyze each scenario and the underlying principles, with examples from sahaba and differences with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five scenarios of ta'n
From the passage, list the five circumstances that give rise to criticism (ta'n) of a hadith: denial by the one narrated from, narrator acting contrary after narration with certainty, narrator acting contrary before narration or date unknown, narrator specifying one possible interpretation over others, and a companion's action contrary to a clear hadith.
These scenarios are not exclusive but represent the main categories discussed.
2
Determine the Hanafi ruling for each scenario
For each scenario, extract whether the hadith is rejected or remains valid. For sure action contrary to narration, the hadith is void; for uncertainty or interpretation, it may remain valid.
Pay attention to the distinction between certainty and doubt.
3
Analyze the example of Ibn Umar and raising hands
Ibn Umar narrated that the Prophet raised his hands at bowing and rising, but Mujahid observed that Ibn Umar himself did not practice it except in the opening takbir. The Hanafi ruling: Ibn Umar's abandonment indicates the hadith is abrogated (mansukh).
This is a classic usul example of a narrator's action contradicting his narration.
4
Examine the dispute over exile punishment
The hadith of Ubadah ibn as-Samit says the unmarried fornicator is flogged and exiled. Al-Shafi'i takes exile as a fixed punishment (hadd). The Hanafi response: Caliph Umar exiled an apostate and then swore never to exile again, proving exile is a policy (siyasa), not a fixed punishment. Thus, the companion's action clarifies the hadith.
This illustrates how a companion's action affects interpretation of a clear text.
5
Distinguish interpretation from contradiction
When a narrator interprets a general or ambiguous hadith in a specific way (e.g., Ibn Umar's interpretation of 'separation' as physical parting), this does not prevent acting on other valid interpretations. Only when the action is clearly contrary does it void the hadith.
The key is whether the text is open to interpretation (muhtamal) or clear (zahir).

يَرْفَعْ يَدَيْهِ عِنْدَ الرُّكُوعِ وَعِنْدَ رَفْعِ الرَّاسِ مِنَ الرُّكُوعِ وَقَدْ صَعْ عَنِ مُجَاهِدٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ صَحِبْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ عَشْرَ سِنِينَ فَلَمْ أَرَاهُ يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ إِلا فِى تَكْبِيرَةِ الافتتاح فتَرْك الْعَمَل بِهِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى انْتِسَاخِه.
ترجمہ و تشریح اس عیب کا بیان جو حدیث کو لاحق ہوتا ہے ۔ وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ عَنْ بَيَانِ التُقْسِبُعَاتِ الْأَرْبَعِ ہے۔ مصنف جب سنت کی چاروں تقسیموں سے فارغ ہو گئے تو انھوں نے اس طعن (عیب ) کا بیان شروع کیا جو حدیث کو راوی کی جانب سے یا اس کے غیر سے لاحق ہوا کرتا ہے۔ تو فرما لو المروى عنه اذا أنكر الروایۃ اور مروی عنہ جب سرے سے روایت کا انکار کر دے پس اگر انکار جامد ہے (یعنی جان بوجھ کر انکار کرنے والا ) بایں طور کہ وہ کہتا ہے تو نے مجھ پر جھوٹ بولا حالا نکہ یہ حدیث میں نے تجھ سے روایت نہیں کی تو اس قسم کا انکار بالا تفاق عمل بالحدیث کو ساقط کر دیتا ہے اور اگر انکار متوقف ہے (یعنی کسی تامل کرنے والے نے انکار کیا ہو ) مزادہ کہتا ہے مجھے یاد نہیں ہے کہ میں نے تم سے یہ حدیث روایت کی ہے یاوہ کہتا ہے کہ میں یہ حدیث نہیں جانتا تو اس میں ائمہ کا اختلاف ہے امام کرتی اور احمد بن فضیل کے نزدیک اس روایت پر مکمل ساقط ہے اور امام شافعی اور امام مالک کے نزدیک عمل ساقط نہیں ہو گا۔
أَوْ عَمَلَ بِخِلافِهِ بَعْدَ الرواية- یا روایت حدیث کے بعد روایت کرنے والا اس حدیث کے خلاف عمل کرے اور یہ خلاف پورے یقین کے ساتھ ہو تو دونوں صورتوں میں حدیث پیل کرنا ساقط ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ اگر راد کی نے اس حدیث کے منسوخ ہونے کی واقفیت کی وجہ سے اس حدیث کا خلاف کیا ہے یا اس کے موضوع ہونے کی وجہ سے خلاف کیا ہے تو اس روایت سے حجتہ پکڑنا ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر بے پرواہی کی وجہ سے غفلت کی بنا پر اس کے خلاف عمل کیا ہے تو اس کی عدالت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اس کی مثال وہ حدیث ہے جس کو حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہا نے روایت کیا ہے کہ نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے أَيُّمَا امْرَأَةٍ نَكَحَت بِلا الرَّاءِ لِبَعْضٍ مُحْتمَلاتِه اور راوی کا حدیث کے متعدد احتمالات میں سے بعض محتمل کو متعین کر دینا۔ ہائیں طور کہ حدیث لفظ مشترک تھا پس اس نے تاویل کر سکے ایک معنی کو لے لیا اور اس پر مکمل کر لیا۔ لا يَمْنَعُ العمل ہے۔ تو اس کے دوسرے محتمل معنی پرعمل کرنے سے نہیں روکتا ہے جیسے حضرت عبد اللہ بن. عمر رضی اللہ عنہ نے روایت کیا ہے کہ جناب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے۔ المتبايعان بالخيار مَالَمْ يَتَفَرْنَا (بائع اور مشتری کو اس وقت تک اختیار حاصل ہے جب تک دونوں متفرق) جدانہ ہو جائیں اس روایت مالم يتفرقا میں دونوں احتمال ہے تفرق بالابدان اور تفرق بالا اقوال حضرت ابن عمر نے تفرق سے تفرق ابدان مراد لیا ہے جیسا کہ امام شافعی کا مسلک ہے مگر یہ اس بات کے منافی نہیں کہ ہم تفرق بالا توال پر عمل کریں والا متاع اور راوی کا اپنی روایت کردہ حدیث پر عمل کرنے سے رک جانا ویسا ہی ہے جیسا کہ اس روایت کے خلاف عمل کرنا ۔ یعنی عمل اس روایت کے خلاف ہو جس کو اس راوی نے روایت کیا ہے لہذا یہ حدیث حجت ہونے سے خارج ہو جائے گی۔ جیسے حضرت ابن عمر نے روایت کیا کہ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ كَانَ يَرْفَعُ | يَدَيْهِ عِنْدَ الرَّكُوعِ وَعِنْدَ رَفع الراس مِنَ الرَّكُوع كر في كريم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم رکوع میں جاتے وقت اور رکوع سے سر اٹھاتے وقت رفع یدین کرتے تھے حالانکہ حضرت مجاہد سے مروی ہے فرمایا کہ میں حضرت ابن عمر کے ساتھ دس سال تک رہا میں نے رفع یدین کرتے ہوئے علاوہ تکبیر افتتاح کے ان کو نہیں دیکھا۔ لہذا راد کی حدیث کا حدیث پر عمل کا ترک کر دینا اس کے منسوخ ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ وَعَمَلُ الصَّحَابِي بِخَلافِهِ يُوجِبُ الطِّعْنَ إِذَا كَانَ الْحَدِيثِ ظَاهِرًا لَا يَحْتَمِلُ الجفاء عَلَيْهِمْ مِنْ هُنَا شروع فِي الطِّعْنِ مِنْ غَيْرِ الرَّرِئ وَمِثَالُهُ مَا رَوَى عُبَادَةٌ الْخِفَاءَ بن الصَّامِتِ أَنه قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ الْبِكْرُ بِالْبِكْرِ جَلْدُ مِائَةٍ وَتَغْرِيْبُ عَامٍ فَيَتَمسك به الشافعي وَيَجْعَلُ النّفى إلى عَام جَزَاءً مِنْ الْحَد وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ إِنَّ عُمَرَ نَفْسَ رَجَلاً فَارْتَدَّ وَلَحِق بِالرُّومِ فَحَلَفَ أَن لا يَنْفِى أَحَدًا أَبَدًا فَلَوْ كَان النَّفْى حَدًا لَمَا خَلَفَ تَرْكِهِ فَعْلِمَ أنْ النَّفْى سُنَةٌ كَانَ سِيَاسَةٌ لَاحَدًا وَحَدِيثُ الْحُدُودِ كَانَ ظَاهِرًا لا يَحْتَمِلُ الْجِفَاء عَلَى الْخُلَفَاءِ الَّذِيْنَ نُصِبُوا الإِقَامَةِ الْحُدُودِ وَاحْتَرَزَ به عَمَّا كَانَ يَحْتَمِلُ الْخِفَاءَ عَلَيْهِمْ فَإِنَّهُ لا يُوجِبُ جَرْحًا فِيْهِ كَحَدِيثِ وُجُوبِ الْوُضُوءِ بِالْقَيْقَةِ فِي الصَّلَوَةِ رَوَاهُ بْنُ خَالِدِ الْجُهَنِ وَابُو مُوسَى الأَشْعَرِى وَالطَّعْنُ الْمُبْهَمُ مِنْ أَبْعَةِ الْحَدِيثِ لَأَيَجْرَ الرَّاوِى عِنْدَنَا بِأَنْ يَقُولَ هَذَا الْحَدِيث
He would raise his hands at the bowing and at raising the head from bowing, and it is narrated from Mujahid that he said: I accompanied Ibn Umar for ten years and I did not see him raise his hands except in the opening takbir. So abandoning action on it is evidence of its abrogation. Translation and explanation: The description of this defect that afflicts hadith. And when he finished explaining the four divisions... He said: al-marwi anhu when he denies the narration... Or he acts contrary to it after narration... And the narrator's specification of some of its possibilities does not prevent action... And the companion's action contrary to it necessitates criticism when the hadith is clear and does not admit concealment... Example: Ubadah ibn as-Samit narrated: The Prophet said: 'The unmarried fornicator is flogged one hundred lashes and exiled for a year.' Ash-Shafi'i holds to this and makes exile a prescribed punishment. But we say: Umar exiled a man who apostatized and joined the Romans, then swore never to exile anyone. If exile were a fixed punishment, he would not have abandoned it. So we know exile is a policy, not a punishment. And the hadith on punishments was clear, not admitting concealment from the caliphs appointed to carry out punishments...
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the criticism (ta'n) that afflicts hadith. It explains various scenarios where a hadith may lose its binding authority due to the action or stance of the narrator (rawi) or the one narrated from (marwi 'anhu). The first scenario: if the one narrated from denies the narration outright, the hadith is rejected by consensus. If he expresses uncertainty (e.g., 'I do not remember'), there is a difference: according to Imam al-Kirmani and Ahmad ibn Fudayl, the narration is rejected; according to al-Shafi'i and Malik, it is not. The second scenario: if the narrator acts contrary to his own hadith after narrating it with certainty, this voids the hadith's authority because it indicates that the hadith is abrogated or fabricated. If he acts carelessly, his own reliability ('adala) is affected. An example is the hadith of Aisha that a marriage without a guardian is invalid, yet she acted contrary to it. The third scenario: if the narrator acts contrary before narrating, it does not harm the hadith because he may have changed his position after learning it. If the date of narration is unknown, doubt remains, but doubt does not void the hadith. The fourth scenario: if the narrator interprets a general or ambiguous hadith in a specific way, this does not prevent acting on other possible interpretations. Example: Ibn Umar narrated 'The two parties have a choice as long as they have not separated' and took 'separation' as physical parting, but that does not forbid acting on verbal parting. The fifth scenario: the companion's action against a clear (zahir) hadith that has no room for interpretation leads to criticism. But if the hadith is open to interpretation, it does not. Example: the hadith of flogging and exile for unmarried fornicators; the caliph Umar once exiled an apostate and then vowed never to exile again, proving exile is not a fixed punishment but a policy. Thus, the companion's action does not necessarily reject the hadith if the hadith is clear. The passage also mentions that unspecified criticism from an opponent (like 'this hadith is weak' without detail) does not harm the narrator according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
طعن (ta'n): A defect or criticism that invalidates a hadith or its use as evidence
راوی (rawi): The narrator of a hadith; his action contrary to his narration may void the hadith
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a hadith that is no longer applicable because a later revelation or stronger proof overrides it
ظاہر (zahir): A text whose meaning is clear and not open to multiple interpretations

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Sahabi narrates a hadith but then acts contrary to it with certainty, what is the Hanafi ruling regarding that hadith as evidence?
A) The hadith remains valid evidence because the Sahabi's action does not affect its authenticity.
B) The hadith is rejected as evidence because the contradiction proves it is abrogated or fabricated.
C) The hadith is considered weak due to the Sahabi's unreliability.
D) The hadith is only rejected if the Sahabi explicitly denies narrating it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school voids a hadith as evidence if the narrator or companion acts contrary to it with certainty, indicating abrogation or fabrication, but allows flexibility when the text is open to interpretation.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Sahabi's Contrary Practice and Its Impact on Hadith Criticism
States the rule that a Sahabi's practice contrary to a clear hadith indicates criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a Sahabi's practice contrary to a clear (zahir) hadith indicates criticism (ta'n) and distinguish it from cases where the hadith is hidden (khafi).

Core Idea
A Sahabi's divergent practice only impugns a hadith if the hadith was undeniably clear and widely known.

This lesson examines a critical principle in Hanafi usul: the effect of a Companion's action that contradicts a narrated hadith. The Hanafi school argues that such contradiction can undermine the hadith, but only if the hadith was so clear (zahir) that no Companion could have been unaware of it. Through the case of exile for fornication, we see how this principle resolves apparent conflicts between textual evidence and historical practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
State the condition under which a Sahabi's contrary practice causes criticism of a hadith according to the passage: it must be a clear (zahir) hadith that does not admit hiddenness (khafa).
2
Analyze the Example (Exile)
Examine the hadith of 'Ubada ibn al-Samit prescribing exile for fornicators. Note the Shafi'i position that exile is a fixed hadd. Then consider Caliph 'Umar's action: he exiled a man who apostatized, then swore never to exile again. Understand the Hanafi reasoning: if exile were a hadd, 'Umar could not abandon it; hence it is a discretionary measure (siyasa).
This example shows the rule in action: the hadith is clear, and 'Umar's contrary practice indicates that the apparent meaning is not binding.
3
Distinguish the Counterexample (Laughter in Prayer)
Study the hadith obligating wudu from audible laughter, narrated by Ibn Khalid al-Juhani and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Abu Musa did not act on it, but the passage says this does not cause criticism because the hadith was hidden (khafi) and not widely known among the Sahaba.
This contrasts with the exile example: here the hadith is not clear and well-known, so the Sahabi's non-action does not impugn it.
4
Apply the Rule
Determine in practice whether a given hadith is zahir or khafi. Consider the number of narrators, the context, and whether the ruling was commonly practiced.
This step prepares you to use the principle in evaluating hadiths criticized by Sahabi actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَمَلُ الصَّحَابِي بِخِلَافِ الْحَدِيثِ يُوجِبُ الطَّعْنَ إِذَا كَانَ الْحَدِيثُ ظَاهِرًا لَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْخَفَاءَ عَلَيْهِمْ. وَمِثَالُهُ مَا رَوَى عُبَادَةُ بْنُ الصَّامِتِ أَنَّهُ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: الْبِكْرُ بِالْبِكْرِ جَلْدُ مِائَةٍ وَتَغْرِيبُ عَامٍ. فَيَتَمَسَّكُ بِهِ الشَّافِعِيُّ وَيَجْعَلُ النَّفْيَ إِلَى عَامٍ جَزَاءً مِنَ الْحَدِّ. وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ: إِنَّ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ نَفَى رَجُلًا فَارْتَدَّ وَلَحِقَ بِالرُّومِ، فَحَلَفَ أَنْ لَا يَنْفِيَ أَحَدًا أَبَدًا. فَلَوْ كَانَ النَّفْيُ حَدًّا لَمَا خَلَفَ تَرْكَهُ. فَعُلِمَ أَنَّ النَّفْيَ سُنَّةٌ كَانَتْ سِيَاسَةً لَا حَدًّا. وَاحْتَرَزَ بِهِ عَمَّا كَانَ يَحْتَمِلُ الْخَفَاءَ عَلَيْهِمْ، كَحَدِيثِ وُجُوبِ الْوُضُوءِ بِالْقَهْقَهَةِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ رَوَاهُ بْنُ خَالِدٍ الْجُهَنِيُّ وَأَبُو مُوسَى الْأَشْعَرِيُّ فَلَمْ يَعْمَلْ بِهِ أَبُو مُوسَى وَلَمْ يُوجِبْ ذَلِكَ جَرْحًا فِيهِ.
And the practice of a Sahabi contrary to the hadith necessitates criticism when the hadith is clear (zahir) not admitting hiddenness (khafa) upon them. Its example is what 'Ubada ibn al-Samit narrated: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The unmarried with the unmarried: a flogging of one hundred and exile for a year.' Al-Shafi'i holds onto this and makes exile a year a part of the hadd (fixed punishment). And we say: 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) exiled a man and he apostatized and joined the Byzantines, so he swore that he would never exile anyone again. If exile were a hadd, he would not have left it. So it is known that exile was a sunna (practice) that was political (siyasa), not a hadd. And he [the author] guarded by this [condition] against what admits hiddenness upon them, like the hadith of the obligation of wudu from audible laughter in prayer narrated by Ibn Khalid al-Juhani and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari; Abu Musa did not act on it and that did not cause criticism in it.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage lays down a key usul principle: if a Sahabi (Companion) acts contrary to a hadith he himself narrated, that indicates a defect (ṭaʿn) in the hadith, but only if the hadith is clear (ẓāhir) and not hidden (khafī) from the Companion. The author provides two examples. First, the hadith of 'Ubada ibn al-Samit that prescribes flogging and exile for unmarried fornicators. Imam al-Shafi'i uses this hadith to argue that exile is a fixed punishment (ḥadd). The Hanafi school, however, points to the practice of Caliph 'Umar: he exiled a man who then apostatized and fled to enemy territory. Consequently, 'Umar swore never to exile anyone again. If exile were a ḥadd, 'Umar would not have abandoned it, because a ḥadd cannot be abandoned by a ruler's discretion. Hence, exile is a discretionary political measure (siyāsa), not a ḥadd. The second example: the hadith obligating wudu due to audible laughter in prayer, narrated by Ibn Khalid al-Juhani. Abu Musa al-Ash'ari did not act on this hadith, but his non-action does not constitute criticism (jarḥ) because the hadith was hidden (khafī) from him—it was not widely known. Thus, the condition that the hadith must be clear and well-known (ẓāhir) is essential for a Sahabi's contrary practice to cause criticism.

Key Terms
الطعن (al-ṭaʿn): Criticism or defect that undermines the authority of a hadith
الحد (al-ḥadd): Fixed divine punishment that cannot be altered or abandoned
الخفاء (al-khafāʾ): Hiddenness or lack of widespread knowledge of a hadith among Companions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school argue that exile for unmarried fornicators is not a hadd punishment?
A) The hadith of 'Ubada is weak
B) Caliph 'Umar exiled a man and then abandoned the practice, which would be impossible if exile were a fixed hadd
C) The Quran does not mention exile
D) The Shafi'i school agrees with the Hanafi position

Key Takeaway
A Sahabi's contrary practice only implicates a hadith if the hadith was clear and not hidden; this principle underlies the Hanafi distinction between fixed hadd and discretionary siyasa.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Companion's Practice as Critique of Hadith
Explains how a companion's contrary act questions a hadith when the hadith is clear

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a Companion's practice contrary to a hadith can critique the hadith when the hadith is clear (zahir), and distinguish this from cases where the hadith is ambiguous.

Core Idea
A Companion's contrary practice critiques a clear hadith; ambiguous hadith are not harmed by non-action.

In this lesson, we examine how the practice of a Companion (sahabi) that contradicts a reported hadith can serve as a critique of that hadith—but only under the condition that the hadith is clear (zahir). The author illustrates this with two examples: the dispute over exile for fornicators, and the laughter hadith where Abu Musa's caution did not invalidate the narration. This analysis deepens your understanding of how Hanafi usul assesses the strength of ahadith through the lens of Companion practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
What is the author's claim about a Companion's practice contradicting a hadith? Note the condition that the hadith must be clear (zahir).
The author states that such contradiction is a cause for criticism and reinterpretation.
2
Examine the condition
Why must the hadith be clear (zahir) for the Companion's non-action to be a critique? Consider the possibility of hiddenness or ambiguity.
If the hadith is not clear, the Companion's non-action may be due to caution or personal interpretation, not rejection of the text.
3
Analyze the first example
How does the Ubadah hadith and Umar's action illustrate the principle? What does Umar's oath tell us about the nature of exile?
Umar's abandonment of exile after a negative consequence shows he considered it discretionary, not a fixed hadd.
4
Analyze the second example
How does the laughter hadith show the opposite (no critique due to ambiguity)? Why is Abu Musa's non-action excused?
The hadith is not clearly applicable in that context, so his caution is rare and does not impugn the hadith.
5
Derive the usul implication
What does this teach about the Hanafi method of evaluating hadith? When is Companion practice used as a tool for interpretation?
Companion practice, especially of a caliph, can serve as evidence for interpretation or specification (takhsis) of a general ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعمل الصحابی بخلافه الخ اور صحابی کا عمل حدیث کے خلاف ہونا۔ حدیث سے مطعون ترجمہ تشریح ہونے کا باعث اور موجب ہے جب کہ حدیث ظاہر ہو صحابہ پر خار مخفی ہونے کا احتمال نہ رکھتی ہو یہاں سے اس طعن کو شروع فرمایا ہے جو حدیث کو غیر راوی کی جانب سے لاحق ہوتا ہے۔ اس کی مثال وہ حدیث ہے جس کو حضرت عبادہ بن صامت نے روایت کیا ہے کہ نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا البکر بالبكر جلد مائة وتغريب عام کہ کنوار لڑکا [؟] کا اگر کنواری لڑکی کے ساتھ زنا کرے تو ایک سو کوڑے اور ایک سال کی جلاوطنی کی سزا امام شافعی اس سے استدلال کرتے ہیں۔ اور ایک سال کی جلاوطنی کو حد میں شمار کرتے ہیں ۔ وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ إِنْ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله عنه كه حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ نے ایک شخص کو جلاوطن کر دیا تھا تو وہ مرتد ہو گیا۔ اور ملک روم میں داخل ہو گیا۔ تو حضرت مرنے قسم کھائی تھی کہ آئندہ کبھی کسی کو جلا وطن نہ کروں گا۔ پس اگر جلا وطن کرنا حد میں داخل ہوتا تو حضرت سیدنا عمر فاروق رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ اس کے ترک کرنے کا حلف نہ اٹھاتے۔ لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ جلاوطنی کی سزا حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ کی طرف سے سیاست و انتظامی مصالح کے پیش نظر تھی وَاحْتَرَدَ إِذَا كَانَ الحَدِيث ظَاهِراً کی قید سے مصنف رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے اس چیز سے احتراز کیا ہے جو صحابہ سے خفا کا احتمال رکھتی ہو، کیونکہ صحابہ پر کھلی ہونے کا احتمال حدیث میں جرح کا موجب نہیں ہے۔ جیسے قہقہہ والی حدیث جس کی روایت حضرت خالد جہنی نے کی ہے۔ مگر حضرت ابو موسی اشعری نے اس حدیث پر عمل نہیں کیا مگر ان کا اس حدیث پر عمل نہ فرمانا حدیث کو مجروح نہیں کرتا کیونکہ اس کا و تورع [؟] نادر ہے اور بہت ہی کم ایسا ہوا ہے کہ حدیث حضرت ابو موسیٰ پر خفا کا احتمال رکھتی ہو۔
And the practice of the Companion contrary to it... and the Companion's practice being against the hadith is a cause and reason for the hadith being [considered] criticized and interpreted when the hadith is apparent and the Companions do not have any hidden doubt about it. From here [the author] begins that criticism which affects the hadith from the side of other than the narrator. Its example is the hadith that Hadrat Ubadah ibn al-Samit narrated that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'The virgin with the virgin: one hundred lashes and exile for a year.' Imam al-Shafi'i uses this as evidence and considers one year's exile as part of the hadd punishment. And we say that Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) exiled a man, and he apostatized and entered the Byzantine territory, so Umar swore an oath that he would never exile anyone again. So if exile were part of the hadd, Umar would not have taken an oath to abandon it. Thus it is known that the punishment of exile was from Umar's side due to policy and administrative interests. And he [the author] restricts [the criticism] with the condition that the hadith is clear (zahir)—through this restriction the author avoids that which could have the possibility of hiddenness from the Companions, because the possibility that a matter is open to the Companions does not cause criticism of the hadith. Like the hadith about laughter narrated by Hadrat Khalid al-Juhani; Hadrat Abu Musa al-Ashari did not act upon it, but his not acting does not render the hadith defective because his cautiousness is rare and it is very seldom that a hadith has the possibility of being hidden from Abu Musa.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage addresses two related topics: first, the example of a Companion's practice contradicting a hadith (the Ubadah hadith on lashing and exile for unmarried fornicators) and how the Hanafis use Umar's abandonment of exile to argue that exile is not a fixed hadd but a discretionary punishment. Second, it explains the condition that for a Companion's hidden doubt to affect a hadith, the hadith must be clear (zahir); otherwise, mere possibility of hiddenness does not invalidate the hadith, as illustrated by the laughter hadith where Abu Musa's non-action is attributed to rare caution.

Key Terms
تغريب (taghrib): Exile; banishment from one's hometown as a punishment
جرح (jarh): Criticism that impugns the reliability of a narrator or a hadith

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school argue that exile (taghrib) is not a required part of the hadd punishment for unmarried fornicators?
A) Because the hadith of Ubadah is weak
B) Because Umar's practice of exiling a man and then swearing to abandon it shows it was discretionary
C) Because the Quran does not mention exile
D) Because the companion Abu Musa did not act on a similar hadith

Key Takeaway
A Companion's contrary practice critiques a hadith only when the hadith is clear; otherwise, it may be excused as caution or policy.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Valid and Invalid Grounds for Criticizing a Narrator (Jarh)
Listing criteria for accepting criticism and forms rejected

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which criticisms of a narrator are accepted in Hanafi usul and which are rejected, and apply the condition that the critic must be sincere and unbiased.

Core Idea
Not every criticism counts; jarh is only valid when explicit, consensus-based, and from a sincere, unbiased critic.

The Hanafi school sets strict conditions for accepting criticism (jarh) of a narrator. General remarks like 'majruh' are insufficient; the defect must be specific and consensus-based. Moreover, the critic must be known for sincere advice (nasihat), not bias or extremism. This lesson explores the general rule and then the seven specific forms of criticism that are not considered valid jarh, including tadlis, talbis, irsal, and others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Start by locating the opening statement: criticism must be specific and from a sincere critic. General attacks by muhaddithun without explanation are insufficient.
The passage says 'الطعن المتهم' and 'إلا إذا وَقَعَ مُفسراً' – the criticism must be explained.
2
Recognize the condition of the critic
The critic must be known for sincere advice, not bias or extremism. The author warns against biased people who exaggerate rulings.
Look for 'مِمَنْ اسْتَهَرَ بِالنُصَيْحَةِ دُونَ التعصب'.
3
Enumerate the invalid grounds
The passage lists seven specific grounds that are not accepted as jarh: tadlis, talbis, irsal, riding a beast, joking, young age, and abundance of fiqh knowledge.
The list begins with 'حتى لا يُقبل الطعن بالتدلیس'.
4
Understand the reason for each invalid ground
For example, tadlis only implies irsal, which itself is not a defect; the Prophet joked, so joking cannot disqualify; many Companions narrated at a young age with precision.
Each invalid ground is accompanied by a rationale; e.g., 'الإرسال تبعا لفكر الإسلام وهو ليس بطعن'.
5
Apply the rule to a hypothetical critique
Given a statement like 'This narrator is weak because he knows many fiqh rulings', evaluate whether it is valid jarh per Hanafi usul. It is not; abundance of fiqh is a sign of strength.
Use the list to test any criticism against the seven invalid categories.

الخ-- کیونکہ زیادہ سے زیادہ اس طریقہ پر مرسل ہونے کا شبہ کیا جائے گا۔ مگر جب کہ میری مرسل [؟] کوئی جرح میں شمار نہیں کی جاتی تو مرسل ہونے کا شک بدرجہ اولیٰ شہر سے بالا تر ہو گا۔ وَالتَّلْبِيْسُ وَهُوَ أَن يَذْكُرَ الرَّاوِي شَيْخَهُ بِالْكُنْيَةِ لَا بِالاسْمِ أَوْ يَذْكُرُهُ بِصِفَةٍ غَيْرِ مشهُورَةٍ حَتَّى لَا يُعْرَفَ فِيمَا بَيْنَ النَّاسِ وَلَا يَطْعَنُوا عَلَيْهِ كَمَا يَقُولُ سُفْيَانُ الثَّوْرِي حَدَّثَنِي أَبُو سَعِيدٍ وَهُوَ كُنْيَةٌ لِلْحَسَنِ الْبَصْرِي وَالْكَلْبِي جَمِيعًا وَوَقَعَ فِي بَعْضِ الْفُسْح [؟] فهُنَا قَوْلُهُ وَالإِرْسالُ تَبَعًا لِفِكْرِ الْإِسْلَام [؟] وَهُوَ يَصْلُحُ جَرْحًا وَالْمِزَاحُ وَهُوَ لَا يَصْلُحُ جَرْحًا لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ كَانَ يُمَازِحُ كَثِيرًا وَلَكِنْ لَا يَقُولُ إِلَّا الْحَقَّ كَمَا قَالَ لِعَجُوزٍ إِنَّ الْعَجَائِزَ لَا تَدْخُلُ الْجَنَّةَ فَلَمَّا وَلَّتْ تَبْكِي قَالَ أَخْبِرُوهَا بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى إِنَّا أَنْشَأْنَاهُنَّ إِنْشَاءً فَجَعَلْنَاهُنَّ أَبْكَارًا عُرُبًا وَحَدَاثَةُ السِّنِّ أَي صِغَرُهُ كَمَا فِي الضَّبْطِ وَالْإِتْقَانِ وَاسْتِكْثَارُ مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ كَمَا طَعَنَ بِذَلِكَ بَعْضُ الْمُحَدِّثِينَ عَلَى أَصْحَابِنَا فَإِنَّ ذَلِكَ دَلِيلُ قُوَّةٍ جَوْدَتِهِ [؟] وَقَدْ كَانَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ يَحْفَظُ عِشْرِينَ أَلْفَ حَدِيثٍ مِنَ الْمَوْضُوع
And the criticism that is suspected (al-mat'un al-muttaham) etc. — In our view, the criticism of the muhaddithun does not render the narrator defective; for example, if one says 'the hadith is majruh or munkar' or similar, the narration is still acted upon. Unless the criticism is explained specifically such that it is unanimously considered a grounds for jarh — everyone agrees, with no disagreement. If there is a case where some consider it jarh and others not, even then the jarh comes only from one who is known for sincere advice, not bias, because biased people have greatly harmed the religion: they declare makruh as haram and mandub as fard. Alas, today some of our illiterate or semi-literate followers develop such traits, abandoning obligatory acts and emphasizing supererogatory ones, leaving makruh and adopting harder acts. The commentators say: the jarh of such people is not considered. Hence, criticism through tadlis is not accepted. The following types of criticism are not accepted: (1) Tadlis: linguistically, concealing the defect of a commodity from the buyer; in hadith terminology, concealing the detail in the isnad by saying 'haddathana fulan 'an fulan' instead of 'haddathana fulan qala akhbarana fulan' — because at most it gives the impression of irsal, and since irsal itself is not a ground for jarh, the doubt of irsal is even less harmful. (2) Talbis: when the narrator mentions his shaykh by kunya rather than name, or by an obscure attribute, so that he is not recognized and people do not criticize him, like Sufyan al-Thawri saying 'haddathani Abu Sa'id' which is the kunya of both al-Hasan al-Basri and al-Kalbi. (3) Irsal: following the thought of Islam [?] and it is also not a criticism as we stated. (4) Riding a beast (rakd al-dabbah) as some peers criticized Muhammad ibn al-Hasan for it, but it is a permissible action for those engaged in jihad and not valid jarh. (5) Joking (mizah): it is not valid jarh because the Prophet ﷺ often joked but only spoke the truth, as he said to an old woman, 'Old women do not enter Paradise,' and when she left crying, he said, 'Tell her the word of Allah: Indeed We have created them a new creation and made them virgins, loving, and of equal age.' (6) Young age (hadathat al-sinn): as Sufyan al-Thawri said to Abu Hanifa, 'What does this young one say?' That is so because many Companions narrated in their youth, provided they had precision at the time of learning and integrity at the time of transmission, and they were not habitual narrators; Abu Bakr was not accustomed to narrating, yet no one surpassed him in accuracy. (7) Abundance of fiqh issues (istikthar masa'il al-fiqh): as some muhaddithun criticized our companions for it, but that is a sign of strength and excellence; Abu Yusuf used to memorize twenty thousand fabricated hadiths.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage outlines the Hanafi criteria for accepting criticism (jarh) of a narrator. First, general criticism by muhaddithun without specific details is not sufficient to reject a narration; the criticism must be explicit and based on a universally recognized ground. Second, the critic must be known for sincere religious advice, not bias or extremism, as biased people may overstate rulings. Then the author lists six specific forms of criticism that are invalid: tadlis (concealing details in the isnad), talbis (hiding a shaykh's identity), irsal (sending without a link), riding a beast (a frivolous criticism), joking (since the Prophet himself joked), young age (many Companions narrated when young), and abundance of fiqh knowledge (a sign of strength, not weakness). The passage also gives examples for each, such as Sufyan al-Thawri's use of the kunya Abu Sa'id for both al-Hasan al-Basri and al-Kalbi, and the anecdote about the old woman and joking. The overall message is that jarh is only accepted under strict conditions to protect hadith narration from frivolous attacks.

Key Terms
جرح (jarh): Valid criticism that impairs a narrator's reliability; must be explicit and from a sincere critic
تدلیس (tadlis): Hiding details in the isnad, e.g., using 'an 'an without specifying direct hearing
تلبيس (talbis): Mentioning a shaykh by an obscure attribute to conceal identity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, why is tadlis (concealing details in the isnad) not considered a valid ground for rejecting a hadith?
A) Because the Prophet himself used tadlis
B) Because the worst possible implication is that the hadith is mursal, and mursal is not a defect
C) Because all narrators practice tadlis
D) Because tadlis only occurs in fabricated hadiths

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, jarh is only valid when the criticism is explicit, based on a consensus defect, and issued by a sincere critic free from bias.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
12 min
Hanafi Hierarchy for Resolving Ta'arud Between Evidences
Explaining the hierarchy of recourse when evidences conflict

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy for resolving ta'arud between evidences, distinguishing true contradiction from apparent disagreement, and identify the correct recourse when two verses or two sunnahs conflict.

Core Idea
When two evidences contradict, they cancel; the ruling is sought from the next level in the hierarchy: Quran → Sunnah → Companions' sayings or Qiyas → Original principle.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar lays out the procedural rules for dealing with apparent contradictions (ta'arud) between Islamic legal proofs. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for any student of Hanafi usul, as it governs how a jurist navigates conflicting sources to derive the correct ruling. We will walk through the conditions for true ta'arud, the stepwise recourse from Quran to Sunnah to Companions' sayings or qiyas, and finally the fallback to the original principle when no evidence is determinative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the evidences and verify conditions for ta'arud
First, determine if there is a genuine contradiction: the two evidences must address the same act, at the same time and place, and give opposing rulings (e.g., halal vs. haram). If the locus, time, or relation differ, it is not ta'arud.
Examples: marriage (halal for wife, haram for mother-in-law) has different loci; wine (halal in early Islam, later haram) has different times.
2
Classify the level of the conflicting evidences
Identify whether both are from the Quran, both from the Sunnah, or one from each. The hierarchy dictates the next step: if both are verses, move to the Sunnah; if both are sunnahs, move to Companions' sayings (aqwal al-sahaba) or qiyas.
If one is Quran and one is Sunnah, the Quran generally prevails, but the passage does not discuss that case.
3
Apply the hierarchy for Quran vs. Quran → Sunnah
When two verses conflict, they cancel each other (tasāqatā). Do not resort to a third verse, as that would be tarjih by multiplicity, which is not permissible. Instead, turn to the Sunnah (hadith).
Example: surah al-Muzzammil (73:20) vs. surah al-A'raf (7:204) on recitation during prayer — both apply to prayer, so they cancel, and the hadith 'The imam's recitation suffices' is used.
4
Apply the hierarchy for Sunnah vs. Sunnah → Companions' sayings or Qiyas
If two sunnahs conflict, recourse is to either the sayings of the Companions or qiyas. Fakhr al-Islam uses 'aw' (or), indicating no fixed order. Three views exist: (1) Companions' sayings always precede, (2) qiyas always precedes, (3) Companions' sayings precede in matters not accessible to qiyas, and qiyas precedes in matters accessible.
Example: eclipse prayer — different hadiths on number of rak'ahs lead to qiyas on other prayers.
5
If all else fails, revert to the original principle (asl)
When no evidence from Quran, Sunnah, Companions, or qiyas can resolve the conflict, the original ruling (before revelation) is maintained. This is the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity).
Example: donkey's saliva — conflicting reports on its meat led to uncertainty, so the original rule (permissibility or purity, depending) was applied.

Source Text
