بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ معارضہ کے صادق آنے کے لئے اتحاد نسبت کی قید ضروری ہے کیوں کہ بیوی میں حلت یہ نسبت اس کے شوہر کے ہے اور حرمت شوہر کے علاوہ کی طرف نسبت سے ہے اس کو بھی تعارض نہیں کہا جاتا ۔ وَحُكْمُها بَيْنَ الأتَيْنِ الْمَصِيرُ إلى السُّنَّةِ لأَنَّ الآيَتَيْنِ إِذَا تَعَارَضًا تَسَاقَطَنَا فَلَا بُدُ لِلْعَمَلِ مِنَ الْمَصِيرِ إِلى مَا بَعْدَهُ وَهُوَ السُّنَّةُ وَلا يُمْكِنُ الْمَصِيرُ الى الآيَةِ الثَّالِثَةِ لأَنَّهُ يُقْضَى إِلَى التَّرْجِيحِ بَكَثْرَةِ الأَدلَّةِ وَذَالِكَ لَآيَجُوزُ وَمِثَالُهُ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَىٰ فَاقْرُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ القُرْآنِ مَعَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقَرْآنُ فَاسْتَمِعُوْا لَهُ وَاَنْصِتُوا فَإِنَّ الاَوَّلَ يَعُمُومِهِ يُوجِبُ الْقِرَاءَةَ عَلَى الْمُقْتَدِي وَالثَّانِي بِخُصُوصِهِ يُنْفِيْهِ وَقَدْ ورَدَا فِي الصَّلُوةِ فَتَسَاقَطًا فَيُصَارُ إِلَى حَدِيثٍ بَعْدَهُ وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلاَمُ مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ اِمَامُ فَقِرَاءَةُ الاِمَامِ قَرَاءَةً لَهُ وَبَيْنَ السَّنَتَيْنِ الْمَصِيْرِ إِلَى أَقْوَالِ الصَّحَابَةِ أَوْ الْقَيَاسِ هَكَذَا ذَكَرَ فَحْرُ الإسلام بِكَلِمَةِ أَوْ فَلَا يَفْهَمُ التَّرْقِيب بَيْنَهُما وَقِيلَ أَقْوَالُ الصَّحَابَةِ مَقَدَّمَةٌ عَلَى الْقَيَاسِ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ فِيْهَا يُدْرَكَ بِالْقَيَاسِ أوْلاً وَقِيْلَ الْقِيَاسِ مُقَدَّمٌ مُطْلَقًا وَقِيلَ فِي التَّطبِيقِ أَنْ أَقْوَالَ الصَّحَابَةِ مُقَدَّمَةٌ فِيْمَا لأَيُدْرَكَ بِالْقِيَاسَ وَالْقَيَاسُ مُقَدَّمَ فِيْمَا يُدْرَكَ بِهِ وَمِثَالُهُ مَا روى إن النَّبيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ صَلَّى صَلوةَ الْكَسَوْفِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ بِرُكُوعِ وسجدَتَيْنِ وَرَوَتْ عَائِسَةَ أَنَّهُ صَلاهَا بَارْبَعِ رُكُوعَاتٍ وَاربَعِ سَجْدَاتِ فَيَتَعَارَضَانِ فَيُصَارُ إِلَى الْقَيَاسِ بَعْدَهُ وَهُوَ الاِعْتِبَارُ بِسائر الصلوة وَعِنْدَ الْعِجْزِ يَجِبُ تَقْرِيْرَ الأَصْوَلِ أَى إِذَا عَجِرٌ عَنِ الْمَصِيرِ باضن تَعَارَضَتِ المُتَنَانِ وَأَقَوّالُ الصَّحَابَةِ وَالْقَيَاسُ أَيْضًا وَلَمْ يُوجَدْ دَلِيْل بَعْدَهُ فِحِينَئِذٍ يَجِبُ تَقْرِيرُ كُلِّ شيْءٍ عَلى أَصْلِهِ وَإِبْقَاءَ مَا كَانَ عَلَى مَا كَانَ كَمَا فِي سَوْرِ الْحِمَارِ لَمَّا تَعَارَضَتِ الدلائل وَجَبَ تَقْرِيرُ الأَصْوَلِ فَانْهُ رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ نَهى عَنْ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الأَهْلِيَةِ فِي يَوْم خَيْبَرَ وَأَمَرَ بِالْقَاءِ الدَيْرِ طُبِعَ فِيْهَا لُحُومُهَا وَرَوَى غَالِبُ مَنْ فِيْرَ أَنَّهُ قَالَ لرّسول الله صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَمْ يَبْقَ مِنْ مَالِي الأمُمَيْرَاتِ فَقَالَ كُلُّ مِنْ سمِيْنَ مَالِكَ فَابَاحَ لَحُوْمَهَا فَلَمَّا وَقَعَ التَّعَارُضُ فِي لُحُومِهَا لَزِمَ الإِسْتِبَاهُ فِي سوْرِهَا لأَنَّهُ مُتَوَلدٌ مِنْهَا. وحُكْمُها بَيْنَ الآيَتَيْنِ الْمَصِيرُ إلى السنة اور معارضے کا حکم یہ ہے کہ جب دو آئوں ترجمہ و تشریح میں ہو تو سنت کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔ کیوں کہ دو آیتیں جب متعارض ہوں گی تو ساقط ہو جائیں گی۔ اس لئے عمل کرنے کے لئے ان کے مابعد کی طرف جاتا ہوگا اور وہ سنت ہے اور تیسری آیت کی طرف جانا ممکن نہیں ہے کیوں کہ یہ کثرت دلائل کی بنیاد پر ترجیح کی طرف لے جاتا ہے اور وہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کی مثال میں آیت فَاقْرُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ کو آیت وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْآنِ فَاسْتَمِعُوا کے ساتھ پیش کیا جاتا ہے کیوں کہ اول آیت اپنے عموم کی وجہ سے مقتدی پر قرآت کو واجب کرتی ہے۔ اور دوسری آیت اپنی خصوص کے سبب مذکورہ حکم کی نفی کرتی ہے۔ حالانکہ دونوں آیتیں نماز کے باب میں وارد ہوئی ہیں۔ لہذا دونوں ساقط العمل ہو جائیں گی پھر اس کے بعد حدیث کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا اور وہ حدیث یہ ہے۔ مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِمَامٌ فقراءة الإمام قراءة له. وَبَيْنَ السَّنْتَيْنِ الْمَصِيرُ إلى أقوال الصحابہ اور جب دوستوں کے درمیان تعارض ہو تو اقوال صحابہ یا قیاس کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا ایام فخر الاسلام نے اس طرح کلمہ او" کے ساتھ ذکر کیا ہے لہذا دونوں اقوال صحابہ اور قیاس میں ترتیب کا لحاظ نہ کیا جائے گا اور بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ اقوال صحابہ قیاس پر مقدم ہیں برا یہ ہے کہ قیاس مدرک با القیاس ہو یا مدرک با لقیاس نہ ہو۔ اور بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ ان دونوں اقوال میں تعمیق دی جائے گی۔ کہ اقوال صحابہ فِيْمَا لا يُدْرَكَ بِالْقَيَاسِ میں مقدم ہیں اور مدرک بالقیاس میں قیاس ہم رکھا جائے گا۔ اور اس کی مثال وہ حدیث ہے جسے روایت کیا گیا ہے کہ نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے صلوۃ کسوف نے
No preference of any kind exists in essence or attributes. Thus no contradiction occurs between the mufassir (exegete) and the ruling, nor between 'ibarat al-nass' and 'isharat al-nass', because each is superior to the other in terms of description. Therefore among hadith, no contradiction occurs between mashhur and ahad, nor between the specific and the general-mukhasas al-ba'd of the Book of Allah, because they are superior to each other in terms of essence. They occur in two conflicting rulings, meaning they are found in two contradictory rulings, such that one indicates permissibility and the other prohibition; otherwise there is no contradiction. The author mentioned this under the rubric of 'weakness' and 'rukun', otherwise it is among the conditions of contradiction, as the author says: 'Its condition is unity of place and time along with conflicting rulings.' Its condition is that there is unity of time and place along with difference in the ruling. Thus marriage establishes permissibility for the wife and prohibition for her mother (i.e., mother-in-law), but this is not called contradiction because the locus of permissibility and prohibition is not one. Similarly, wine was permissible in early Islam and later prohibited; this is also not called contradiction because the time of permissibility and prohibition is not unified. Likewise, if there is no conflict in the ruling, it is not called mu'arada, and this is clear. Some have said that for mu'arada to be true, unity of relation is necessary because permissibility for the wife is relative to her husband, and prohibition relative to someone else; this is also not called contradiction. The ruling between two [conflicting] verses is recourse to the Sunnah, because when two verses conflict, they cancel each other; so for action, one must turn to what comes after them, which is the Sunnah. Resorting to a third verse is not possible because it would lead to preference by multiplicity of proofs, which is not permissible. Its example is His statement: 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an' along with His statement: 'When the Qur'an is recited, listen to it and be silent.' The first by its generality obligates recitation upon the follower, and the second by its particularity negates it. Both occur in prayer, so they cancel each other, then recourse is to a hadith after them, which is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever has an imam, the imam's recitation is his recitation.' And between two sunnahs [that conflict], recourse is to the sayings of the Companions or qiyas. Thus Fakhr al-Islam mentioned with the word 'aw' (or), so no order is understood between them. It is said: the sayings of the Companions are preferred over qiyas, whether or not it is attainable by qiyas. It is also said: qiyas is preferred absolutely. It is also said in application: the sayings of the Companions are preferred in matters not attainable by qiyas, and qiyas is preferred in matters attainable by it. Its example is the report that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed the eclipse prayer as two rak'ahs, each rak'ah with one bowing and two prostrations; and 'A'isha reported that he performed it with four bowings and four prostrations. They conflict, so recourse is to qiyas after it, which is analogy to other prayers. And when unable, one must establish the original principle, i.e., when one is unable to resort to what has been mentioned, having conflicting texts, sayings of the Companions, and qiyas, and no proof after that is found, then one must keep everything upon its original principle and leave it as it was, as in the case of the saliva of a donkey: when proofs conflicted regarding its meat, it became necessary to establish the original principle regarding its saliva because it is derived from it. The ruling between two verses is recourse to the Sunnah... [Urdu re-explanation follows]
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar discusses the rules for dealing with ta'arud (apparent contradiction) between Islamic legal evidences. It first clarifies that true contradiction only exists when two evidences give conflicting rulings for the same act at the same time and place; otherwise it is not considered ta'arud. Examples given: marriage vs. mother-in-law (different loci), wine in early vs. later Islam (different times), and the wife-husband relationship (different relations). The main focus is on the hierarchy of resolution when conflict occurs between two evidences of the same category. When two Quranic verses conflict, they are both set aside and recourse is taken to the Sunnah (hadith). The example given is the apparent conflict between the verse commanding recitation in prayer ('faqra'u ma tayassara') and the verse commanding silent listening ('wa idha quri'a al-Qur'anu fastami'u'). Since both apply to the prayer context, they cancel out, and we move to the hadith that the imam's recitation suffices for the follower. When two sunnahs (hadiths) conflict, recourse is to the sayings of the Companions (aqwal al-sahaba) or to qiyas (analogy). The author notes two opinions: one that Companions' sayings are always preferred, another that qiyas is always preferred, and a third that Companions' sayings are preferred in matters beyond qiyas, while qiyas is preferred in matters accessible to qiyas. The eclipse prayer example illustrates conflict between hadiths on the number of bowings, leading to qiyas on other prayers. Finally, if all else fails, one must revert to the original principle (asl) — meaning keep things as they were before evidence, e.g., the ruling on donkey saliva following conflicting reports on its meat. The passage ends with a lengthy Urdu re-explanation.

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'arud): Apparent contradiction between two evidences leading to conflicting rulings, requiring resolution through hierarchy of recourse.
متعارضان (muta'aridayn): Two evidences that appear to contradict each other in ruling.
أقوال الصحابة (aqwal al-sahaba): Legal opinions of the Companions of the Prophet, considered a source in the hierarchy for resolving conflict between sunnahs.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive rulings when texts conflict, considered after aqwal al-sahaba in the hierarchy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two sunnahs conflict, what does Fakhr al-Islam's use of the word 'aw' (or) indicate about the order between aqwal al-sahaba and qiyas?
A) Aqwal al-sahaba are always preferred.
B) Qiyas is always preferred.
C) No fixed order; the jurist may choose either.
D) Aqwal al-sahaba are preferred in matters of 'ibadat, qiyas in mu'amalat.

Key Takeaway
True ta'arud requires unity of time and place; the hierarchy proceeds from Quran to Sunnah to aqwal or qiyas, and finally to the original principle.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Rule of Affirming vs. Negating Narrations (al-Muthbit wa al-Nafi)
Establishing the rule that affirming evidence is preferred over negating evidence, with a condition for equality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule regarding conflict between affirming and negating narrations, distinguish al-Karkhi's view from Ibn Aban's, and apply the condition that resolves their disagreement.

Core Idea
Affirming evidence is preferred over negation unless the negation is based on clear evidence, not mere istishab.

When two narrations appear to conflict—one affirming an additional ruling, the other denying it—which takes precedence? The Hanafi school has an established usul rule that the affirming (muthbit) is generally preferred over the negating (nafi), but this is not unconditional. This lesson unpacks the definitions, the two scholarly views within the school, and the key condition that determines when they become equal.

Guided Path
1
Define the terms
Understand what muthbit and nafi mean: muthbit establishes an additional matter not previously proven, nafi keeps the original ruling by denying that addition.
Muthbit is always based on evidence; nafi may be based on evidence or mere istishab.
2
State the two positions
Al-Karkhi holds that muthbit is preferable to nafi; Ibn Aban holds they are equal and require tarjih.
Both scholars are within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the condition
If nafi is based on clear evidence (dalil) or known to rely on evidence, it equals muthbit; if based on istishab, muthbit is preferred.
This condition resolves the disagreement between the two scholars.
4
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis sometimes follow muthbit, sometimes nafi, depending on whether the nafi is evidence-based.
This explains apparent inconsistencies in Hanafi rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمُثْبت أولى مِنَ النَّافِی هذه قَاعِدَةٌ مُسْتَقِلَةٌ لاَ تَعلُق لَهَا بِمَا سَبَقَ يَعْنِي إِذا تَعَارَضَ الْمُثْبِتُ وَالنَّافِي فَالْمُثْبِتْ أَوْلَى بِالْعَمَلِ مِنَ النَّافِى عِنْدَ الْكُرْخِي وَعِنْدَ ابْنِ أَبَانَ يَتَعَارَضَانِ أَيُّ يَتَسسَاوِيَانِ فَبَعْدَ ذَالِكَ يُصَارُ إِلَى التَّرْجِيْحِ بِحَالِ الرَّاوِي وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْمُثْبِت مَا يُثْبِتُ امْرًا عَارِضًا زَائِدًا لَمْ يُكُن ثَابِتا فِيْمَا مَضَى وَبِالنَّافِي مَا يَعْقِي الأَمْرُ الزَّائِدَ وَيُبْقِيْهِ عَلى الأَصْلِ وَلَمَّا وَقَعَ الاِخْتِلافُ بَيْنَ الْكَرْخِي وَابْن أَبَانَ وَوَقَع الاِخْتِلافُ فِي عَمَل أَصْحَابِنَا أَيْضًا فَفِي بَعْضِ الْمَوَاضِعَ يَعْمَلُوْنَ بِالْمُثْبَتِ وَفِي بِعْضِهَا بِالنَّافِي أَشْبَارُ الْمُصْفَ إِلى قَاعِدَة فِي ذَالِكَ تَرْفَعُ الْخِلافَ عَنْهُمْ فَقَالَ وَالأَصْلُ فِيهِ أَنَّ النَّفْى إن كَانَ مِنْ جِئْسٍ مَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ بِأَنْ كَانَ مَبْنِيًا عَلَى دَلِيْلٍ وَعَلَامَةٍ ظَاهِرَةٍ وَلَا يَكُونُ مُبْنِيًا على الاسْتِصْحَابِ الَّذِي لَيْسَ بِحُجَّةٍ أَوْ كَانَ مِمَّا يَسْتَبِهُ حَالُهُ لَكِنْ عُرِفَ أَنَّ الرَّاوِى اِعْتَمَدَ دَلِيْلَ الْمَعْرِفَةِ يَعْنِي كَانَ النفى فِى نَفْسِهِ مِمَّا يَحْتِمَلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُسْتَفَارًا مِنَ الدَّلِيلِ وَأَنْ يَكُونَ مُبْنِها عَلَى الاسْتِصْحَابِ لَكِنْ لَمَّا تَقُحْصَ عَنْ حَالِ الرَّاوِئ عُلِمَ أَنَّهُ اعْتَمَدَ عَلَى الدَّلِيلِ وَلَمْ يُنَبَّهُ عَلَى صَرْفِ ظَاهِرِ الْحَالِ فَفِى هَاتَيْنِ الصُّوْرَتَيْنِ كَانَ مِثْلُ الإِثْبَاتِ لَأَنْ الإثْبَات لاَ يَكُون إِلا بِدَلِيْل فَإِذَا كَانَ النُّفِي أَيْضًا بِدَلِيْلٍ كَانَ مِثْلَهُ فَيَتَعَارَضَ. بَيْنَهُمَا وَيُحْتَاجَ بَعْدَ ذَالِكَ إِلَى دَفْعِهِ فَجَاءَ مَذْهَبُ ابْنُ أَبَانَ وَإِلا فَلَا أَنْ لَمْ يُكُن النَّفْى مِن جِئْسٍ مَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ وَلَا مَا عُرِفَ أَنَّ الرَّاوِي اعْتَمَدَ عَلَى الدَّلِيلِ بَلْ بنَاهُ عَلَى ظَاهِرِ الْحَالِ الْمَاضِيَةِ فَلا يَكُونَ مِثْلُ الإِثْبَاتِ فِي مُعَارَضَتِهِ بِل الإِثْبَاتُ أَوْلى لأنَّهُ ثَابِت بالدِّلِيلِ فَجَاء مَذْهَبُ الْكَرْخِي فَنَحْنُ نَحْتَاجُ حِ إِلَى ثَلاثَةِ أَمْثَلَةِ مَثَالَيْنِ لِكَوْنِ النَّفِي مُعَارِضا لِلإِثْبَاتِ وَمِثَالُ لَكَوْنِ الإِثْبَاتِ أَوْلَى | مِنْهُ عَلَى مَا بَيْنَهَا الْمُصَنَّف بِتَمَامِهَا لَكِنْ أَوْرَدَهَا عَلَى غَيْرِ تَرْتِيبِ اللَّفْ فَجَاءَ أولاً بمثال قوله والأ فَلا فَقَالَ فَالنَّفَى فِي حَدِيث بَرِيْرَةَ وَهِيَ الَّتِي كَانَتْ مُكَاتبَةٌ لعَائِشَةَ وَكَانَتْ فِي نِكَاحِ عَبْدٍ فَلَمَّا أَدَّتْ بُدَلَ الْكِتَابَةِ قَالَ لَهَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مَلَكُت يُصْعَكَ فَاخْتَارِئ وَلَكِن أُخْتلِف فِي أَنه حِينَ خَيْرَهَا هَلْ يَقِى
And the affirming is preferable to the negating. This is an independent rule having no relation to what preceded, meaning: when the affirming and negating are contradictory, then at al-Karkhi the affirming is preferable to act upon over the negating. And at Ibn Aban, they contradict, i.e., they are equal; then after that one turns to preference by the condition of the narrator. And by 'affirming' is meant what establishes an incidental additional matter that was not established in the past, and by 'negating' what negates the additional matter and keeps it upon the original. And when disagreement occurred between al-Karkhi and Ibn Aban, and disagreement also occurred in the practice of our companions, for in some places they act upon the affirming and in some upon the negating, the author pointed to a rule in that which removes the disagreement from them. So he said: The principle in it is that the negation, if it is of the kind that is known by its evidence, i.e., it is based on evidence and a clear sign, and is not based on istishab which is not a proof, or if its status is ambiguous but it is known that the narrator relied on evidence of knowledge—meaning the negation in itself is such that it could be derived from evidence or based on istishab, but when investigating the state of the narrator, it is known that he relied on evidence and did not build on the apparent surface of the case—then in these two forms it is like the affirmation, because affirmation is only by evidence; so if the negation is also by evidence, it is like it, and they conflict, and after that one needs to remove the conflict. So came the school of Ibn Aban. Otherwise, if the negation is not of the kind known by its evidence, nor is it known that the narrator relied on evidence, but rather he built it on the apparent previous state, then it is not like the affirmation in opposing it; rather the affirmation is preferable because it is established by evidence. So came the school of al-Karkhi. Then we need three examples: two for the negation opposing the affirmation, and one for the affirmation being preferable over it, as the author fully explained, but he presented them out of order. So he first gave the example of his statement '...' He said: The negation in the hadith of Barira—she was a mukataba [slave with contract of manumission] belonging to Aisha, and she was married to a slave. When she paid the price of her kitaba, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to her: 'You have obtained your freedom, so choose.' But there is disagreement about whether, when he gave her the choice, there remained... [text cuts off]
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage introduces another usul rule: when a muthbit (affirming narration) conflicts with a nafi (negating narration), the muthbit is given precedence according to Imam al-Karkhi. Ibn Aban holds that they are equal and then one must seek tarjih based on the narrator's reliability. The author explains the definitions: muthbit establishes an additional ruling that was not previously present, while nafi denies that addition and keeps the original state. Al-Karkhi's position is that nafi is not considered a proof unless it is based on direct evidence and not on istishab (presumption of continuity). If the nafi is based on a clear evidence (dalil) or if it is known that the narrator relied on evidence despite ambiguity, then it becomes equal to muthbit and they conflict, requiring tarjih—this is Ibn Aban's view. If the nafi is merely based on the apparent previous state (istishab), then it is not equivalent and muthbit is preferred. The author promises three examples: two where nafi opposes muthbit (so they conflict) and one where muthbit is clearly preferable. He begins with the example from the hadith of Barira, regarding her marriage to a slave and the choice given upon emancipation, but the text cuts off. This rule is particularly relevant when dealing with apparently contradictory hadiths or narrations.

Key Terms
المُثْبِت (al-muthbit): A narration that establishes an additional (accidental) matter that was not previously proven.
النَّافِي (al-nāfī): A narration that negates the additional matter and keeps the ruling on the original state.
الاستصحاب (al-istiṣḥāb): Presumption of continuity of the original ruling until evidence changes it.
التَّرْجِيح (al-tarjīḥ): Preferring one evidence over another based on external factors like narrator reliability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Karkhi, when does a negating narration (nafi) become equal to an affirming narration (muthbit)?
A) When the nafi is based on istishab
B) When the nafi is based on clear evidence
C) Never, because muthbit is always stronger
D) Only if the narrator is a sahabi

Key Takeaway
The affirming narration is preferred over the negating unless the negating is based on clear evidence, in which case they conflict and require tarjih.

Al-Muthbit Awla min al-Nafi: Conditions of the Affirmation Preference Rule
Explanation of a usul rule with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule 'al-muthbit awla min al-nafi' by distinguishing when negation is based on istishab versus substantive evidence, and determine which Hanafi usuli's approach applies.

Core Idea
The affirming proof wins over negation only when negation relies on istishab; if negation has its own evidence, both must be weighed.

This passage presents a foundational usul rule for resolving apparent contradictions between two reports. The rule seems simple, but its application depends critically on the nature of the negating evidence. We will explore the positions of two Hanafi masters—al-Karkhi and Ibn Aban—and see how their disagreement shapes the fiqh ruling on a slave woman's option after emancipation.

Guided Path
1
State the rule and its apparent meaning
Identify the Arabic maxim 'al-muthbit awla min al-nafi' and its literal translation. Understand that it gives priority to the affirming proof over the negating proof in cases of ta'arud.
The rule is general, but it has conditions.
2
Distinguish between the two Hanafi positions
Al-Karkhi holds the affirmer is always preferred. Ibn Aban holds that if negation is based on substantive evidence, both are equivalent and require external tarjih.
The key is the basis of the negation.
3
Analyze the condition that separates them
If negation is based on istishab (presumption of continuity), it is weaker; if based on independent evidence (dalil), it is equivalent to affirmation.
Istishab is a weak proof in the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the rule to the Barirah hadith
The narrators agree that Barirah's husband was a slave originally. The conflicting reports differ on whether he became free. The negating report (he remained slave) relies on istishab; the affirming report (he became free) is based on evidence. Thus al-Karkhi's rule applies.
This matches the Hanafi position that the option exists regardless of the husband's status.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa) gives the option in all cases; Shafi'i school restricts it to when the husband remains a slave.
The usul rule directly impacts a fiqh ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمثبت أولى من النافي. وهذا قاعدة مستقل. يعني إذا تعارض مثبت ونافي فالمثبت أولى عند الكرخي. وعند ابن أبان يبقى التعارض ثم يرجح بعد النظر في حال الراوي. والمثبت ما يثبت أمرا عارضا كان معدوما في الماضي. والنافي ما ينفي أمرا زائدا ويبقي الأصل. والأصل فيه أن النفي إن كان من جنس ما يعرف بدليله أو كان مما يشتبه حاله لكن عرف أن الراوي اعتمد دليل المعرفة فإنه مثل الإثبات في التعارض ويحتاج إلى دفع التعارض فعند ذلك مذهب ابن أبان. وإن لم يكن كذلك بل بناه على ظاهر الحال الماضية فلا يكون مثل الإثبات بل الإثبات أولى فعند ذلك مذهب الكرخي. فنحتاج إلى ثلاثة أمثلة: مثالين لكون النفي معارضا للإثبات ومثال لكون الإثبات أولى. فذكر المصنف أولا مثال النفي في حديث بريرة رضي الله عنها. وكانت مكاتبة لعائشة وكانت في نكاح عبد فلما أدت بدل الكتابة قال لها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ملكت بضعك فاختاري. واختلف في أنه حين خيرها هل بقي زوجها عبدا أم صار حرا؟ فقيل: إنه كان عبدا على حاله وهو مختار الشافعي حيث لا يثبت الخيار للمعتقة إلا إذا كان زوجها عبدا. وقيل: قد صار حرا وهو مختار أبي حنيفة حيث يثبت الخيار للمعتقة سواء كان زوجها عبدا أو حرا. فالحرية وإن كانت أصلية في دار الإسلام والعبودية عارضة لكن لما اتفقت الرواة على أن زوجها كان عبدا في الحقيقة وإنما وقع الاختلاف في الحرية العارضة كان خبر العبودية نافيا للحرية العارضة ومبقيا له على الأصل وخبر الحرية مثبتا للأمر العارض. فخبر النفي وهو ما روي أنها أعتقت وزوجها
The one who affirms is preferable over the one who negates. This is an independent rule. Meaning, when there is contradiction between an affirmer and a negator, the affirmer is preferable according to al-Karkhi. According to Ibn Aban, the contradiction remains, then preference is given after examining the state of the narrator. The affirmer is that which establishes an incidental matter that was non-existent in the past. The negator is that which negates an additional matter and keeps the original. The principle regarding it is that if the negation is of the type known by its evidence, or is of a type whose state is ambiguous but it is known that the narrator relied on the evidence of knowledge, then it is like affirmation in causing contradiction and needs to be resolved; in that case the school of Ibn Aban applies. If it is not like that, but rather is based on the apparent prior state, then it is not like affirmation, and affirmation is preferable; in that case the school of al-Karkhi applies. We need three examples: two examples where negation contradicts affirmation, and one example where affirmation is preferable. The author first mentioned the example of negation in the hadith of Barirah, may Allah be pleased with her. She was a mukatabah of A'ishah and was married to a slave. When she paid the kitabah, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to her: 'You have gained ownership of yourself, so choose.' And there is disagreement about whether at the time he gave her the choice her husband remained a slave or became free. It is said that he remained a slave, and this is the chosen view of al-Shafi'i, as he does not affirm the option for an emancipated slave woman if her husband is a slave. And it is said that he became free, and this is the chosen view of Abu Hanifah, as he affirms the option for an emancipated slave woman regardless of whether her husband is a slave or free. Freedom, although it is the original state in dar al-Islam, and slavery is incidental, but since the narrators agreed that her husband was indeed a slave originally, and the disagreement was only about incidental freedom, the report of slavery negates incidental freedom and keeps him upon the original, while the report of freedom affirms the incidental matter. So the report of negation, which is that she was freed while her husband...
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the usul rule 'al-muthbit awla min al-nafi' (the affirming proof is preferable over the negating proof) and its application. The author first states the rule and immediately presents the ikhtilaf between two Hanafi usulis: Imam al-Karkhi holds that the affirming proof is absolutely preferable, while Ibn Aban holds that both remain in contradiction and require external tarjih based on the narrator's reliability. The key to the disagreement lies in the nature of the negation. The author explains that if the negation is based on a substantive dalil (evidence) or is known to be based on a narrator's reliance on such dalil rather than on istishab (presumption of continuity), then it is equivalent to an affirming proof and both enter into ta'arud. In that case, Ibn Aban's method of seeking tarjih applies. But if the negation is merely based on istishab—i.e., the apparent prior state—then it does not compete with the affirming proof, and al-Karkhi's rule applies: the affirmer is preferred. The passage then introduces the hadith of Barirah as the first example. Barirah was a mukatabah of A'ishah, married to a slave. When she gained her freedom, the Prophet gave her the choice to remain with her husband or separate. The dispute is whether her husband was still a slave at that moment or had also become free. The narrators agree that he was originally a slave; they differ about the incidental freedom. The report saying he remained a slave is a negation based on istishab (original slavery), so according to al-Karkhi it does not outweigh the affirming report that he became free. Abu Hanifa thus affirms the option in all cases, while al-Shafi'i restricts it to when the husband is a slave. The passage ends abruptly while continuing the discussion.

Key Terms
المثبت (al-muthbit): The one who affirms an incidental matter (amr 'arid) that was previously non-existent
النافي (al-nafi): The one who negates an additional matter and affirms the original state
الاستصحاب (al-istishab): Presumption of continuity of the original state until evidence changes it

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does negation become equivalent to affirmation and require external tarjih?
A) When the negation is based on istishab
B) When the negation is based on substantive evidence or known to be based on such
C) Always, regardless of the basis
D) Only when the narrator is unreliable

Key Takeaway
The rule 'al-muthbit awla min al-nafi' applies definitively only when the negation is based on istishab; if negation rests on its own evidence, both proofs must be weighed externally.

Conflicting Reports: Muthbit Preferred Over Nafi
Applying usul to cases of contradictory reports on purity and permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a positive report (muthbit) is preferred over a negation (nafi) when conflicting reports lack evidence, and identify when a nafi report becomes acceptable due to supporting evidence.

Core Idea
When reports conflict, the positive claim overrides the negation unless the negation is backed by clear evidence.

This lesson examines the Hanafi usul rule for resolving contradictions between reports on purity and permissibility. Using the example of water purity and the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah, we learn how evidence-based reports are distinguished from mere negations. Understanding this principle is crucial for deriving rulings in cases of conflicting testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting reports
Recognize which report is a positive claim (muthbit) affirming an incidental state (e.g., impurity, ihram) and which is a negation (nafi) asserting the original ruling (purity, halal).
2
Examine the evidentiary basis of the nafi report
Determine whether the nafi report is supported by evidence (ma yu'rafu bi-dalilihi) or merely states the original ruling without any supporting observation or reasoning.
3
Apply the Hanafi preference rule
If the nafi lacks evidence, the muthbit is given precedence. If the nafi has evidence (e.g., direct observation of the chain of purity), both are considered, but the muthbit still overrides unless the nafi's evidence is equally strong.
The original ruling (asl) is only used when evidence is balanced.
4
Analyze the Maymunah hadith
One report says the Prophet married Maymunah in ihram (muthbit), another says halal (nafi). The muthbit is preferred because the nafi reporter lacks evidence; additionally, the muthbit narrator (Ibn Abbas) is more reliable.
5
Conclude the practical ruling
In cases of conflicting reports on water purity or food permissibility, the report affirming impurity/prohibition takes precedence unless the opposing report is clearly evidenced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطَّهَارَةُ أَوِ الحِلُّ لَمْ يُقْبَلُ خَيْرُهُ لأَنَّهُ نَفِيَ بِلا دَلِيلِ وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ أَخَذَهُ مِنَ الْعَيْنِ الْجَارِيَةِ أَوْ الْحَوْضِ الْعَشْرِ فِي الْعَشْرِ وَجَعَلَهُ بِنَفْسِهِ فِي الإِناءِ الطَّاهِرِ الْجَدِيدِ أوِ الْمُسَيْلِ بِحَيْثُ لا يَعْمُكُ فِي طَهَارَتِهِ وَلَمْ يُقَارِقُهُ مُنْذُ الْقَى الْمَاءَ فِيهِ حَتى يُتَوَهُمَ أَنَّهُ الْقِى فِيْهِ النَّجَاسَةَ أَحَدٌ كَانَ هَذَا النَّفْئُ مِنْ جِنْسِ مَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ. فَخَبَرُ النَّفْي فِي بَابِ حَدِیث میمونه پس لی کی خیبر (حدیث) میمونہ کے باب میں اوردہ ترجم تشريح وَهُوَ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ تَزَوْجَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرم ہے یعنی وہ حدیث جو مروی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت میمونہ سے نکاح فرمایا اس حالت میں کہ وہ محرم تھے ما يعرف بدلیلہ کی جنس سے ہے و دلیل محرم کی ظاہری حالت و کیفیت ہے مثلاً بغیر سلے ہوئے کپڑے پہننا اور ناخونوں کانہ کا نما اور سر کے بالوں کا نہ موٹر نا یہ علم مستند الی دلیل ہے۔ معارض الإثبات الخ اس لئے نفی معارض ہو گی ثبت کی یعنی وہ حدیث جو مروی ہے کہ اس حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت میمونہ رضی اللہ عنھا سے نکاح کیا اس حالت میں کہ آپ حلال (بغیر احرام کے ) تھے اس وجہ سے کہ جس نے اس کی خبر دی ہے اس میں شک نہیں کہ اس نے آپ کو دیکھا ہو گا کہ بغیر احرام ( محللین) کا لباس پہنے ہوئے تھے اور ان کی حیات میں تھے پس جب دونوں خبروں میں تعارض مساوی طور پر واقع ہوا تو دونوں میں سے ایک کو ترجیح دینے کی ضرورت ہوئی راوی کی حالت کو پیش نظر رکھ کرو جعل روایتہ ابن عباس اور ترجیح دینا حضرت ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہ کی روایت کو اور وہ یہ ہے کہ آپ نے نکاح فرمایا اس حالت میں کہ آپ محرم تھے۔ أولى مِنْ بِوَايَةِ يَزِيدَ بْن الأهتم اولی ہے یزید ابن اسم کی روایت سے روایت یہ ہے کہ آپ نے ان سے نکاح کیا اس حالت میں کہ آپ حلال تھے (بغیر احرام حالت میں تھے ) کیوں کہ یزید ابن اسم ضبط اور اتقان میں ان کے مساوی نہیں ہیں اس توجیہ کی رو سے زیر بحث سندیں حدیث تفی معمولی قرار دی گئی۔ وَطَهَارَةُ المَاءِ وَحِلُّ الطعام پانی کی عمارت اور طعام کی حلت کی خیر ما يعرف بدلیل کی جنس سے ہے یہ اس کی مثال ہے کہ راوی نے دلیل معرفت پر اعتماد کیا ہے مگر مصنف کی عبارت میں تھوڑی سی مساحت پائی جاتی ہے بہتر یہ تھا کہ یوں فرماتے پانی اور طعام کی حلت ما تشتبه حاله کی جنس ہے ہے لیکن جب مصنف نے پہچان لیا کہ راوی نے دلیل معرفت پر اعتماد کیا ہے تو یہ حدیث ما يعرف بدلیلہ کے قبیل سے ہو گئی۔ وئیانہ اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ پانی کی اصل طہارت ہے اور طعام میں اصل حلت ہے جب اس کی خبر دینے والوں میں تعارض واقع ہوا اپس دونوں میں سے ایک کہتا ہے کہ نجس یا حرام ہے تو اس میں شک نہیں کہ یہ امر عارضی کو ثابت کرتی ہے اس کائل نے دلیل ہی سے کہا ہو گا پھر دوسر ارادی آیا اور کہتا ہے کہ یہ طاھر ہے یا حلال ہے تو ضروری ہو گیا کہ اس راوی کی حالت کی تلاش و تحقیق کی جائے ہیں اگر اس کی خبر صرف یہ ہے کہ اصل اس میں حالت یا مھارت ہے تو اس کی خبر قبول نہ کی جائے گی کیوں کہ یہ نفی بلادلیل کے ہے۔ لہذا اس وقت نجاست یا حرمت کی خیر اولی ہو گی کیوں کہ وہ مثبت ہے اور اگر اسکی خیر کسی دلیل سے ہے اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے اس پانی کو جاری چشمہ سے حاصل کیا ہے دو دردہ حوض سے لیا ہے اور خود اپنے ہاتھ سے برتن میں رکھا ہے جو کہ پاک تھا نیا برتن تھا یا دھلا ہوا تھا اس طرح پر کہ اس کی طھارت میں کسی قسم کا کوئی شک نہیں ہے اور وہ اس برتن سے پانی رکھنے کے بعد جدا بھی نہیں ہوا ہے تا کہ یہ وہم پید ا ہو کہ اس پر تین یا پانی میں کسی نے نجاست ڈال دی ہو گی تو اس قسم کی تھی وہ کہلاتی ہے جو ما يعرف بدلیل کی جنس سے ہے۔ كَالنَّجَاسَةِ وَالْحُرْمَةِ لَوُوَقَعَ التَّعَارَضَ بَيْنَ الْخَبْرَيْنِ فَوَجَبَ الْعَمَلُ بِالأَصْلِ وَهُوَ الحل والطهَارَةُ وَقَدْ بَالغَنَا فِي تَحْقِيقِ الأَمثلة ع بِمَا لَأَمَزِيدَ عَلَيْهِ
Purity or permissibility: his report is not accepted because it is a negation without evidence, and that evidence is that he took it from a flowing spring or a ten-by-ten basin and placed it himself in a new pure vessel or a washed vessel, such that there is no doubt about its purity, and he did not leave it since putting the water in it up to the point that one might suspect someone threw impurity into it. So this negation is from the type of what is known by its evidence. The report of negation in the chapter of the hadith of Maymunah... And the report of negation in the chapter of the hadith of Maymunah: it is what is narrated that he married her while he was in ihram. That hadith is from the type of what is known by its evidence, and the evidence of ihram is the apparent state and condition, such as wearing unstitched garments, not trimming nails, and not combing hair; this knowledge is based on evidence. Opposing the positive report... so the negation is opposed by the affirmation. That is, the hadith narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) married Maymunah (may Allah be pleased with her) while he was halal (without ihram) because the one who reported it no doubt saw him wearing the clothes of the non-muhrim (the lawful ones) and he was alive. When the two reports conflict equally, the need arises to prefer one over the other by considering the state of the narrator. They gave preference to the narration of Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) that he married while in ihram, over the narration of Yazid ibn al-Asamm that he married while halal, because Yazid ibn al-Asamm is not equal to him in precision and reliability. Based on this reasoning, the reports under discussion concerning the hadith of negation were considered ordinary. And the purity of water and the permissibility of food: the report of purity/permissibility is from the type of what is known by its evidence. This is an example where the reporter relied on evidence of knowledge, but the author's expression has a slight inaccuracy. It would have been better if he said: the purity of water and permissibility of food are from the type of what is ambiguous in its state. But when the author realized that the reporter relied on evidence, this hadith became from the category of what is known by its evidence. Its explanation is that the original ruling of water is purity and of food is permissibility. When the reporters differ, one says it is impure or forbidden; no doubt this proves an incidental matter, and that speaker must have said so based on evidence. Then another reporter comes and says it is pure or permissible; it becomes necessary to investigate the state of this reporter. If his report is only that the original state or knowledge is such, then his report is not accepted because it is a negation without evidence. Therefore, at that time, the report of impurity or prohibition is given precedence because it is positive. And if his report is based on some evidence, and that evidence is that he took this water from a flowing spring or from a large basin and placed it himself in a vessel that was pure, new or washed, such that there is no doubt in its purification, and he did not leave it after placing the water up to the point that one might suspect someone threw impurity in it, then this type of report is called from the type of what is known by its evidence. Like impurity and prohibition: when conflict occurs between the two reports, acting upon the original ruling becomes obligatory, which is permissibility and purity. We have elaborated on the verification of examples beyond which there is no addition.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is an usul al-fiqh discussion on the treatment of conflicting reports (khabar) regarding the purity of water and permissibility of food, and by extension, any similar case. The author explains that a report claiming impurity or prohibition is considered a muthbit (positive claim) because it asserts an incidental state that requires evidence. In contrast, a report claiming purity or permissibility is often a nafi (negation) of that incidental state, which without evidence is rejected. However, if the reporter of purity/permissibility has clear evidence—such as having directly taken the water from a pure source and placed it in a pure vessel with no possibility of contamination—then his report is considered 'known by its evidence' (ma yu'rafu bi-dalilihi) and is accepted. The author illustrates this through the famous hadith of the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah (may Allah be pleased with her): one report says he was in ihram, another says he was halal. The report of ihram is muthbit (positive), and the report of halal is nafi. The latter is rejected unless it has supporting evidence. In the case of water and food, the original ruling (asl) is purity and permissibility. When two reports conflict, if one is muthbit and the other nafi, the muthbit is preferred. The author emphasizes that this analysis is thorough and complete.

Key Terms
مَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ (mā yuʿrafu bi-dalīlihi): A report whose validity is known by the evidence provided by the reporter, such as direct observation or clear reasoning
نَفْي (nafy): A report that denies an incidental state (e.g., impurity) and asserts the original ruling
إِثْبَات (ithbāt): A report that affirms an incidental state contrary to the original ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul discussed, when a conflict arises between a report claiming water is impure and a report claiming it is pure, and the latter report's reporter merely states the original purity without evidence, which report is given precedence?
A) The report of purity because it aligns with the original ruling
B) The report of impurity because it is a positive claim (muthbit) while the other is a negation without evidence
C) Both reports are rejected and further investigation is required
D) The report of the majority of narrators

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a positive report (muthbit) is preferred over a negation (nafi) when the latter lacks evidence, unless the nafi is supported by clear evidence that equalizes the scale.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
beginner

Tarjih: The Primacy of Narrator Reliability
Stating the rule that preference among reports is not based on number, gender, or freedom of narrators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that preference among conflicting reports is based on narrator reliability ('adalah), not on number, gender, or social status, and cite the examples of 'A'ishah and Bilal.

Core Idea
Reliability ('adalah) governs tarjih, not quantity, gender, or freedom.

In Hanafi usul, when two reports conflict, the key to preference is the reliability of the narrators, not how many there are, their gender, or whether they are free or slave. This passage establishes that principle and illustrates it with the examples of 'A'ishah and Bilal, who despite being a woman and a freed slave, were more virtuous than many men and free persons.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage explicitly states that preference does not occur by superiority of number, masculinity/femininity, or freedom/slavery. This is the core rule.
The Arabic phrase 'لا يقع بفضل عدد الرواة بالذكورة والأنوثة والحرية' captures this.
2
Recognize the exclusive criterion
The passage then explains that 'what is considered in this chapter is reliability ('adalah).' This is the sole factor for preference.
'Adalah includes moral uprightness and precision in transmission.
3
Understand the rationale
Reliability does not differ by number, gender, or freedom. The examples of 'A'ishah and Bilal demonstrate that a female and an enslaved person can have higher 'adalah than many men and free persons.
This reinforces that external factors are irrelevant to reliability.
4
Connect to illustrative examples
'A'ishah (RA) was more virtuous than most men; Bilal (RA) was more virtuous than most free men. The passage also notes that a small group of just narrators is better than a large group of sinful ones.
These examples are given as proof for the rule.

ثُمَّ يَقُولُ المُصنف وَالتَّرْجِيْعُ لَا يَقَعُ بِفَصْلِ عَدَدِ الرُّوَاةِ بِالذَّكُورَةِ وَالأنْوْثَةِ وَالْحُرِّيَةِ يَعْني إِذَا كَانَ فِي أَحَدٍ الْحَبَرَيْنِ الْمُتَعَارَضَيْنِ كَثْرَةُ الرُّوَاةِ فِي الْآخَرِ قَلْتُهَا أَوْ كَانَ رَاوَى أَحَدِهِمَا مَذْكُرًا وَالآخَرِ مُونْثًا أَوْ رَاوِيُّ أَحَدِهِمَا حُرًّا وَالْآخَرِ عَبْدًا لَمْ يَرَجْحُ اَحَدُ الْخَبَرَيْنِ عَلَى الْآخَرِ بِدَهِ الْمِيْرِ لأَنَّ الْمُعْتَبَرَ فِي هَذَا الْبَابِ الْعَدَالَةُ وَفِيَ لاتَخْتَلِفُ بِالْكَثْرَةِ وَالذُكُورَةِ وَالْحَرْيَةِ فَإِنْ عَائِشَةَ كَانَتْ أَفْضَلَ مِنْ أَكْثَرِ الرِّجَالِ وبَلاَلاً كَانَ أَفْضَلَ مِنْ أكثر الحراير وَالْجَمَاعَةُ القَلِيْلَةُ الْعَادِلَةُ أَفْضَلُ مِن الْجَمَاعَةِ الكَثِيرَةِ الْعَاصِيةِ - وفِي قَوْلِهِ فَضْلُ عَدَدِ الرُّواةِ اشارَةٌ إِلَى أَنْ عَدَدَ لَا يَتَرَحُ عَلَىٰ عَدَدِ بَعْدَ أَنْ كَانَ فِى دَرَجَةِ الأَحَادِ وَأَمَّا إِنْ كَانَ فِي جَانِبِ وَاحِدٌ وَفِي جَانِبِ اثْنَانِ يُتَرَجَحُ خَيْرُ اثْنَيْنِ عَلَى خَبَرَ الْوَاحِدِ وَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ يَتَرَجَحُ جِهَةُ الْكَثْرَةِ عَلَى جَانِبِ الْقِلْةِ تَمَسكَا بِمَا ذَكَرَ مُحَمَّدٌ فِي مَسَائِلِ الْمَاءِ وَلَكِنَّا تَرَكْنَاهُ بِالاسْتِحْسَانِ وَأَذَا كَانَتْ فِي أَحَدِ الْخَبَرِيْنِ زِيَادَةُ فَإِنْ كَانَ الرَّاوِئ وَاحِدًا يُؤْخَذُ بِالْمُثْبِتِ لِلزَّيَادَةِ كَمَا فِي الخَبَرِ الْمَرْوِي فِي التُحَالُفِ وَهُوَ مَا رَوَى ابْنُ مَسْعُوْدٍ إِنَّهُ إِذَا اخْتَلَفَ الْمُتَبَايَعَانِ وَالسَّلعَةُ قَائِمَةٌ تَحَالَنَا وَتُرَادُ وَفِي رَوَايَةٍ أُخْرِى عَنْهُ لَمْ يَذْكُرُ قَوْلَهُ وَالسَّلعَةُ قَائِمَةٌ فَاَخَذْنَا بِالْمُثْبِتِ لِلزَّيَادَةِ وَقُلْنَا لاجئ التَّحَالُف إِلا عِنْدَ قِيَامِ السَّلْعَةِ فَكَانَ حذَبُ الْقَيْدِ مِنْ بَعْضٍ الرُّوَاةِ لِقِلَّةِ الضَّبْطِ
Then the author says: Preference does not occur by superiority of number of narrators, by masculinity or femininity, or by freedom or slavery. That is, if one of the two conflicting reports has many narrators and the other few, or one narrator is male and the other female, or one is free and the other slave, one report is not preferred over the other by this matter, because what is considered in this chapter is reliability ('adalah), and it does not differ by number, masculinity, or freedom. Indeed, 'A'ishah was more virtuous than most men, and Bilal was more virtuous than most free men. And a small group of just narrators is more virtuous than a large group of sinful ones. And in his saying 'by superiority of number of narrators' is an indication that number does not outweigh number when both are in the grade of ahad. But if on one side there is one narrator and on the other side two, the report of two is preferred over the report of one. Some said the side of many is preferred over the side of few, clinging to what Muhammad mentioned in the issues of water, but we left that by istihsan. And if in one of the two reports there is an increase (ziyadah), and the narrator is the same, the positive one for the increase is taken, as in the report narrated concerning the oath (tahāluf): Ibn Mas'ud narrated that if the two buyers differ and the commodity is still present, they take an oath and return it. In another narration from him, he did not mention his saying 'and the commodity is still present.' So we took the positive report for the increase and said: there is no oath except when the commodity is present. So the omission of the condition by some narrators was due to lack of precision.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a rule in tarjih (preference) between conflicting ahadith. The author clarifies that mere numerical superiority, gender, or freedom/enslavement of narrators does not give preference. The key criterion is reliability ('adalah). He offers examples that 'A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her) and Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him) were superior to many men and free persons. However, there is an exception: if one side has one narrator and the other has two, the two narrators are given preference because the additional number indicates greater reliability (assuming both sides are equally 'adil). Regarding an increase (ziyadah) in one version from the same narrator, we accept the positive (muthbit) version because the omission is likely due to lack of precision. The example is the hadith on tahāluf (oath) in sales: one version includes the condition 'while the commodity is still present', another omits it; we take the version with the condition.

Key Terms
تَرْجِيْع (tarjīʿ): The process of preferring one report over another when they conflict
زِيَادَة (ziyādah): An additional piece of information in one version of a hadith from the same narrator
عَدَالَة (ʿadālah): Reliability and uprightness of a narrator

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which factor is the sole basis for preferring one report over another?
A) The number of narrators
B) The gender of narrators
C) The reliability (adalah) of narrators
D) The freedom of narrators

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school of usul prioritizes narrator reliability ('adalah) over numerical majority, gender, or social status when conflicting reports require tarjih.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Tarjih: Exceptions and the Ziyadah Rule
Explaining the exception for one vs. two narrators, the rule for accepting increases (ziyadah), and the dispute with majority preference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when one narrator faces two, the two are preferred, and that an increase (ziyādah) from the same narrator is accepted, and evaluate the dispute with those who prioritize majority based on Imam Muhammad's water issues.

Core Idea
Two narrators trump one, and a narrator's addition is accepted over omission.

While the general rule prioritizes reliability, there is a specific exception: when one side has a single narrator and the other has two (both equally reliable), the two narrators are preferred. Additionally, if the same narrator adds an extra detail in one version, that detail is accepted because omission is due to lack of precision. Some scholars cite Imam Muhammad's water issues to argue for majority preference, but Hanafis set that aside by istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Understand the exception for one vs. two narrators
The passage states: 'if on one side there is one narrator and on the other side two, the report of two is preferred over the report of one.' This is a specific exception to the general rule that number does not matter.
This exception applies only when both sides are equally reliable ('adil).
2
Learn the ziyadah rule
When the same narrator gives two versions, one with an additional detail (ziyadah), we accept the version with the addition (muthbit) because the omission is attributed to lack of precision.
The example of the tahāluf hadith illustrates this: one version includes 'while the commodity is still present', the other does not; we take the version with the condition.
3
Analyze the dispute over majority preference
Some scholars argue that majority should always be preferred, citing Imam Muhammad's rulings on water issues. The Hanafi response: 'we left that by istihsan' and maintain that reliability is primary, accepting the exception only for one vs. two.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the practical difference in which report is preferred in a given case.

ثُمَّ يَقُولُ المُصنف وَالتَّرْجِيْعُ لَا يَقَعُ بِفَصْلِ عَدَدِ الرُّوَاةِ بِالذَّكُورَةِ وَالأنْوْثَةِ وَالْحُرِّيَةِ يَعْني إِذَا كَانَ فِي أَحَدٍ الْحَبَرَيْنِ الْمُتَعَارَضَيْنِ كَثْرَةُ الرُّوَاةِ فِي الْآخَرِ قَلْتُهَا أَوْ كَانَ رَاوَى أَحَدِهِمَا مَذْكُرًا وَالآخَرِ مُونْثًا أَوْ رَاوِيُّ أَحَدِهِمَا حُرًّا وَالْآخَرِ عَبْدًا لَمْ يَرَجْحُ اَحَدُ الْخَبَرَيْنِ عَلَى الْآخَرِ بِدَهِ الْمِيْرِ لأَنَّ الْمُعْتَبَرَ فِي هَذَا الْبَابِ الْعَدَالَةُ وَفِيَ لاتَخْتَلِفُ بِالْكَثْرَةِ وَالذُكُورَةِ وَالْحَرْيَةِ فَإِنْ عَائِشَةَ كَانَتْ أَفْضَلَ مِنْ أَكْثَرِ الرِّجَالِ وبَلاَلاً كَانَ أَفْضَلَ مِنْ أكثر الحراير وَالْجَمَاعَةُ القَلِيْلَةُ الْعَادِلَةُ أَفْضَلُ مِن الْجَمَاعَةِ الكَثِيرَةِ الْعَاصِيةِ - وفِي قَوْلِهِ فَضْلُ عَدَدِ الرُّواةِ اشارَةٌ إِلَى أَنْ عَدَدَ لَا يَتَرَحُ عَلَىٰ عَدَدِ بَعْدَ أَنْ كَانَ فِى دَرَجَةِ الأَحَادِ وَأَمَّا إِنْ كَانَ فِي جَانِبِ وَاحِدٌ وَفِي جَانِبِ اثْنَانِ يُتَرَجَحُ خَيْرُ اثْنَيْنِ عَلَى خَبَرَ الْوَاحِدِ وَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ يَتَرَجَحُ جِهَةُ الْكَثْرَةِ عَلَى جَانِبِ الْقِلْةِ تَمَسكَا بِمَا ذَكَرَ مُحَمَّدٌ فِي مَسَائِلِ الْمَاءِ وَلَكِنَّا تَرَكْنَاهُ بِالاسْتِحْسَانِ وَأَذَا كَانَتْ فِي أَحَدِ الْخَبَرِيْنِ زِيَادَةُ فَإِنْ كَانَ الرَّاوِئ وَاحِدًا يُؤْخَذُ بِالْمُثْبِتِ لِلزَّيَادَةِ كَمَا فِي الخَبَرِ الْمَرْوِي فِي التُحَالُفِ وَهُوَ مَا رَوَى ابْنُ مَسْعُوْدٍ إِنَّهُ إِذَا اخْتَلَفَ الْمُتَبَايَعَانِ وَالسَّلعَةُ قَائِمَةٌ تَحَالَنَا وَتُرَادُ وَفِي رَوَايَةٍ أُخْرِى عَنْهُ لَمْ يَذْكُرُ قَوْلَهُ وَالسَّلعَةُ قَائِمَةٌ فَاَخَذْنَا بِالْمُثْبِتِ لِلزَّيَادَةِ وَقُلْنَا لاجئ التَّحَالُف إِلا عِنْدَ قِيَامِ السَّلْعَةِ فَكَانَ حذَبُ الْقَيْدِ مِنْ بَعْضٍ الرُّوَاةِ لِقِلَّةِ الضَّبْطِ
Then the author says: Preference does not occur by superiority of number of narrators, by masculinity or femininity, or by freedom or slavery. That is, if one of the two conflicting reports has many narrators and the other few, or one narrator is male and the other female, or one is free and the other slave, one report is not preferred over the other by this matter, because what is considered in this chapter is reliability ('adalah), and it does not differ by number, masculinity, or freedom. Indeed, 'A'ishah was more virtuous than most men, and Bilal was more virtuous than most free men. And a small group of just narrators is more virtuous than a large group of sinful ones. And in his saying 'by superiority of number of narrators' is an indication that number does not outweigh number when both are in the grade of ahad. But if on one side there is one narrator and on the other side two, the report of two is preferred over the report of one. Some said the side of many is preferred over the side of few, clinging to what Muhammad mentioned in the issues of water, but we left that by istihsan. And if in one of the two reports there is an increase (ziyadah), and the narrator is the same, the positive one for the increase is taken, as in the report narrated concerning the oath (tahāluf): Ibn Mas'ud narrated that if the two buyers differ and the commodity is still present, they take an oath and return it. In another narration from him, he did not mention his saying 'and the commodity is still present.' So we took the positive report for the increase and said: there is no oath except when the commodity is present. So the omission of the condition by some narrators was due to lack of precision.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a rule in tarjih (preference) between conflicting ahadith. The author clarifies that mere numerical superiority, gender, or freedom/enslavement of narrators does not give preference. The key criterion is reliability ('adalah). He offers examples that 'A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her) and Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him) were superior to many men and free persons. However, there is an exception: if one side has one narrator and the other has two, the two narrators are given preference because the additional number indicates greater reliability (assuming both sides are equally 'adil). Regarding an increase (ziyadah) in one version from the same narrator, we accept the positive (muthbit) version because the omission is likely due to lack of precision. The example is the hadith on tahāluf (oath) in sales: one version includes the condition 'while the commodity is still present', another omits it; we take the version with the condition.

Key Terms
تَرْجِيْع (tarjīʿ): The process of preferring one report over another when they conflict
زِيَادَة (ziyādah): An additional piece of information in one version of a hadith from the same narrator
عَدَالَة (ʿadālah): Reliability and uprightness of a narrator

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the tahāluf hadith, why does the Hanafi school prefer the version that includes the condition 'while the commodity is still present'?
A) Because it has more narrators
B) Because the narrator is a male
C) Because the narrator who added the condition is considered more precise
D) Because the condition is supported by consensus

Key Takeaway
When narrators conflict in number (one vs. two) or in content (addition vs. omission), Hanafi usul provides clear rules for preference, always anchored in reliability and precision.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Tarjih: Preference by 'Adala, Not by Numbers or Demographics
Explaining that tarjih does not occur by quantity, gender, or freedom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that tarjih is not based on quantity, gender, or freedom, and apply the rule regarding ziyada when the narrator is the same.

Core Idea
Tarjih relies on 'adala, not numbers or demographics; a narrator's addition is accepted if the source is the same.

When two reports conflict, which one should we prefer? Some might think that a report narrated by many people is stronger, or that a male narrator outweighs a female, or a free person outweighs a slave. The Hanafi school clarifies that none of these factors determine preference. Instead, the key is the narrator's integrity ('adala). This lesson unpacks that foundational rule and also explains how to handle a case where one version of a hadith includes an extra wording (ziyada) while another omits it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
The author states that preference (tarjih) does not occur due to superiority in number of narrators, nor due to masculinity/femininity, nor due to freedom/slavery. Understand that the only relevant factor is the moral character ('adala) of the narrators.
This is a general principle for ahad reports, not for mutawatir.
2
Examine the examples given
The text provides two examples: Aisha (female) was superior to most men, and Bilal (a slave) was superior to most free persons. Also, a small group of upright people is better than a large group of sinful ones. These illustrate that numbers and demographics do not guarantee stronger evidence.
The examples are from the lifetime of the Prophet ﷺ, showing practical application.
3
Understand the exception for two vs one
Although numbers alone do not give preference when both reports are ahad, if one side has a single narrator and the other has two, the report of the two outweighs the one. This is because two narrators provide stronger certainty than one.
This is an exception to the general rule, but still within the ahad category.
4
Handle the addition (ziyada) rule
When the same narrator reports a hadith with an additional wording in one version and without it in another, the version with the addition is accepted. The omission is considered a lack of precision (qillat al-dabt).
This applies when the narrator is the same person; if different narrators, other rules apply.

Source Text

كَالنَّجَاسَةِ وَالْحُرْمَةِ لَوْ وَقَعَ التَّعَارُضُ بَيْنَ الْخَبَرَيْنِ فَوَجَبَ الْعَمَلُ بِالأَصْلِ وَهُوَ الْحَلُّ وَالطَّهَارَةُ وَقَدْ بَالَغْنَا فِي تَحْقِيقِ الأَمْثِلَةِ بِمَا لا مَزِيدَ عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ يَقُولُ الْمُصَنِّفُ وَالتَّرْجِيحُ لَا يَقَعُ بِفَضْلِ عَدَدِ الرُّوَاةِ وَبِالذُّكُورَةِ وَالأُنُوثَةِ وَالْحُرِّيَّةِ يَعْنِي إِذَا كَانَ فِي أَحَدِ الْخَبَرَيْنِ الْمُتَعَارِضَيْنِ كَثْرَةُ الرُّوَاةِ وَفِي الْآخَرِ قِلَّتُهَا أَوْ كَانَ رَاوِي أَحَدِهِمَا مُذَكَّرًا وَالْآخَرِ مُؤَنَّثًا أَوْ رَاوِي أَحَدِهِمَا حُرًّا وَالْآخَرِ عَبْدًا لَمْ يَتَرَجَّحْ أَحَدُ الْخَبَرَيْنِ عَلَى الْآخَرِ بِذَلِكَ لأَنَّ الْمُعْتَبَرَ فِي هَذَا الْبَابِ الْعَدَالَةُ وَهِيَ لا تَخْتَلِفُ بِالْكَثْرَةِ وَالذُّكُورَةِ وَالْحُرِّيَّةِ فَإِنَّ عَائِشَةَ كَانَتْ أَفْضَلَ مِنْ أَكْثَرِ الرِّجَالِ وَبِلالاً كَانَ أَفْضَلَ مِنْ أَكْثَرِ الْحَرَائِرِ وَالْجَمَاعَةُ الْقَلِيلَةُ الْعَادِلَةُ أَفْضَلُ مِنَ الْجَمَاعَةِ الْكَثِيرَةِ الْعَاصِيَةِ - وَفِي قَوْلِهِ فَضْلُ عَدَدِ الرُّوَاةِ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّ عَدَدًا لا يَتَرَجَّحُ عَلَى عَدَدٍ بَعْدَ أَنْ كَانَا فِي دَرَجَةِ الآحَادِ وَأَمَّا إِنْ كَانَ فِي جَانِبٍ وَاحِدٌ وَفِي جَانِبٍ اثْنَانِ فَيَتَرَجَّحُ خَبَرُ اثْنَيْنِ عَلَى خَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ وَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ يَتَرَجَّحُ جِهَةُ الْكَثْرَةِ عَلَى جَانِبِ الْقِلَّةِ تَمَسُّكًا بِمَا ذَكَرَ مُحَمَّدٌ فِي مَسَائِلِ الْمَاءِ وَلَكِنَّا تَرَكْنَاهُ بِالاسْتِحْسَانِ وَإِذَا كَانَتْ فِي أَحَدِ الْخَبَرَيْنِ زِيَادَةٌ فَإِنْ كَانَ الرَّاوِي وَاحِدًا يُؤْخَذُ بِالْمُثْبِتِ لِلزِّيَادَةِ كَمَا فِي الْخَبَرِ الْمَرْوِيِّ فِي التَّحَالُفِ وَهُوَ مَا رَوَى ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ أَنَّهُ إِذَا اخْتَلَفَ الْمُتَبَايِعَانِ وَالسِّلْعَةُ قَائِمَةٌ تَحَالَفَا وَتُرَادُ [؟] وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ أُخْرَى عَنْهُ لَمْ يَذْكُرْ قَوْلَهُ وَالسِّلْعَةُ قَائِمَةٌ فَأَخَذْنَا بِالْمُثْبِتِ لِلزِّيَادَةِ وَقُلْنَا لا يَجِيءُ التَّحَالُفُ إِلاَّ عِنْدَ قِيَامِ السِّلْعَةِ فَكَانَ حَذْفُ الْقَيْدِ مِنْ بَعْضِ الرُّوَاةِ لِقِلَّةِ الضَّبْطِ كَالنَّجَاسَةِ وَالْحُرْمَةِ
Like najasah and hurmah: if conflict occurs between two reports, acting upon the original becomes necessary, which is permissibility and purity. And we have elaborated on the verification of examples beyond which there is no more. Then the author says: preference does not occur by superiority of number of narrators, nor by masculinity and femininity, nor by freedom. Meaning: if in one of the two conflicting reports there is numerousness of narrators and in the other scarcity, or the narrator of one is male and the other female, or the narrator of one is free and the other is a slave, then one of the two reports does not outweigh the other by that, because what is considered in this chapter is 'adala (uprightness), and it does not differ by numerousness, masculinity, or freedom. For Aisha was better than most men, and Bilal was better than most freemen. And a small group of upright people is better than a large group of disobedient people. And in his saying 'superiority of number of narrators' there is an indication that one number does not outweigh another when both are in the degree of ahad. But if on one side there is one and on the other side two, then the report of two outweighs the report of one. Some said that the side of plurality outweighs the side of scarcity, adhering to what Muhammad mentioned in the issues of water, but we abandoned it by istihsan. And when in one of the two reports there is an addition, then if the narrator is one, the positive (report) with the addition is taken, as in the report narrated about the mutual oath, which is what Ibn Mas'ud narrated: when the two sellers dispute and the commodity is present, they take an oath and it is [returned?]. And in another narration from him he did not mention his saying 'and the commodity is present', so we took the positive for the addition and said: the mutual oath does not occur except when the commodity is present. So the omission of the condition by some narrators was due to lack of precision — like najasah and hurmah.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the principles of tarjih (preference) between conflicting reports. The author begins by stating a foundational principle: when two reports conflict, the default (asl) is to act on what confirms permissibility and purity (halal and tahara). Then the author (musannif) declares that preference is not granted based on the number of narrators, gender (male/female), or status (free/slave). The reason is that the only criterion in this context is 'adala (integrity and uprightness), which is unaffected by these factors. To illustrate, Sayyidah Aisha radiya Allahu 'anha was superior to most men, and Sayyidina Bilal radiya Allahu 'anhu was superior to most free persons. Moreover, a small group of upright people is better than a large group of sinful ones. The phrase 'superiority of number of narrators' in the author's words indicates that one number does not outweigh another when both reports are of the ahad category. However, if one side has a single narrator and the other has two, the report of the two outweighs the one. Some scholars argued that numerical majority always gives preference, citing Imam Muhammad's statements in the issues of water, but the Hanafi school abandoned this via istihsan. Then the passage addresses the situation where one report contains an additional wording (ziyada). If the narrator is the same, the report that includes the addition is taken, as exemplified by the hadith of tahaluf (mutual oath) from Ibn Mas'ud. In one narration, the condition 'and the commodity is present' is included; in another, it is omitted. The Hanafi position is to accept the version with the addition, making the oath procedure contingent on the commodity's presence. The omission by some narrators is attributed to weak memory.

Key Terms
تَرْجِيح (tarjih): Preferring one report over another when they conflict
عَدَالَة ('adala): Integrity and uprightness of a narrator, the basis for accepting testimony or narration
زِيَادَة (ziyada): Additional wording found in one narration but absent in another
مُثْبِت (muthbit): The narration that confirms the addition
اسْتِحْسَان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of reasoning that abandons a clear qiyas for a stronger consideration

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is taken when one narration includes an additional wording and the other does not, assuming the narrator is the same?
A) The report without the addition, as it is more cautious.
B) The report with the addition, as it is positive and preserves extra detail.
C) Both reports are rejected as they conflict.
D) Preference is given based on the number of narrators.

Key Takeaway
Tarjih is not by numbers or demographics; the only valid criterion is 'adala, and an addition from the same narrator is accepted as a confirmation.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Obligation of Following a Companion: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on taqlid of Sahaba in non-qiyas matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of taqlid of a Sahabi in non-qiyas matters, distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf using examples from the text.

Core Idea
In matters beyond qiyas, a Companion's statement is binding; reason alone is insufficient.

This lesson examines a foundational usul dispute: is it obligatory to follow a Companion's opinion when rational analogy (qiyas) cannot reach a ruling? The Hanafi school holds that such matters must be resolved by taqlid of a Sahabi, as their statements are presumed to originate from the Prophet ﷺ. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, argues that no Companion is inherently authoritative due to their disagreements. We will explore both positions, their evidence, and the practical consequences through concrete cases.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core claim: taqlid of a Sahabi is wajib in matters not accessible by qiyas. The text says 'the practice of our companions has agreed upon following (taqlid) in that which is not accepted by analogy.'
2
Present the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i holds that taqlid of a Sahabi is never binding, because the Companions disagreed among themselves, and no one Companion is more entitled to be followed than another.
3
Analyze the Hanafi evidence from the text
Two examples are given: (1) The minimum menstruation period, set at three days based on Aisha's statement, since reason cannot determine it. (2) The prohibition of 'inah (selling before receiving payment), where Aisha condemned the practice, overriding the qiyas that would allow it.
In both cases, the Hanafis argue that the Companion's statement must be from the Prophet because human intellect is incapable of reaching the ruling.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference in qiyas-accessible matters
For matters that can be resolved by qiyas, Hanafi imams differed: Abu Hanifa followed Ibn Umar's opinion requiring declaration of capital amount in salam, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad followed qiyas that pointing suffices.
This shows that the obligation of taqlid is limited to non-qiyas matters; where qiyas can operate, ijtihad is allowed.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The key difference is in rulings like the minimum menstruation period: Hanafis rule three days following Aisha; Shafi'is may follow other evidence or qiyas.
The thamarah shows how this usul dispute directly affects fiqh rulings.

فِيهِ فَلا يَكُونُ حُجَّةٌ عَلَى غَيْرِهِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يُقَلِّدُ أَحَدٌ مِنْهُمْ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ مُدْرَكًا مِنَ الْقِيَاسِ أَوْ لَا لِأَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ كَانَ يُخَالِفُ بَعْضُهُمْ بَعْضًا وَلَيْسَ الصَّحَابَةُ أَحَدُهُمْ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْآخَرِ مِنَ الْبُطْلَانِ وَقَدِ اتَّفَقَ عَمَلُ أَصْحَابِنَا بِالتَّقْلِيدِ فِيمَا لَا يُقْبَلُ بِالْقِيَاسِ يَعْنِي أَنَّ أَبَا حَنِيفَةَ رَحْمَةُ اللهِ وَصَاحِبَيْهِ كُلُّهُمْ مُتَّفِقُونَ بِتَقْلِيدِ الصَّحَابِيِّ كَمَا فِي أَقَلِّ الْحَيْضِ فَإِنَّ الْعَقْلَ قَاصِرٌ بِدَرْكِهِ فَعَلِمْنَا جَمِيعًا بِمَا قَالَتْ عَائِشَةُ أَقَلُّ الْحَيْضِ لِلْجَارِيَةِ الْبِكْرِ وَالشَّيْبَةِ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيْهَا وَأَكْثَرُهُ عَشَرَةٌ وَشَرَى مَا بَاعَ بِأَقَلَّ مِمَّا بَاعَ قَبْلَ نَقْدِ الثَّمَنِ الْأَوَّلِ فَإِنَّ الْقِيَاسَ يَقْتَضِي جَوَازَهُ وَلَكِنَّا قُلْنَا بِحُرْمَتِهِ جَمِيعًا عَمَلًا بِقَوْلِ عَائِشَةَ لِتِلْكَ الْمَرْأَةِ وَقَدْ بَاعَتْ بِسِتِّ مِائَةٍ بَعْدَ مَا شَرَتْ بِثَمَانِ مِائَةٍ مِنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَرْقَمَ بِئْسَ مَا شَرَيْتِ وَاشْتَرَيْتِ أَبْلِغِي زَيْدَ بْنَ أَرْقَمَ بِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى أَبْطَلَ حَجَّهُ وَجِهَادَهُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِنْ لَمْ يَتُبْ وَاخْتَلَفَ عَمَلُهُمْ فِي غَيْرِهِ أَنَّ عَمَلَ أَصْحَابِنَا فِي غَيْرِ مَا يُدْرَكُ بِالْقِيَاسِ فَإِنَّهُ حِينَئِذٍ بَعْضُهُمْ يَعْمَلُونَ بِالْقِيَاسِ وَبَعْضُهُمْ يَعْمَلُونَ بِقَوْلِ الصَّحَابَةِ كَمَا فِي إِعْلَامِ قَدْرِ رَأْسِ الْمَالِ فَإِنَّ أَبَا حَنِيفَةَ يَشْتَرِطُ إِعْلَامَ قَدْرِ رَأْسِ الْمَالِ فِي السَّلَمِ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُشَارًا إِلَيْهِ عَمَلًا بِقَوْلِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ وَأَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَمْ يَشْتَرِطَا عَمَلًا بِالرَّأْيِ لِأَنَّ الْإِشَارَةَ أَبْلَغُ فِي التَّعْرِيفِ مِنَ التَّسْمِيَةِ وَفِيهِ كِفَايَةٌ فَلَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى التَّسْمِيَةِ.
Thus it is not a proof for others. Al-Shafi'i said: None of them is to be followed, whether the matter is accessible by analogy or not, because the Companions used to contradict one another, and no Companion is more entitled than another to be followed in matters of nullity. And the practice of our companions (Hanafis) has agreed upon following (taqlid) in that which is not accepted by analogy, meaning that Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and his two companions are all agreed upon following the Companion, as in the minimum of menstruation, for the intellect is incapable of perceiving it. So we all knew by what Aisha said: 'The minimum of menstruation for a virgin and an old woman is three days and their nights, and its maximum is ten.' And he bought what he sold for less than what he sold before payment of the first price; analogy requires its permissibility, but we all said it is prohibited, acting upon the statement of Aisha to that woman who sold for six hundred after she had bought for eight hundred from Zayd ibn Arqam: 'What an evil purchase and sale you made! Inform Zayd ibn Arqam that Allah the Exalted has nullified his Hajj and Jihad with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, if he does not repent.' And their practice differed in other matters: our companions' practice in matters not accessible by analogy—some of them act by analogy and some act by the statement of the Companion, as in informing the amount of capital in salam. For Abu Hanifa requires informing the amount of capital in salam, even if it is pointed to, acting upon the statement of Ibn Umar. But Abu Yusuf and Muhammad did not require it, acting by opinion because pointing is more effective in identification than naming, and it is sufficient, so naming is not needed.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the obligation of taqlid (following) a Companion's statement. The text begins by stating that a Companion's statement is not binding on others per Shafi'i, who argues that Companions disagreed among themselves and none is inherently more authoritative. The Hanafis, however, have agreed upon taqlid in matters not accessible by qiyas (analogy), as reason alone cannot determine rulings. Two examples illustrate this: (1) The minimum duration of menstruation, set at three days and nights following Aisha's report, since reason cannot ascertain it. (2) The prohibition of selling an item before receiving payment for a lower price (a form of 'inah), where qiyas would allow it but the Hanafis forbid it based on Aisha's strong condemnation. In contrast, for matters accessible by qiyas, Hanafi imams differed: Abu Hanifa followed Ibn Umar's opinion requiring declaration of capital amount in salam even when the object is present, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad followed qiyas that pointing suffices. This shows that the Hanafi school prioritizes a Companion's statement in non-qiyas areas due to its likely prophetic origin, but allows ijtihad where qiyas can operate.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Following the opinion of a mujtahid or Sahabi without demanding proof.
غير مدرك بالقياس (ghayr mudrak bi al-qiyas): A matter that cannot be determined by rational analogy because reason is incapable of reaching it, such as the exact limits of menstruation days.
مدرك بالقياس (mudrak bi al-qiyas): A matter that can be resolved by qiyas, i.e., analogy based on known rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when is taqlid of a Companion required?
A) In all matters, regardless of qiyas
B) Only in matters that can be resolved by qiyas
C) In matters that cannot be accessed by qiyas
D) Never, because Companions disagreed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates taqlid of a Sahabi only in matters where qiyas cannot reach, based on the presumption that such statements originate from the Prophet ﷺ.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Conditions for Taqlid of a Companion's Saying
Explaining scenarios of following a Sahabi's statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on taqlid of a Companion's saying to the three scenarios and determine whether taqlid is wajib, permissible, or forbidden.

Core Idea
Following a Companion's saying is not always binding – it depends on whether other Companions knew, accepted, or opposed it.

This passage clarifies the nuanced Hanafi position on following the statements of the Companions. While their proximity to revelation gives their views weight, the madhhab recognizes that not every Companion's statement is automatically binding. The text outlines three distinct scenarios that determine whether taqlid is obligatory, optional, or subject to internal scholarly disagreement. Understanding these scenarios is crucial for a jurist determining the authority of a qawl al-sahabi in istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Scan the text for the three possibilities regarding a Companion's saying: (a) it does not reach another Companion, (b) it reaches and is met with silence, (c) it reaches and is opposed.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For (b), silence indicates consensus; taqlid is wajib. For (c), valid ikhtilaf; muqallid may choose. For (a), internal ikhtilaf exists among Hanafis.
3
Understand the concept of ijma' murakkab
When Companions hold only two opinions, adopting a third is forbidden. This is composite consensus.
4
Apply the rule to a new case
Given a Companion's saying and the reaction of others, classify the type and state the ruling for a muqallid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں جن سے احتراز کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے جیسے عام آگ کا لگ جانا وغیرہ تو ایسی صورت میں اجیر مشترک بھی بالا تفاقی ضامن نہ ہو گا۔ یہ مذکورہ اختلاف جو صحابی کے قول کی تقلید عدم تقلید کے بارے میں فقہاء میں اختلاف پایا جارہا ہے۔ فِي كُلِّ مَا ثَبَتَ عَنْهُمْ مِنْ غَيْرِ خَلاف صرف اس صورت میں ہے کہ جبکہ کوئی حکم کسی صحابی سے ثابت اور اس کے متعلق دوسرے صحابہ کا اختلاف منقول نہ ہو یادہ حکم معلوم ہونے کے بعد دوسرے صحابہ کے بطور تسلیم کے سکوت اختیار کرنے سے ثابت نہ ہو یعنی ایک صحابی نے کوئی بات فرمائی مگر یہ بات ے کسی صحابی تک نہیں پہنچی تو ہمارے علاوہ میں باہم اختلاف ہے کہ اس کی تقلید کی جائے گی یا نہیں بعض علماء اس صحافی کے قول کی تقلید کے قائل ہیں اور بعض قائل نہیں ہیں اور بہر حال اس صحابی کا قول جب دوسرے صحابی سیک پہنچا تو یہ دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا دوسرے صحابی نے اس قول کو سن کر تسلیم کرتے ہوئے سکوت فرمایا اس کی مخالفت فرمادی۔ اگر سکوت فرمایا تو یہ اجتماع ہو گیا۔ لہذا اجماع کی تقلید واجب ہو گی اور اگر سن کر دوسرے صحابی نے اس کے خلاف قول کیا تو یہ دو مجتہدوں کے اختلاف کے درجہ میں شمار ہوگالہذ ا مقلد کے لئے جائز ہے کہ دونوں میں سے جس کی چاہے اقتداء کرے اور اس کی تیسری شق (صورت کی طرف تعدی) اختیار کرنا جائز نہیں یعنی مقلد کے لئے یہ جائز نہیں کہ دونوں اقوال کو چھوڑ کر تیسر امسلک خود نکال لے۔ کیونکہ دور ایوں میں صحابہ کا اختلاف محدود ہو تو اجماع مرکب کہلاتا ہے جس کا حکم یہی ہے کہ ان دونوں اقوال کو چھوڑ کر کوئی تیسر امسلک اختیار کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اس مقام پر بس اس قدر سمجھ لینا کافی ہے۔
That which it is not possible to avoid, such as a general fire breaking out, then in such a case the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) is also not liable by agreement. This mentioned difference regarding the taqlid or non-taqlid of a Companion's saying is found among jurists. It is only concerning every ruling established from them without disagreement; that is, when a ruling is established from a Companion and no disagreement from other Companions is narrated, or after the ruling becomes known, other Companions do not object by way of acceptance, i.e., a Companion said something but that statement did not reach another Companion, then there is difference among us (Hanafis) whether taqlid of it is made or not. Some scholars are of the view of taqlid of that Companion's saying, and some are not. In any case, when that Companion's saying reaches another Companion, it is either that the other Companion heard the statement and remained silent in acceptance, or he opposed it. If he remained silent, then that becomes consensus, so taqlid of the consensus is obligatory. And if upon hearing, another Companion opposed it, then this is counted as a difference between two mujtahids. Hence, it is permissible for a muqallid to follow whichever of the two he wishes. And adopting a third possibility (going beyond the two) is not permissible; i.e., it is not permissible for a muqallid to abandon both opinions and derive a third path himself, because when the difference of the Companions is limited, it is called 'composite consensus' (ijma' murakkab), whose ruling is that it is not permissible to leave both opinions and adopt a third. At this point, understanding this much is sufficient.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the conditions under which a Companion's saying (qawl al-sahabi) may be followed. The author explains that the ruling applies only when there is no known disagreement from other Companions. Three scenarios are outlined: (1) The Companion's statement does not reach any other Companion – there is ikhtilaf among scholars whether taqlid is allowed. (2) It reaches another Companion who remains silent – this indicates acceptance and forms consensus (ijma), making taqlid wajib. (3) It reaches another Companion who openly opposes it – this becomes a valid difference between two mujtahids, and a muqallid may choose either opinion. A third view not expressed by any Companion is forbidden because it would violate the principle of 'composite consensus' (ijma' murakkab). Note: The first sentence about a hireling is likely a continuation from a previous discussion and is not directly part of this ruling.

Key Terms
قول الصحابي (qawl al-sahabi): A legal opinion or statement attributed to a Companion of the Prophet.
تقلید (taqlid): Following the ruling of a mujtahid without evidence.
اجماع مرکب (ijma' murakkab): Composite consensus: when scholars agree on two conflicting opinions, no third is allowed.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of mujtahids, considered binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when another Companion remains silent after hearing a Companion's statement?
A) It becomes ijma and taqlid is wajib
B) It is a valid ikhtilaf and muqallid may choose
C) Taqlid is not allowed
D) It is not binding

Key Takeaway
A Companion's saying may be followed only in specific contexts; silence of others creates binding ijma, opposition creates choice, and ignorance creates scholarly disagreement.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
