Child's Will and Choice Between Parents: Hanafi Usul Analysis
Ruling on child's will invalid and dispute on child's choice between parents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a child's will and explain why the Hanafi school rejects the child's right to choose between parents, using the principle of specificity (khushusiyyah) of the Prophet's action.

Core Idea
A child's will is invalid; the child has no choice between parents—the Prophet's precedent was specific, not general.

This passage addresses two aspects of a child's legal capacity: testamentary disposition and custody choice. The Hanafi school holds that a child's will is absolutely invalid because it constitutes pure harm. It then examines the dispute regarding a child's right to choose between separated parents, contrasting the Shafi'i position based on a hadith with the Hanafi response that the hadith was specific and not generalizable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal capacity issues
Recognize that the passage addresses two distinct rulings for a child: validity of a will and the right to choose between parents after separation.
These are based on the child's lack of full legal capacity (ahliyyat).
2
Understand the Hanafi dalil for invalidating the will
The child's will is pure harm (darar mahd) because it removes ownership; thus it is invalid regardless of beneficiary or timing of death.
No dispute is mentioned on this point in the text.
3
Recognize the Shafi'i proof for child's choice
Imam al-Shafi'i cites a hadith where the Prophet gave a child choice between parents in a similar situation, arguing it establishes a general principle.
The hadith is referenced but not quoted verbatim.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis argue the Prophet's action was specific (khass) due to a supplication (du'a) and cannot be generalized by qiyas.
This is a core usul principle: a specific incident does not create a general rule.
5
Apply the usul principle of specificity
Explain that without generalizable evidence, the child has no choice; custody is determined by gender: son with father, daughter with mother.
The thamarah al-khilaf is different custody outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نزدیک بچہ کی وصیت بالکل باطل ہے کیونکہ وصیت ضرر محض ہے اور ملک کا تیر کا ازالہ کر دیتا ہے اور برابر ہے کہ بھلائی کے لئے وصیت کرے یا غیر بھلائی کے لئے کرے اور برابر ہے کہ بلوغ سے پہلے موت واقع ہو جائے یا بلوغ کے بعد انتقال ہو و اختیار احد الابوین اور ماں باپ میں سے کسی ایک کو اختیار کرنا اس صورت میں ہے کہ جبکہ ماں باپ کے درمیان جدائی واقع ہو جائے اور ماں حق مضانت کو پورے کر چکی ہو تو امام شافعی نے نزدیک بچہ کو اختیار حاصل ہے کہ دونوں میں سے جس کو چاہیے اختیار کرنے کیونکہ ایسے ہی صورت حال میں جناب بنی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے بچہ کو اختیار دیا تھا کہ دونوں میں سے جس کو چاہیے اختیار کرلے وهذه المنفعة الخ یہ منفعت ایسی ہے کہ دل کے تصرف کرنے سے اس کا حاصل ہونا ممکن نہیں ۔ ہے لہذا بچہ کا تصرف اس میں معتبر ہوگا وعندنا ليس كذالك اور ہمارے نزدیک ایسا نہیں ہے (یعنی بچہ کو اس کا اختیار نہیں ہے بلکہ بیٹا اپنے باپ کے پاس قیام کرے گا تا کہ آداب شریعت سے روشناس ہو جائے اور لڑکی ماں کے پاس ٹھہرے گی تاکہ عورتوں سے مخصوص مسائل معلوم کر سکے ( مثلا حیض و نفاس کے) وَتُخْبرُ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ اور جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا اختیار دینا بچہ کے لئے اس اصول کے پیش نظر نہ تھا کہ اس کے حق میں زیادہ نفع ہے بلکہ اس میں آپ کی دعا شامل تھی جو اس بچہ کے حق میں اختیار سے زیادہ باعث برکت و نفع تھی اس لئے حضور کے اس تعامل پر قیاس نہیں کرنا چاہیے۔
In our view, the will of a child is completely invalid because a will is pure harm and it removes the disposition of ownership. It is equal whether he makes a will for good or for other than good, and equal whether death occurs before puberty or after. And the choice of one of the parents: that the child choose one of the mother or father occurs in the case when separation occurs between the parents and the mother has fulfilled the right of breastfeeding. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the child has the right to choose whichever of the two he wishes, because in a similar situation the Prophet ﷺ gave a child a choice that he may choose whichever he wishes. 'And this benefit...' This benefit is such that it cannot be obtained by the disposition of the mind. Therefore the child's disposition in this is considered valid. In our view it is not like that, meaning the child does not have this choice. Rather, the son will stay with his father so that he becomes acquainted with the etiquettes of the Shari'ah, and the daughter will stay with her mother so that she can learn matters specific to women (like menstruation and postpartum). And the Prophet's giving a choice was not based on the principle that it is more beneficial for the child, but rather it included his supplication which was more blessed and beneficial for that child than the choice. Therefore one should not make an analogy (qiyas) on his action.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that a child's will is absolutely invalid because it constitutes pure harm (darar mahd) by removing ownership. The ruling applies equally whether the will is for good or not, and whether the child dies before or after puberty. The passage then addresses the issue of khiyar al-abawayn (choice between parents upon separation). Imam Shafi'i holds that the child may choose which parent to live with, based on a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ gave a child such a choice. The benefit of this choice is considered a pure benefit that can be realized by the child's own will, so the child's choice is valid. However, the Hanafis disagree, saying the child does not have this right of choice. Instead, they rule that the son stays with the father to learn the etiquettes of the Shari'ah, and the daughter stays with the mother to learn feminine matters. They argue that the Prophet's action in that specific case was due to a special supplication (du'a) and not a general principle, so it cannot be extended by qiyas.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyat): A testamentary disposition by a child which is invalid in Hanafi law due to harm.
اختیار احد الابوین (ikhtiyar ahad al-abawayn): The child's right to choose between mother and father after separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, where does a son stay after his parents' separation?
A) With his mother
B) With his father
C) He may choose
D) With both equally

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's action in a specific case does not establish a general rule; usul principles require distinguishing between general and specific.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
The Nature of I'taq: Definition Dispute and Its Legal Consequences
Definition dispute and its furu' consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi definition of i'taq as izalat al-milk to resolve issues of partial emancipation and explain the Sahibayn's opposing position with its logical arguments.

Core Idea
I'taq is either removal of ownership (Abu Hanifa) or establishment of freedom (Sahibayn) — and that definition determines whether it can be partial.

This passage delves into a core usul dispute within the Hanafi school itself: is the act of emancipation (i'taq) divisible? The answer hinges on how we define i'taq — as the removal of the master's ownership or as the creation of freedom in the slave. The passage also explores the practical consequences for a slave's capacity to own a concubine, perform Hajj, marry, and pay blood-money, demonstrating how a tahlili (definitional) dispute can produce different furu' outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of i'taq
Locate the definitions attributed to Abu Hanifa (izalat al-milk) and the Sahibayn (itbat al-'itq). Understand each as a tahlil (definitional analysis) of the act.
The Sahibayn's definition is presented first in the text.
2
Follow the logical argument from each definition regarding divisibility
Trace why each definition leads to a different conclusion about tajazzi (partiality). Abu Hanifa: ownership is divisible, so its removal is divisible. Sahibayn: freedom is indivisible, so its establishment cannot be partial.
Pay attention to the three logical absurdities the Sahibayn cite.
3
Analyze the supporting analogy of purchasing a relative
Examine how Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to argue that i'taq can be indirect: just as buying a relative causes emancipation through removal of ownership, partial emancipation can cause partial freedom.
This is a key dalil aqli.
4
Apply the definition to the slave's legal capacity
From the definitional dispute, the passage derives specific rulings: a slave cannot own a concubine, his Hajj counts as nafl, he can marry with master's consent, and he can pay blood-money.
Note that both definitions lead to the same outcomes on these issues, showing that the dispute is primarily about the nature of i'taq itself.
5
Appreciate how usul definitions produce different furu'
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: in partial emancipation, the definition determines whether half or the entire slave is freed. Recognize that the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
This is a classic example of a tahlili dispute affecting fiqh rulings.

So that what you said may be correct. That is because the emancipator only acts in what is his pure right, and his right is ownership that is divisible, not slavery or the right of Allah. But by removing ownership, slavery is removed, and by its removal, freedom is established subsequently through an intermediary, like the purchase of a near relative: it becomes emancipation through the intermediary of ownership. Slavery contradicts ownership of property due to the existence of being owned in it while it is property, so they cannot combine because ownership is capacity and being owned is incapacity. It was said there is a discussion: it is not possible for them to combine in it from two different aspects. Being owned occurs in it from the aspect of property, and ownership from the aspect of humanity. So the slave and the mukatab cannot own a concubine, i.e., taking a female slave for sexual intercourse, even if the master permits them both. The mukatab is specifically mentioned even though the mudabbar is also the same because he became more entitled to his earnings, so that might suggest permissibility of concubinage, so he removed the doubt by mentioning it like freedom which is its opposite. Similarly, according to them, the ruling of i'taq is also not divisible in the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because i'taq means establishing freedom; thus freedom is the effect of i'taq. So if i'taq were divisible and the master freed part of the slave, then either freedom is established in the whole slave, leading to an effect without a cause, or freedom is not established in any part, leading to a cause without effect, or it is established in one part and not in another, requiring divisibility of the right. The author expressed this meaning in his statement: 'lest there be an effect without a cause, or a cause without an effect, or divisibility of the right.' Abu Hanifa said that it is removal of ownership, and ownership accepts divisibility, so removal of ownership necessarily also accepts divisibility. Slavery contradicts ownership of property because the attribute of being owned exists in it; therefore they cannot combine. Some said there is an objection: why can these two attributes not exist in the slave from two different aspects? Being owned is from the perspective of property, and being an owner is from the perspective of humanity, so there is no contradiction. So the slave and mukatab cannot own a concubine, i.e., taking a female slave for intercourse, even if the master permits them. The mukatab is specifically mentioned because he becomes more entitled to his earnings, suggesting permissibility, so the doubt is removed. Hajj is not valid from them; even if they perform it, it counts as supererogatory, even with the master's permission, because their benefits except prayer and fasting remain for the master, and they do not have the ability to perform it. Unlike a poor person who performs Hajj then becomes rich: his performance counts for the obligation because ownership of wealth is not a condition per se but a condition for ability to perform. It does not contradict ownership of other than wealth like marriage and blood-money. Indeed, he is capable of marriage because fulfilling sexual desire is a need, and he has no way to concubinage, so marriage is determined. But it is contingent upon the master's consent because the dower is attached to his neck, causing harm to the master. Similarly, he is capable of blood-money because he needs survival, and there is no survival without it. Therefore the master does not have...

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the nature of i'taq (emancipation) and its implications for a slave's legal capacity. The text begins by presenting the view that i'taq is the establishment of freedom (itbat al-itq), which cannot be partial because it is a single indivisible right of Allah. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that if i'taq were divisible, logical absurdities would follow: either the effect (freedom) exists without a cause, or the cause exists without effect, or the right is divided. The author then presents Abu Hanifa's view that i'taq is the removal of ownership (izalat al-milk), and since ownership is divisible, i'taq can be partial. Abu Hanifa supports this by analogy: removing ownership causes the removal of slavery unintentionally, and freedom follows indirectly, just as purchasing a relative leads to emancipation indirectly. The text then addresses an objection: how can a slave be both owned and an owner? It explains that these attributes come from different perspectives: being owned is from the aspect of property, while being an owner is from the aspect of humanity. Thus a slave cannot own a concubine because that would require him to be an owner of property while being himself property, which is contradictory. The rule extends to a mukatab (slave on contract of manumission) because he has partial ownership of his earnings, which might imply permission to own a concubine, but the text clarifies he cannot. The discussion then moves to the validity of Hajj for a slave: it is not valid as an obligatory Hajj even with the master's permission, because the slave's benefits (except prayer and fasting) belong to the master, so he lacks independent ability. If a poor person performs Hajj and later becomes rich, it counts for the obligation because ability at the time of performance suffices. Finally, the text explains that a slave can marry because it is a necessity for fulfilling sexual desire, but he cannot take a concubine. However, marriage requires the master's consent because the dower becomes a debt on the slave, potentially harming the master. The slave is also considered capable of paying blood-money (diya) because it is essential for survival. This passage highlights the Hanafi method of resolving apparent conflicts between legal principles and practical needs, often using istihsan and consideration of different aspects (jihaat).

Key Terms
الإعتاق (al-i'taq): The act of freeing a slave; according to Abu Hanifa, it is removal of ownership; according to the Sahibayn, it is establishment of freedom.
التجزي (al-tajazzi): The property of being divisible into parts; used for ownership and acts.
التسرى (al-tasari): Taking a concubine (female slave for sexual intercourse).
الحجة (al-hijja): The obligatory Hajj (Hajj al-Islam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), why can i'taq not be partial?
A) Because ownership is indivisible
B) Because i'taq is the establishment of freedom, which is an indivisible right of Allah
C) Because the slave's body is indivisible
D) Because the master's intention must be complete

Key Takeaway
The definition of i'taq as removal of ownership (izalat al-milk) allows partial emancipation, while the definition as establishment of freedom (itbat al-'itq) does not.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Equality in Qisas: Free and Slave
Ruling on qisas between free and slave with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that a free person may be killed in qisas for a slave, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on honor.

Core Idea
Qisas is based on equality in life, not honor; a free person may be killed for a slave.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that a free person can be executed in retribution (qisas) for killing a slave. The passage argues that qisas is grounded in the Quranic principle 'a life for a life' (al-Ma'idah 5:45), which applies equally to free and slave. The Shafi'i objection based on the slave's lack of human honor (karamah) is rejected because honor is irrelevant to qisas; the equality in life suffices, just as qisas applies between male and female despite differences in blood money.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on qisas between free and slave
Find in the passage the statement that a free person is killed for a slave (yuqtal al-hurr bi al-‘abd qisas-an). Note the proof cited: 'al-nafs bi al-nafs' (a life for a life) from the Quran.
The Hanafi position is that equality in life, not honor, is the basis for qisas.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i objection
Read the phrase 'wa ‘inda al-Shafi‘i la yuqtal al-hurr bi al-‘abd li-‘adam ahliyyat al-karamat al-insaniyyah' – the Shafi‘i school denies qisas because a slave lacks human honor capacity. Understand that this objection introduces a different criterion (honor) for equality.
The Shafi'i argument focuses on karamah (honor) as a prerequisite for qisas.
3
Examine the Hanafi response and analogy
The author responds by comparing free-slave qisas to male-female qisas: just as a man is killed for a woman despite her blood money being less, so a free person is killed for a slave despite the slave's lower status. This shows that karamah is not a condition.
The analogy to gender differences strengthens the Hanafi argument.
4
Identify the dalil and its epistemological weight
The primary dalil is the Quranic text (al-Ma'idah 5:45) which is qat‘i al-thubut and qat‘i al-dalalah in its general command. The Hanafi school treats this as a definitive proof.
The authority of the proof is high; no ikhtilaf on the text itself, only on its application.

وَالْكَرَامَات الآخِرُ صَفَةٌ زَائِدَةً فِي الْحُرُ لاَ يَتَعَلى بِهَا الْقَصَاصُ كَمَا يَجْرِى ذَالِكَ فِيْمَا بَيْنَ الذَّكَرِ وَالأُنْثَى وَإِنْ كَانَ يَنتَقِص بَدْلُ دَمِهَا عَنْ بَدْلِ دَم الذِّكَرِ وَعِنْدَ الشافعي لايُقْتَلُ الْحُرُ بِالْعَبْدِ لِعَدَم أَهْلِيَةِ الْكَرَامَاتِ الإِنْسانِيَةِ فَامْتَنَتَعْ الْقِصَاصِ لِعَدَمِ الْمُسَمَاوَاةِ وَصَحُ أَمَانُ الْمَادُونِ بِالْقِتَالِ لَا الْمَادُونِ فِي التَّجَارَةِ للكفار لانه كما إذنَهُ لِمَوْلَى بِالْقِتَالِ صَارَ شَرِيْكًا فِي الْغَنِيْمَةِ فَالآمَانُ تَصْرِفْ فِي حَقٌّ نَفْسِهِ قَصَدًا ثُمَّ يَكُوْنَ فِى حَقٌّ غَيْرِهِ ضِمْنًا وَإِنَّمَا قَيْدَ بِالْمَادُوْنِ لَأَنَّ فِي أمَانِ الْمَحْجُورِ خِلاَفًا فَعِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لايصح لأنَّهُ لَأَحَقُّ لَهُ فِي الْجِهَادِ حَتَّى يَكُونَ مُسْتَقِطًا حَقٌّ نَفْسِهِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَالسَّافَعِى يَصحُ أَمَانَهُ لأَنَّهُ مُسْلِمٌ مِنْ أَهْلِ نَصْرَةِ الدِّينِ وَلَعَلَّهُ فِيهِ يَكُونُ مَصْلَحَةٌ لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ وَاقْرَارُهُ بِالْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ أَنْ صَبَحْ اِقْرَارُ الْعَبْدِ الْمَادُونِ بِمَا يُوجِبُ الْحُدُوْدَ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَأَنْ كَانَ يَسْتَرِكَ فِيْهِ الْمَحْجُورُ أَيْضًا لَأَنْ إِقْرَارَهُ يَصِيرُ مُلاً قيا حق نَفْسِهِ الَّذِي هُوَ الدَّمُ وَإِنْ كَانَ الإِتْلافُ مَالِيَةُ الْمَوْلَى بَطْرِيْقِ الضَّمْنِ وَالْعَبْدُ فِيهِ : - اور غلام اس بارے میں یعنی دونوں قسم کی عصمت کے حاصل ہونے میں کالعد ترجمه تشریحی آزاد کے مانند ہے بہر حال ایمان کے معاملے میں غلام کا آزاد کے مانند ہونا بالکل ظاہر ہی ہے باتی دار الاسلام میں غلام کا دار الاسلام کی حفاظت میں ہونا تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ غلام اپنے آقا کے تابع ہے جب اس کا آقادار الاسلام میں محفوظ ہے تو اس کا غلام بھی محفوظ ہو گا یا اس وجہ سے کہ آقا چونکہ مسلمان ہے اس نئے اسلام کی وجہ سے اور اگر غیر مسلم ہے تو ذمہ کی وجہ سے محفوظ ہے وانما يؤثر في قيمته - البته مقدار قیمت میں رقیت کا اثر ظاہر ہوگا یعنی رقیتہ کا اثر اس کی قیمت کے نقصان کی صورت میں ظاہر ہو گا حتی کہ اگر کسی وجہ سے اسکی قیمت دس ہزار دراہم کی مقدار کو پہونچ جائے تو اس کی قیمت میں سے دس درہم کم کر لئے جائیں گے تاکہ آزاد کی قیمت سے اسکی قیمت تھوڑی کم رہے والہذا اور اسی وجہت کہ عصمت کے بارے میں غلام آزاد کے مشابہ ہے يقتل الحر بالعبد قصاصا غلام کے بدلے آزاد کو قصاص میں مقتل کیا جائے گا ہمارے نزدیک اس وجہ سے کہ قصاص کی بنیاد جس اصل (دلیل) پر ہے ینی ( النفس با نفس ) اس میں آزاد اور غلام میں مساوات پائی جاتی ہے۔ والكرامات الآخر الخ باقی دوسرے کرامات و اعزازات جو آزاد میں پائے جاتے وہ اس کی ایک زائد فضیات ہے اس سے قصاص کا کوئی تعلق نہیں ہے جس طرح قصاص مردو عورت کے درمیان جاری ہوتی ہے اگر چہ حلقت و مرتبہ کے لحاظ سے عورت کا خون مرد کے مقابلے میں ناقص اور کم درجہ کا ہوتا ہے وعند الشافعي لا يقتل الحر اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک غلام کے بدلے قصاص میں آزاد کو قتل نہ کیا جائے گا کیونکہ غلام میں انسانی شرافت و کرامت کی اہمیت نہیں پائی جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں میں مساوات کے موجود نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے قاص ممنوع ہے وصیح امان المازون اور اجازت یافتہ غلام کا امن دینا معتبر ہے اس جملے کا خطف مصنف کے سابقہ قول بقتل " پر ہے یعنی چونکہ غلام عصمت و حفاظت کے بارے میں حر کے مشابہ ہے ماذون بالقتال کا امان دینا صحیح ہے ماذون بالقتال وہ غلام ہے جس کو آقاء نے کفار سے جہاد کرنے کی اجازت دیدی ہے۔ ماذون المتجازه اجازت سے مراد وہ غلام نہیں ہے جس کو آجانے تجارت کرنے کی اجازت دے رکھی ہے لانه لما اذنه المولى للقتال الخبازون بالقتال سے امان دینے کی صحت کی وجہ یہ کہ جب آقا نے غلام کو کفار سے جہاد میں شرکت کی اجازت دیدی ہے تو مال غنیمت میں شریک ہوگا پس اپنے نفس کے حق میں امان دینا تو مولی کی طرف سے قصدا ہے پھر اس کے ضمن میں اس کی اجازت بھی شمار ہو جائے گی جو غلام غیر کے حق میں امان کا استعمال کرتا ہے مصنف نے متن میں عید کے ساتھ مازون کی قید اس نے بڑ ھالیا ہے کہ کیونکہ عبد مجور سے امان دینے کی صورت میں اختلاف ہے پس امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک سیع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کو جہاد میں شرکت کا حق نہیں ہے تاکہ اس کے بارے میں کہا جاسکے کہ یہ اپنے نفس کے حق کے ساقط کرنے والا ہے اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک عہد مہجور کا امان دینا صحیح ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی دین اسلام کی مدد کرنے کا بحیثیت مسلمان اہل ہے ممکن ہے کہ اس میں بھی مسلمانوں کے لئے کوئی۔ مصلحت دیکھا ہو۔ وَإقْرَارة بالحدود والقصاص اور صحیح ہے اس کا اقرار کرنا حدود و قصاص کے متعلق یعنی عبد مازون کا ایسی چیز کا اقرار کر لینا درست ہے جو حدود قصاص کو واجب کرتا ہو اگر چہ اس میں عبد مهجور بھی اس کے اگرچہ ساتھ شریک ہے کیونکہ اس کا اقرار کرنا اس کے حق سے مل جائیگا جو اس کے نفس کے حق میں اس کو حاصل ہے یعنی دم اگر چہ ضمنا اس اقرا کے صحیح جاننے میں مولی کے مالی حق کا اختلاف ہلاک کرنا لازم آتا ہے (مگر چونکہ یہ ضمنا ہے اس لئے اس کا اختیار نہیں کیا گیا۔ وبالسرَقَةِ الْمُسْتَهْلَكَةِ أوَ الْقَائِمَةِ فَيَجِبُ القَطْعُ في المُسْتَهْلُكَةِ وَلَأَصْحَانُ عَلَيْهِ لأنَّهُ لا يَجْتَمِعُ مَعَ الْقَطْعِ وَيُرَدُّ الْمَالُ فِي الْقَائِمَةِ إِلى المَسرُوقِ مِنْهُ وَيَقْعُ وَهَذَا كلة فِي الْمَادُون وَفِي الْمَجُ اخْتِلافُ أَي إِنْ أَقَرَّ الْعَبْدُ الْمَحْجُورُ بالسرقة فَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَالُ مَالِكًا قُطِعَ وَلَأَصْحَانَ وَإِنْ كَانَ قَائِمًا فَإِنْ صَدقَة الْمَوْلَى قُطِعَ وَيُرَدُّ إِنْ كَذَّبَهُ الْمَوْلى فَفِيهِ اخْتِلافُ فَعِنْدَ أبي حَنِيفَةً يُقْطَعُ وَيُرَدُّ وَعِندَ أَبِي يُؤسف وَيُقْطَعُ وَلا يُرَدُ وَلكِنْ يَضْمِنُ مِثْلَهُ بَعْدَ الإِعْتَاقِ وَعِنْدَ مُحمدٍ لا يُخْلُعُ وَلا وَلاَيُرَدُّ
And the remaining honors are an additional quality in the free person, qisas is not based upon it as occurs between male and female, even though the blood-money of the female is less than that of the male. According to al-Shafi'i, a free person is not killed for a slave due to the lack of human honor capacity, so qisas is prevented due to lack of equality. And the aman of the authorized (ma'dhun) slave for fighting is valid, not the authorized for trade with the disbelievers, because when the master permitted him for fighting, he becomes a partner in spoils, so the aman is a disposal in his own right directly, then it becomes for others indirectly. He restricted it to the authorized because there is a dispute regarding the aman of the interdicted (mahjur) slave: according to Abu Hanifa it is not valid because he has no right in jihad to be able to drop his own right; according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i his aman is valid because he is a Muslim from the people of aiding the religion, and perhaps there is a benefit for the Muslims in it. And his iqrar (confession) regarding hudud and qisas: the iqrar of the ma'dhun slave for that which necessitates hudud and qisas is valid, even if the mahjur slave also shares in it, because his iqrar becomes binding on his own right which is the blood, even though the destruction of the master's property occurs indirectly. And the slave in this... And regarding theft of consumed or existing property: cutting is obligatory for consumed property, but [the hand] is not returned to him because it does not combine with cutting, and the property is returned to the victim in the case of existing property. All this applies to the ma'dhun slave. For the mahjur, there is a dispute: if he confesses to theft, if the property is destroyed, he is cut and not impaired? If it exists, if the master confirms him, he is cut and the property is returned; if the master denies him, there is a dispute: according to Abu Hanifa, he is cut and the property is returned; according to Abu Yusuf, he is cut and not returned, but he must guarantee its like after emancipation; according to Muhammad, he is not cut nor is the property returned.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal capacity of slaves in three areas: qisas, aman, and iqrar. The author first establishes that the slave is like a free person in terms of inviolability ('isma) for qisas, though not in honor (karamat). The proof is the Quranic principle 'a life for a life' (al-Ma'idah 5:45) which includes both free and slave. The Shafi'i objection based on lack of human honor is rejected because qisas is based on equality in life, not honor. Then the author addresses aman (granting safe conduct) by slaves. A ma'dhun slave (authorized for fighting) can give aman because he shares in spoils and thus has authority over his own right. But a mahjur slave (interdicted, not authorized) cannot give aman according to Abu Hanifa because he has no right in jihad; Muhammad and al-Shafi'i allow it for potential benefit to Muslims. Finally, iqrar (confession): a ma'dhun slave's confession for crimes entailing hudud (fixed punishments) or qisas is valid even if it affects the master's property indirectly, because the confession pertains to his own life. For theft by a ma'dhun, the rule is that if the stolen property is consumed, the hand is cut; if still existing, the hand is cut and the property returned. For a mahjur slave confessing theft, there is disagreement among the Hanafi masters: Abu Hanifa cuts the hand and returns the property; Abu Yusuf cuts but does not return, instead the slave guarantees after emancipation; Muhammad does not cut nor return. The passage concludes by highlighting the ikhtilaf (disagreement) in the case of mahjur.

Key Terms
قِصَاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind, specifically execution of the killer for intentional homicide.
كَرَامَة (karamah): Human honor or dignity; Shafi'i considers this a prerequisite for qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school permit qisas between free and slave despite the slave's lower blood money?
A) Because the master's consent is sufficient.
B) Because qisas is based on equality in life, not honor or money.
C) Because the slave is equal to a free person in all respects.
D) Because the Quran explicitly says 'a free for a free'.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qisas between free and slave is valid because the Quranic text 'a life for a life' is general and applies to all human lives.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
Aman and Iqrar of Slaves: Capacity and Ikhtilaf
Rulings on aman and iqrar of ma'dhun and mahjur slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the aman and iqrar of a ma'dhun (authorized) slave and a mahjur (interdicted) slave, and identify the ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams.

Core Idea
A slave's legal capacity in aman and iqrar depends on master's authorization; the mahjur slave's acts are disputed among the Hanafi masters.

This lesson explores the rules for slaves granting safe conduct (aman) and making confessions (iqrar). The passage distinguishes between a ma'dhun slave authorized for fighting (whose aman is valid) and one authorized for trade (invalid for aman). For the mahjur (interdicted) slave, there is a three-way ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa invalidates his aman, while Muhammad and al-Shafi'i allow it for potential benefit. Similarly, in iqrar for hudud and qisas, the ma'dhun's confession is valid; for theft by a mahjur, Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad disagree on cutting the hand and returning the property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of slaves: ma'dhun and mahjur
Find definitions: ma'dhun is a slave authorized by the master for a specific purpose (fighting or trade); mahjur is interdicted from legal actions. The passage discusses rules for each.
The distinction is key to understanding the rulings.
2
Analyze the ruling on aman (safe conduct) for ma'dhun and mahjur
The passage states that the aman of a ma'dhun slave for fighting is valid because he shares in spoils; the aman of a ma'dhun for trade is not. For the mahjur, Abu Hanifa says invalid; Muhammad and al-Shafi'i say valid.
Note the difference: authorization for fighting grants rights in jihad; authorization for trade does not.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf on mahjur's aman
Abu Hanifa's reason: the mahjur has no right in jihad to drop his own right. Muhammad and al-Shafi'i: he is a Muslim and may bring benefit. This is a usul dispute over whether capacity can be inferred from general Islamic identity.
This is a classic ikhtilaf in usul al-fiqh: generality of capacity vs. specific authorization.
4
Apply the same analysis to iqrar (confession)
The ma'dhun slave's iqrar for hudud and qisas is valid because it pertains to his own life. For theft, there are detailed rules: if consumed, hand cut; if existing, hand cut and property returned. For the mahjur's iqrar of theft, the imams have differing rulings: Abu Hanifa cuts and returns; Abu Yusuf cuts but does not return (guarantee after freedom); Muhammad does not cut nor return.
The ikhtilaf revolves around whether the mahjur's confession is binding when it affects the master's property.

اِقْرَارُ الْعَبْدِ الْمَادُونِ بِمَا يُوجِبُ الْحُدُوْدَ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَأَنْ كَانَ يَسْتَرِكَ فِيْهِ الْمَحْجُورُ أَيْضًا لَأَنْ إِقْرَارَهُ يَصِيرُ مُلاً قيا حق نَفْسِهِ الَّذِي هُوَ الدَّمُ وَإِنْ كَانَ الإِتْلافُ مَالِيَةُ الْمَوْلَى بَطْرِيْقِ الضَّمْنِ وَالْعَبْدُ فِيهِ : - اور غلام اس بارے میں یعنی دونوں قسم کی عصمت کے حاصل ہونے میں کالعد ترجمه تشریحی آزاد کے مانند ہے بہر حال ایمان کے معاملے میں غلام کا آزاد کے مانند ہونا بالکل ظاہر ہی ہے باتی دار الاسلام میں غلام کا دار الاسلام کی حفاظت میں ہونا تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ غلام اپنے آقا کے تابع ہے جب اس کا آقادار الاسلام میں محفوظ ہے تو اس کا غلام بھی محفوظ ہو گا یا اس وجہ سے کہ آقا چونکہ مسلمان ہے اس نئے اسلام کی وجہ سے اور اگر غیر مسلم ہے تو ذمہ کی وجہ سے محفوظ ہے وانما يؤثر في قيمته - البته مقدار قیمت میں رقیت کا اثر ظاہر ہوگا یعنی رقیتہ کا اثر اس کی قیمت کے نقصان کی صورت میں ظاہر ہو گا حتی کہ اگر کسی وجہ سے اسکی قیمت دس ہزار دراہم کی مقدار کو پہونچ جائے تو اس کی قیمت میں سے دس درہم کم کر لئے جائیں گے تاکہ آزاد کی قیمت سے اسکی قیمت تھوڑی کم رہے والہذا اور اسی وجہت کہ عصمت کے بارے میں غلام آزاد کے مشابہ ہے يقتل الحر بالعبد قصاصا غلام کے بدلے آزاد کو قصاص میں مقتل کیا جائے گا ہمارے نزدیک اس وجہ سے کہ قصاص کی بنیاد جس اصل (دلیل) پر ہے ینی ( النفس با نفس ) اس میں آزاد اور غلام میں مساوات پائی جاتی ہے۔ والكرامات الآخر الخ باقی دوسرے کرامات و اعزازات جو آزاد میں پائے جاتے وہ اس کی ایک زائد فضیات ہے اس سے قصاص کا کوئی تعلق نہیں ہے جس طرح قصاص مردو عورت کے درمیان جاری ہوتی ہے اگر چہ حلقت و مرتبہ کے لحاظ سے عورت کا خون مرد کے مقابلے میں ناقص اور کم درجہ کا ہوتا ہے وعند الشافعي لا يقتل الحر اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک غلام کے بدلے قصاص میں آزاد کو قتل نہ کیا جائے گا کیونکہ غلام میں انسانی شرافت و کرامت کی اہمیت نہیں پائی جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں میں مساوات کے موجود نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے قاص ممنوع ہے وصیح امان المازون اور اجازت یافتہ غلام کا امن دینا معتبر ہے اس جملے کا خطف مصنف کے سابقہ قول بقتل " پر ہے یعنی چونکہ غلام عصمت و حفاظت کے بارے میں حر کے مشابہ ہے ماذون بالقتال کا امان دینا صحیح ہے ماذون بالقتال وہ غلام ہے جس کو آقاء نے کفار سے جہاد کرنے کی اجازت دیدی ہے۔ ماذون المتجازه اجازت سے مراد وہ غلام نہیں ہے جس کو آجانے تجارت کرنے کی اجازت دے رکھی ہے لانه لما اذنه المولى للقتال الخبازون بالقتال سے امان دینے کی صحت کی وجہ یہ کہ جب آقا نے غلام کو کفار سے جہاد میں شرکت کی اجازت دیدی ہے تو مال غنیمت میں شریک ہوگا پس اپنے نفس کے حق میں امان دینا تو مولی کی طرف سے قصدا ہے پھر اس کے ضمن میں اس کی اجازت بھی شمار ہو جائے گی جو غلام غیر کے حق میں امان کا استعمال کرتا ہے مصنف نے متن میں عید کے ساتھ مازون کی قید اس نے بڑ ھالیا ہے کہ کیونکہ عبد مجور سے امان دینے کی صورت میں اختلاف ہے پس امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک سیع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کو جہاد میں شرکت کا حق نہیں ہے تاکہ اس کے بارے میں کہا جاسکے کہ یہ اپنے نفس کے حق کے ساقط کرنے والا ہے اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک عہد مہجور کا امان دینا صحیح ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی دین اسلام کی مدد کرنے کا بحیثیت مسلمان اہل ہے ممکن ہے کہ اس میں بھی مسلمانوں کے لئے کوئی۔ مصلحت دیکھا ہو۔ وَإقْرَارة بالحدود والقصاص اور صحیح ہے اس کا اقرار کرنا حدود و قصاص کے متعلق یعنی عبد مازون کا ایسی چیز کا اقرار کر لینا درست ہے جو حدود قصاص کو واجب کرتا ہو اگر چہ اس میں عبد مهجور بھی اس کے اگرچہ ساتھ شریک ہے کیونکہ اس کا اقرار کرنا اس کے حق سے مل جائیگا جو اس کے نفس کے حق میں اس کو حاصل ہے یعنی دم اگر چہ ضمنا اس اقرا کے صحیح جاننے میں مولی کے مالی حق کا اختلاف ہلاک کرنا لازم آتا ہے (مگر چونکہ یہ ضمنا ہے اس لئے اس کا اختیار نہیں کیا گیا۔ وبالسرَقَةِ الْمُسْتَهْلَكَةِ أوَ الْقَائِمَةِ فَيَجِبُ القَطْعُ في المُسْتَهْلُكَةِ وَلَأَصْحَانُ عَلَيْهِ لأنَّهُ لا يَجْتَمِعُ مَعَ الْقَطْعِ وَيُرَدُّ الْمَالُ فِي الْقَائِمَةِ إِلى المَسرُوقِ مِنْهُ وَيَقْعُ وَهَذَا كلة فِي الْمَادُون وَفِي الْمَجُ اخْتِلافُ أَي إِنْ أَقَرَّ الْعَبْدُ الْمَحْجُورُ بالسرقة فَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَالُ مَالِكًا قُطِعَ وَلَأَصْحَانَ وَإِنْ كَانَ قَائِمًا فَإِنْ صَدقَة الْمَوْلَى قُطِعَ وَيُرَدُّ إِنْ كَذَّبَهُ الْمَوْلى فَفِيهِ اخْتِلافُ فَعِنْدَ أبي حَنِيفَةً يُقْطَعُ وَيُرَدُّ وَعِندَ أَبِي يُؤسف وَيُقْطَعُ وَلا يُرَدُ وَلكِنْ يَضْمِنُ مِثْلَهُ بَعْدَ الإِعْتَاقِ وَعِنْدَ مُحمدٍ لا يُخْلُعُ وَلا وَلاَيُرَدُّ
And the remaining honors are an additional quality in the free person, qisas is not based upon it as occurs between male and female, even though the blood-money of the female is less than that of the male. According to al-Shafi'i, a free person is not killed for a slave due to the lack of human honor capacity, so qisas is prevented due to lack of equality. And the aman of the authorized (ma'dhun) slave for fighting is valid, not the authorized for trade with the disbelievers, because when the master permitted him for fighting, he becomes a partner in spoils, so the aman is a disposal in his own right directly, then it becomes for others indirectly. He restricted it to the authorized because there is a dispute regarding the aman of the interdicted (mahjur) slave: according to Abu Hanifa it is not valid because he has no right in jihad to be able to drop his own right; according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i his aman is valid because he is a Muslim from the people of aiding the religion, and perhaps there is a benefit for the Muslims in it. And his iqrar (confession) regarding hudud and qisas: the iqrar of the ma'dhun slave for that which necessitates hudud and qisas is valid, even if the mahjur slave also shares in it, because his iqrar becomes binding on his own right which is the blood, even though the destruction of the master's property occurs indirectly. And the slave in this... And regarding theft of consumed or existing property: cutting is obligatory for consumed property, but [the hand] is not returned to him because it does not combine with cutting, and the property is returned to the victim in the case of existing property. All this applies to the ma'dhun slave. For the mahjur, there is a dispute: if he confesses to theft, if the property is destroyed, he is cut and not impaired? If it exists, if the master confirms him, he is cut and the property is returned; if the master denies him, there is a dispute: according to Abu Hanifa, he is cut and the property is returned; according to Abu Yusuf, he is cut and not returned, but he must guarantee its like after emancipation; according to Muhammad, he is not cut nor is the property returned.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal capacity of slaves in three areas: qisas, aman, and iqrar. The author first establishes that the slave is like a free person in terms of inviolability ('isma) for qisas, though not in honor (karamat). The proof is the Quranic principle 'a life for a life' (al-Ma'idah 5:45) which includes both free and slave. The Shafi'i objection based on lack of human honor is rejected because qisas is based on equality in life, not honor. Then the author addresses aman (granting safe conduct) by slaves. A ma'dhun slave (authorized for fighting) can give aman because he shares in spoils and thus has authority over his own right. But a mahjur slave (interdicted, not authorized) cannot give aman according to Abu Hanifa because he has no right in jihad; Muhammad and al-Shafi'i allow it for potential benefit to Muslims. Finally, iqrar (confession): a ma'dhun slave's confession for crimes entailing hudud (fixed punishments) or qisas is valid even if it affects the master's property indirectly, because the confession pertains to his own life. For theft by a ma'dhun, the rule is that if the stolen property is consumed, the hand is cut; if still existing, the hand is cut and the property returned. For a mahjur slave confessing theft, there is disagreement among the Hanafi masters: Abu Hanifa cuts the hand and returns the property; Abu Yusuf cuts but does not return, instead the slave guarantees after emancipation; Muhammad does not cut nor return. The passage concludes by highlighting the ikhtilaf (disagreement) in the case of mahjur.

Key Terms
مَأْذُون (ma'dhun): A slave authorized by his master for a specific purpose (fighting or trade).
مَحْجُور (mahjur): A slave interdicted from legal actions, not authorized by his master.
إِقْرَار (iqrar): Confession by a slave regarding a crime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the aman of a mahjur slave disputed?
A) Because he is not a Muslim.
B) Because he has no right in jihad to drop his own right.
C) Because his master has prohibited him from fighting.
D) Because the school cannot agree on whether he owns property.

Key Takeaway
A slave's capacity in aman and iqrar hinges on the master's authorization; the mahjur slave's acts are subject to significant ikhtilaf among the Hanafi masters.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Validity of Aman from a Slave Authorized to Fight
Expansion of a ruling on aman of authorized slave with qiyas reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers the aman of a slave authorized to fight as valid, and identify the usul principle (qiyas) used.

Core Idea
The authorized slave's aman is valid because he represents his master in war, just as a free person can grant aman.

This passage clarifies that a slave whom the master permits to fight may grant aman (safe passage) to an enemy. The commentary builds on the principle that a slave's inviolability is akin to that of a free person, and the master's permission for jihad implies representation in matters of war, including granting aman. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the analogical reasoning (qiyas) that connects the slave's capacity to the free person's capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the legal ruling: the aman of a slave authorized to fight (madhun bil-qital) is valid (sahih).
This is the explicit statement in the matn being expanded.
2
Understand the Basis: Inviolability
Recognize that the slave is similar to a free person in terms of 'ismah (inviolability). Therefore, the default capacity to grant aman is present.
The commentary highlights the analogy: 'the slave in terms of inviolability is similar to the free person'.
3
Analyze the Master's Permission
When the master authorizes the slave for fighting, the slave becomes a representative in jihad. This implies the master's implicit consent for actions like granting aman, since the slave shares in spoils.
The permission for fighting extends to ancillary war-related actions.
4
Reconstruct the Qiyas
Formalize the analogy: Asl (free Muslim) can grant aman; Far' (authorized slave) shares the same illa (capacity to waive his own right due to inviolability and representation). Thus, the ruling transfers.
The text uses qiyas jali: the slave's right is similar to the free person's right in inviolability.
5
Contrast with Restricted Slave
Note that this reasoning only applies to the authorized slave. The restricted slave (abd mahjur) lacks the capacity to participate in jihad, hence a dispute arises.
This sets up the next lesson's ikhtilaf.

Source Text

وصیح امان المازون اور اجازت یافتہ غلام کا امن دینا معتبر ہے اس جملے کا خطف مصنف کے سابقہ قول بقتل " پر ہے یعنی چونکہ غلام عصمت و حفاظت کے بارے میں حر کے مشابہ ہے ماذون بالقتال کا امان دینا صحیح ہے ماذون بالقتال وہ غلام ہے جس کو آقاء نے کفار سے جہاد کرنے کی اجازت دیدی ہے۔ ماذون المتجازه اجازت سے مراد وہ غلام نہیں ہے جس کو آجانے تجارت کرنے کی اجازت دے رکھی ہے لانه لما اذنه المولى للقتال الخبازون بالقتال سے امان دینے کی صحت کی وجہ یہ کہ جب آقا نے غلام کو کفار سے جہاد میں شرکت کی اجازت دیدی ہے تو مال غنیمت میں شریک ہوگا پس اپنے نفس کے حق میں امان دینا تو مولی کی طرف سے قصدا ہے پھر اس کے ضمن میں اس کی اجازت بھی شمار ہو جائے گی جو غلام غیر کے حق میں امان کا استعمال کرتا ہے مصنف نے متن میں عید کے ساتھ مازون کی قید اس نے بڑ ھالیا ہے کہ کیونکہ عبد مجور سے امان دینے کی صورت میں اختلاف ہے پس امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک سیع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کو جہاد میں شرکت کا حق نہیں ہے تاکہ اس کے بارے میں کہا جاسکے کہ یہ اپنے نفس کے حق کے ساقط کرنے والا ہے اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک عہد مہجور کا امان دینا صحیح ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی دین اسلام کی مدد کرنے کا بحیثیت مسلمان اہل ہے ممکن ہے کہ اس میں بھی مسلمانوں کے لئے کوئی۔ مصلحت دیکھا ہو۔
And it is valid that the authorized slave gives aman (security). The sentence is attached to the author's previous statement about qisas. Because the slave in terms of inviolability is similar to the free person. The aman of the slave authorized for fighting (madhun bil-qital) is valid. The authorized for fighting is the slave whom the master permitted to fight against disbelievers. The authorized for commerce is not meant. Because when the master permitted him for fighting, he will share in the spoils. So in his own right, giving aman is intended from the master, then in its implication his permission is also counted. The author in the matn restricted 'abd' with 'madhun' to exclude the restricted slave (mahjur). There is a difference: according to Abu Hanifa, it is not valid because he does not have the right to participate in jihad to be considered as one who can waive his own right. According to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, the aman of the restricted slave is valid because he is capable of assisting the religion of Islam as a Muslim; perhaps there is some maslaha (benefit) for Muslims in it.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the validity of aman (granting safe passage) given by a slave. It distinguishes between a slave authorized by his master to fight (madhun bil-qital) and a slave restricted (mahjur) from such activities. The commentary expands on the matn, explaining that the authorized slave's aman is valid because he represents his master in matters of war and spoils, and his action pertains to his own inviolability. For the restricted slave, there is an ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa holds it invalid because he lacks the capacity to waive his own right in jihad, while Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i consider it valid on grounds of general maslaha and the slave's inherent capability as a Muslim to support Islam.

Key Terms
مأذون بالقتال (madhun bil-qital): A slave whom the master has authorized to participate in fighting against disbelievers.
أمان (aman): A guarantee of safety granted to an enemy combatant or non-Muslim.
عبد محجور (abd mahjur): A slave restricted from financial and legal actions by the master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why is the aman of a slave authorized to fight valid?
A) Because the slave is a Muslim and every Muslim can grant aman.
B) Because the slave is similar to a free person in inviolability and represents his master in war.
C) Because the master can revoke the aman at any time.
D) Because the slave has full legal capacity like a free person.

Key Takeaway
The authorized slave's aman is valid because of his inviolability and the master's representation in war, established through qiyas.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
9 min
The Dispute on Aman from a Restricted Slave
Expansion introducing ikhtilaf on restricted slave's aman with opposing proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi dispute on the aman of a restricted slave and identify the usul principles (ahliyyah, maslaha) involved.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, restricted slave lacks the capacity to waive his own right, so his aman is invalid; for Muhammad, maslaha overrides.

The previous lesson established the validity of aman from a slave authorized to fight. This lesson turns to the case of a restricted slave (abd mahjur) who has not been given permission to fight. Here, a well-known ikhtilaf occurs: Imam Abu Hanifa holds the aman invalid, while his disciple Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i consider it valid. Analyzing this dispute reveals how differing usul principles — capacity (ahliyyah) versus public interest (maslaha) — lead to divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Issue
State the core question: Is the aman granted by a restricted slave (abd mahjur) legally valid and binding?
The restricted slave is one who is not authorized for fighting or trade; his actions are generally restricted by the master.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and Dalil
Abu Hanifa says the aman is invalid. His proof: the restricted slave does not have the right to participate in jihad, so he cannot be considered as one who can waive his own right (isqat haqq nafsih). Granting aman requires this capacity.
The key concept: isqat haqq nafsih — the ability to forgo one's own inviolability.
3
State the Opposing Position and Dalil
Imam Muhammad (Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i say the aman is valid. Their proof: the slave is a Muslim capable of aiding Islam; there may be maslaha (public benefit) in accepting his aman.
They prioritize the potential benefit over the technical lack of capacity.
4
Analyze the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: If the restricted slave grants aman, is it binding? Under Abu Hanifa, the aman is void; under the opposing view, it is binding.
The dispute has real-world implications for the safety of the person granted aman and for the Muslim army.
5
Understand the Usul Principles
Abu Hanifa emphasizes the principle that capacity (ahliyyah al-ada') must be present for the act to be valid. The opposing view emphasizes maslaha and the general capability of a Muslim to support Islam.
This is a classic tension between strict textual analogy (qiyas) and broader considerations of public good.

Source Text

وصیح امان المازون اور اجازت یافتہ غلام کا امن دینا معتبر ہے اس جملے کا خطف مصنف کے سابقہ قول بقتل " پر ہے یعنی چونکہ غلام عصمت و حفاظت کے بارے میں حر کے مشابہ ہے ماذون بالقتال کا امان دینا صحیح ہے ماذون بالقتال وہ غلام ہے جس کو آقاء نے کفار سے جہاد کرنے کی اجازت دیدی ہے۔ ماذون المتجازه اجازت سے مراد وہ غلام نہیں ہے جس کو آجانے تجارت کرنے کی اجازت دے رکھی ہے لانه لما اذنه المولى للقتال الخبازون بالقتال سے امان دینے کی صحت کی وجہ یہ کہ جب آقا نے غلام کو کفار سے جہاد میں شرکت کی اجازت دیدی ہے تو مال غنیمت میں شریک ہوگا پس اپنے نفس کے حق میں امان دینا تو مولی کی طرف سے قصدا ہے پھر اس کے ضمن میں اس کی اجازت بھی شمار ہو جائے گی جو غلام غیر کے حق میں امان کا استعمال کرتا ہے مصنف نے متن میں عید کے ساتھ مازون کی قید اس نے بڑ ھالیا ہے کہ کیونکہ عبد مجور سے امان دینے کی صورت میں اختلاف ہے پس امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک سیع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کو جہاد میں شرکت کا حق نہیں ہے تاکہ اس کے بارے میں کہا جاسکے کہ یہ اپنے نفس کے حق کے ساقط کرنے والا ہے اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک عہد مہجور کا امان دینا صحیح ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی دین اسلام کی مدد کرنے کا بحیثیت مسلمان اہل ہے ممکن ہے کہ اس میں بھی مسلمانوں کے لئے کوئی۔ مصلحت دیکھا ہو۔
And it is valid that the authorized slave gives aman (security). The sentence is attached to the author's previous statement about qisas. Because the slave in terms of inviolability is similar to the free person. The aman of the slave authorized for fighting (madhun bil-qital) is valid. The authorized for fighting is the slave whom the master permitted to fight against disbelievers. The authorized for commerce is not meant. Because when the master permitted him for fighting, he will share in the spoils. So in his own right, giving aman is intended from the master, then in its implication his permission is also counted. The author in the matn restricted 'abd' with 'madhun' to exclude the restricted slave (mahjur). There is a difference: according to Abu Hanifa, it is not valid because he does not have the right to participate in jihad to be considered as one who can waive his own right. According to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, the aman of the restricted slave is valid because he is capable of assisting the religion of Islam as a Muslim; perhaps there is some maslaha (benefit) for Muslims in it.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the validity of aman (granting safe passage) given by a slave. It distinguishes between a slave authorized by his master to fight (madhun bil-qital) and a slave restricted (mahjur) from such activities. The commentary expands on the matn, explaining that the authorized slave's aman is valid because he represents his master in matters of war and spoils, and his action pertains to his own inviolability. For the restricted slave, there is an ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa holds it invalid because he lacks the capacity to waive his own right in jihad, while Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i consider it valid on grounds of general maslaha and the slave's inherent capability as a Muslim to support Islam.

Key Terms
مأذون بالقتال (madhun bil-qital): A slave whom the master has authorized to participate in fighting against disbelievers.
أمان (aman): A guarantee of safety granted to an enemy combatant or non-Muslim.
عبد محجور (abd mahjur): A slave restricted from financial and legal actions by the master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the restricted slave is similar to a free person in inviolability.
B) Because the restricted slave may have been given permission by the master.
C) Because the restricted slave is a Muslim and there may be maslaha in it.
D) Because the aman of any Muslim is always valid.

Key Takeaway
The aman of a restricted slave is disputed: Abu Hanifa invalidates it due to lack of capacity, while Muhammad and al-Shafi'i validate it based on maslaha.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute on a Restricted Slave's Confession of Theft
Intra-Hanafi dispute on a restricted slave's confession of theft

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the restricted slave's confession of theft and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of each.

Core Idea
The hadd penalty and financial liability cannot combine, but the master's authority over a restricted slave splits the school into three rulings.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf concerning a restricted slave's (mahjur) confession of theft. While the authorized slave's (ma'dhun) confession leads to clear rules, the restricted slave's case triggers a three-way split among the school's founders: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this ikhtilaf illuminates how each imam weighed the principles of hadd, daman (financial liability), and the master's authority over the slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context and subject
Identify that the ruling concerns a restricted slave (mahjur) who confesses to theft. Distinguish this from the authorized slave case, which is clear.
The restricted slave lacks permission to trade; his confession does not bind his master.
2
Distinguish the state of the stolen property
Note that the ruling differs based on whether the stolen property is consumed (mustahlaka) or still existing (qa'ima). For consumed property, all agree on amputation and no payment. For existing property, the ruling further depends on whether the master confirms or denies the confession.
The text focuses on the scenario where the master denies the confession and the property is extant.
3
Map the three Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa rules: amputation (qat') and return of property. Abu Yusuf rules: amputation, no return, but the slave must guarantee the equivalent after emancipation. Muhammad rules: no amputation, no return, but the slave must guarantee the equivalent after emancipation.
Each position represents a different resolution of the tension between hadd and property rights.
4
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequences differ: under Abu Hanifa, the victim gets property back and the hadd is applied; under Abu Yusuf, the hadd is applied but the victim only gets compensation after freedom; under Muhammad, no hadd and only delayed compensation.
The disagreement shows how prioritizing the master's denial or the hadd text changes the outcome.
5
Reflect on the underlying usul principles
All imams agree that hadd and daman do not combine (لا يجتمع الحد مع الضمان). But they differ on whether the restricted slave's confession is effective against the master: Abu Hanifa considers it effective (like a free person), Abu Yusuf partially effective, and Muhammad ineffective. This reflects differing views on qiyas and istihsan.
The dispute is a classic example of ikhtilaf in tahlil (legal reasoning) within the same school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإقْرَارة بالحدود والقصاص اور صحیح ہے اس کا اقرار کرنا حدود و قصاص کے متعلق یعنی عبد مازون کا ایسی چیز کا اقرار کر لینا درست ہے جو حدود قصاص کو واجب کرتا ہو اگر چہ اس میں عبد مهجور بھی اس کے اگرچہ ساتھ شریک ہے کیونکہ اس کا اقرار کرنا اس کے حق سے مل جائیگا جو اس کے نفس کے حق میں اس کو حاصل ہے یعنی دم اگر چہ ضمنا اس اقرا کے صحیح جاننے میں مولی کے مالی حق کا اختلاف ہلاک کرنا لازم آتا ہے (مگر چونکہ یہ ضمنا ہے اس لئے اس کا اختیار نہیں کیا گیا۔ وبالسرَقَةِ الْمُسْتَهْلَكَةِ أوَ الْقَائِمَةِ فَيَجِبُ القَطْعُ في المُسْتَهْلُكَةِ وَلَأَصْحَانُ عَلَيْهِ لأنَّهُ لا يَجْتَمِعُ مَعَ الْقَطْعِ وَيُرَدُّ الْمَالُ فِي الْقَائِمَةِ إِلى المَسرُوقِ مِنْهُ وَيَقْعُ وَهَذَا كلة فِي الْمَادُون وَفِي الْمَجُ اخْتِلافُ أَي إِنْ أَقَرَّ الْعَبْدُ الْمَحْجُورُ بالسرقة فَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَالُ مَالِكًا قُطِعَ وَلأَصْحَانَ وَإِنْ كَانَ قَائِمًا فَإِنْ صَدقَة الْمَوْلَى قُطِعَ وَيُرَدُّ إِنْ كَذَّبَهُ الْمَوْلى فَفِيهِ اخْتِلافُ فَعِنْدَ أبي حَنِيفَةً يُقْطَعُ وَيُرَدُّ وَعِندَ أَبِي يُؤسف وَيُقْطَعُ وَلا يُرَدُ وَلكِنْ يَضْمِنُ مِثْلَهُ بَعْدَ الإِعْتَاقِ وَعِنْدَ مُحمدٍ لا يُخْلُعُ وَلا وَلاَيُرَدُّ يُرَدُّ بَلْ يَضْمِنُ الْمَالَ بَعْدَ الاعْتَاق وَدَلائل الكل في كتب الْفِقْهِ وَالْعَرْضِ اور تاہے اقرار کرنا چوری کے بارے میں خواہ مال ترجمہ تشریح مروق بلاک ہوچکا ہو یا موجود ہو نہیں بلاک شدہ میں قطع یہ واجب ہوگا اور اس پر تاوان واجب نہیں ہے کیوں کہ قطع ید کے ساتھ تاوان جمع نہیں ہوتا اور اگر مال مسروق موجود ہو تو اس کو مالک کو دیدیا جائے گا اور ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جائیگا یہ احکامات عید مازون کے لئے ہیں وفی المحجور اختلاف اور مجھور کے متعلق اختلاف ہے یعنی اگر عبد مجور چوری کرنے کا اقرار کرے پس اگر مال ہلاک ہو گیا ہے تو ہا تھ کان دیا جائے گا اور اس پر تاوان نہیں ہے اور اگر مال موجود ہو پس اگر آقا اسکی چوری کرنے کی تصدیق کر دے تو ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جائے گا اور مال واپس کر دیا جائے گا اور اگر مولی اس کی تکذیب کر دے تو اس صورت میں علما کا اختلاف ہے پس امام صاحب کے نزدیک ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا اور مال دلایا جائے گا اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جائے گا اور مال نہ واپس کیا جائے گا البتہ اس مال کے مثل کا تاوین دے گا آزاد ہو جانے کے بعد ۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک نہ ہاتھ کاٹا جائے اور نہ مال واپس کیا جائے بلکہ غلام آزاد ہونے کے بعد چوری کردہ مال کا تاوان اداء کرے ان حضرات کے دلائل کتب فقہ میں دیکھئے۔
And his confession regarding hudud and qisas is valid. That is, the authorized slave's confession of something that necessitates hudud or qisas is valid, even if the restricted slave is also partnered with him in it. Because his confession is attached to his own right that he has in his own person, i.e., blood. Even though incidentally in considering the confession valid, the master's financial right is destroyed. (But since it is incidental, it is not considered.) Regarding theft: if the stolen property is consumed or existing: amputation is obligatory for consumed property, and there is no liability for payment because it does not combine with amputation. For existing property, the property is returned to the owner and he is amputated. All this concerns the authorized slave. For the restricted slave, there is a difference: if the restricted slave confesses to theft, then if the property is destroyed, he is amputated and there is no payment. If the property exists, then if the master confirms, he is amputated and the property is returned. If the master denies, then there is a difference: according to Abu Hanifa, he is amputated and the property is returned; according to Abu Yusuf, he is amputated and the property is not returned, but he must guarantee its equivalent after emancipation; according to Muhammad, he is not amputated nor is the property returned, but he must guarantee the property after emancipation. The proofs of all are in the fiqh books.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal effect of a slave's confession (iqrar) regarding theft. It first states that an authorized slave's confession regarding acts that incur hadd or qisas is valid, even if it involves the master's financial interests, because it pertains to the slave's own right (his life/limbs). Then it turns to the specific case of theft. For the authorized slave: if the stolen goods are consumed (mustahlaka), amputation of the hand is wajib and no financial penalty (daman) is due because hadd and daman cannot combine. If the goods are still extant (qa'ima), the goods are returned to the victim and amputation is carried out. For the restricted slave (mahjur), there is a detailed ikhtilaf among the three Hanafi imams. The text summarizes the positions: Abu Hanifa: amputation and return of goods; Abu Yusuf: amputation but no return; instead, he must give an equivalent after being freed; Muhammad: no amputation and no return; instead, he must pay the value after freedom. The commentary notes that the proofs are in fiqh books.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission, especially of a crime or obligation.
مستهلكة (mustahlaka): Stolen property that has been consumed or destroyed, no longer extant.
قائمة (qa'ima): Stolen property that is still in existence.
عبد مأذون (abd ma'dhun): Authorized slave: a slave given permission by his master to engage in trade.
عبد محجور (abd mahjur): Restricted slave: a slave who is not permitted to trade; his actions are limited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, what happens when a restricted slave confesses to theft of existing property and the master denies?
A) Amputation is not carried out, but the slave must pay the value after freedom.
B) Amputation is carried out, the property is returned, and no payment is due.
C) Amputation is carried out, the property is not returned, but the slave must guarantee the equivalent after freedom.
D) Neither amputation nor return of property; the slave pays after freedom.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's internal ikhtilaf on the restricted slave's confession shows that legal principles (hadd, daman, master's authority) can be weighted differently, producing distinct rulings while remaining within the school.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Slave's Confession to Theft: Dispute Among Hanafi Imams
Explaining the dispute among Hanafi imams regarding a slave's confession to theft

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on an interdicted slave's confession to theft, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of each position.

Core Idea
An interdicted slave's confession to theft splits Hanafi imams on combining hadd and compensation.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the effect of a slave's confession to theft when the master denies it. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for appreciating how the principle of hajr (interdiction) interacts with criminal liability in Hanafi fiqh. The three eponymous imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—each offer a distinct ruling on the combination of the hadd punishment (hand amputation) and financial compensation (damān). By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate these positions and recognize their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two categories of slaves
Recognize that the passage first discusses the authorized slave (abd ma'dhun), then the interdicted slave (abd mahjoor). For the authorized slave, the ruling is uniform: hand is cut and property is returned if present; no compensation if lost.
This baseline is necessary to appreciate where the ikhtilaf arises.
2
Identify the point of ikhtilaf
Focus on the interdicted slave when the master denies the slave's confession. The disagreement concerns whether the hadd punishment can proceed without the master's confirmation and how compensation is handled.
The master's denial is the crucial variable.
3
State each imam's ruling
List the three positions: Imam Abu Hanifa: hand cut and property returned immediately. Imam Abu Yusuf: hand cut, compensation postponed until after emancipation. Imam Muhammad: no hand cut, only compensation after emancipation.
Memorize the positions clearly.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical difference: immediate vs. delayed financial burden on the slave/master, and the immediate application of hadd. This ikhtilaf affects how a mufti rules in contemporary analogous cases (e.g., employees, minors).
The thamarah is the consequence in real-world application.
5
Understand the methodological basis
Although the passage does not provide proofs, each imam's reasoning flows from differing views on whether the master's denial fully blocks the legal effect of the confession and whether hadd and compensation can be combined.
See fiqh books for detailed proofs, as the text directs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالسرقة المستملك أو القائمة اور تا ہے اقرار کرنا چوری کے بارے میں خواہ مال ہلاک ہو چکا ہو یا موجود ہو نہیں ہلاک شدہ میں قطع واجب ہوگا اور اس پر تاوان واجب نہیں ہے کیوں کہ قطع ید کے ساتھ تاوان جمع نہیں ہوتا اور اگر مال مسروق موجود ہو تو اس کو مالک کو دیدیا جائے گا اور ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جائیگا یہ احکامات عبد مأذون کے لئے ہیں وفی المحجور اختلاف اور محجور کے متعلق اختلاف ہے یعنی اگر عبد محجور چوری کرنے کا اقرار کرے پس اگر مال ہلاک ہو گیا ہے تو ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جائے گا اور اس پر تاوان نہیں ہے اور اگر مال موجود ہو پس اگر آقا اس کی چوری کرنے کی تصدیق کر دے تو ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جائے گا اور مال واپس کر دیا جائے گا اور اگر مولی اس کی تکذیب کر دے تو اس صورت میں علما کا اختلاف ہے پس امام صاحب کے نزدیک ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا اور مال دلایا جائے گا اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جائے گا اور مال نہ واپس کیا جائے گا البتہ اس مال کے مثل کا تاوان دے گا آزاد ہو جانے کے بعد ۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک نہ ہاتھ کاٹا جائے اور نہ مال واپس کیا جائے بلکہ غلام آزاد ہونے کے بعد چوری کردہ مال کا تاوان ادا کرے ان حضرات کے دلائل کتب فقہ میں دیکھئے۔
And concerning theft of stolen property or existing property: and confession about theft, whether the property has been destroyed or is present. If destroyed, amputation is obligatory and no compensation is obligatory because amputation and compensation are not combined. If the stolen property is present, it is given to the owner and the hand is cut off. These rulings are for the authorized slave (abd ma'dhun). And concerning the interdicted one (mahjoor), there is disagreement: If an interdicted slave confesses to theft, then if the property is destroyed, the hand is cut and there is no compensation on him. If the property is present, then if the master confirms his theft, the hand is cut and the property is returned. If the master denies, then in that case there is a disagreement among the scholars. According to Imam (Abu Hanifa), the hand is cut and the property is brought (returned). According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the hand is cut and the property is not returned, but he will give compensation equal to it after becoming free. According to Imam Muhammad, neither is the hand cut nor is the property returned; rather, the slave will pay compensation for the stolen property after becoming free. Their proofs are seen in the books of fiqh.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is a commentary discussing the ruling on a slave who confesses to theft. It first distinguishes between two types of slaves: the authorized slave (abd ma'dhun, permitted to trade) and the interdicted slave (abd mahjoor, restricted from transactions). For the authorized slave, the ruling is straightforward: if he confesses to theft, his hand is cut, and if the stolen property is still intact, it is returned to the owner; if lost, no compensation is due because the hadd punishment and monetary liability cannot be combined. For the interdicted slave, there is a difference of opinion among the three Hanafi masters when the master denies the confession. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the hand is cut and the property is returned (the slave must compensate from his own earnings if possible). Imam Abu Yusuf says the hand is cut but the property is not returned immediately; instead, after the slave becomes free, he compensates with an equivalent. Imam Muhammad says neither the hand is cut nor is the property returned; rather, after freedom, the slave pays compensation. The author directs the reader to fiqh books for the detailed proofs of each position. This ikhtilaf illustrates how the principle of hajr (interdiction) interacts with criminal liability.

Key Terms
المحجور (al-mahjoor): A slave who is interdicted from transactions and legal acts affecting property without the master's permission.
السرقة (al-sariqa): Theft meeting the conditions for hadd (e.g., nisab, hirs).
عبد مأذون (abd ma'dhun): An authorized slave permitted by the master to engage in trade and legal acts.
إقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission of a right or liability against oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on an interdicted slave who confesses to theft when the master denies?
A) Hand cut and no compensation.
B) Hand cut and compensation after freedom.
C) Hand cut and immediate return of property.
D) No hand cut, compensation after freedom.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi imams differ on the handling of an interdicted slave's confession to theft when the master denies, affecting the immediate application of hadd and compensation.

The Validity of Kafalah for a Deceased Muflis
Explains ruling on suretyship for a deceased bankrupt with dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kafalah for a deceased muflis and evaluate the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn using the concept of dhimma.

Core Idea
Kafalah requires a valid dhimma; a deceased muflis has no dhimma, so kafalah is invalid.

In this passage, we explore a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding suretyship for a person who died insolvent. The ruling hinges on the nature of dhimma (legal personality) after death. Understanding this dispute sharpens our ability to apply definitions and analogies in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What exactly is being disputed? The validity of kafalah for a deceased bankrupt (muflis) who left no estate or guarantor.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds it invalid because kafalah requires linking one dhimma to another; a deceased muflis lacks a valid dhimma.
The proof is based on the definition of kafalah.
3
State the Sahibayn's objection
The Sahibayn argue that death does not void debts; otherwise tabarru' and afterlife claims would be invalid.
They focus on the debt's survival.
4
Analyze the analogy with the interdicted slave
The slave has a complete dhimma due to life and reason, so kafalah is valid despite barriers to enforcement. This contrasts with the deceased muflis who lacks dhimma entirely.
The distinction is the existence of dhimma, not enforceability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: followers of Abu Hanifa do not allow suretyship for a deceased muflis; followers of the Sahibayn allow it. The ruling also applies to similar cases of dhimma extinction.
The definition of dhimma determines the outcome.

Source Text

الميت المفلس لا تصح امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ مفلس میت کی طرف سے اس کے دین کا کفیل ہو پیچ ں ہے جبکہ بحالت حیات اس کا کوئی کفیل باقی نہ رہا ہو کیونکہ کھال ایک ذمہ کو دوسرے ذمہ سے بلانے کا نام ہے۔ پس جب میت کا ذمہ ہی معتبر باقی نہیں رہا تو کفیل کے ذمہ کو اس کے ذمہ ساتھ کیونکر ملایا جاسکتا ہے بخلاف اس کے کہ اسکی زندگی کی حالت میں اس کے پاس مال رہا ہو یا اس کا کوئی کھیل رہا ہو تو چونکہ اس کا ذمہ کامل ہے تو اس صورت میں میت کی طرف سے کفالت صحیح ہے۔ اس کے بر خلاف اگر کسی شخص نے میت کی طرف سے بغیر کفالت کے تبرع کیا تو یہ درست ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ مفلس میت کی طرف سے کفالت درست ہے کیونکہ موت دین کو بری کر دینے والی مشروع نہیں ہوئی ہے اور اگر میت بری ہو گیا تو تبرع کرنے والے سے قرض کا لے لینا درست نہ ہوتا اور نہ آخرت میں مطالبہ کرنے کا ہی کوئی حق ہو تا۔ بِخِلَافِ العَبْدِ المَحْجُورِ الَّذِي يَقِرُّ بِالدِّيْنِ خلاف عبد مجور کے جو دین کا اقرار کرتا ہو پھر اس کی کفالت کسی آدمی نے کرلی ہو تو درست ہے اگر عبد سے مطالبہ کا حق نہیں ہے اس کی آزادی سے پہلے لان دَمَّتَهُ فِي حَقْهِ كَامِلَةٌ کیونکہ غلام کا ذمہ بذات خود کامل ہے زندگی اور عقل کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اور مطالبہ بھی فی الجملہ ثابت ہے اذيتصور أن يَصدَقَهُ مَوْلاً، أو يُعتقہ اس وجہ سے کہ ممکن ہے کہ آقا اسکی تصدیق کر دے یا اس کو آزاد کر دے تو غلام سے فی الحال مطالبہ کیا جاسکتا ہے جب اسکی طرف سے مطالبہ صحیح ہے تو کفالہ بھی اس کی طرف صحیح ہے لیکن فرق اتنا ہے کہ کفیل سے دین کا مطالبہ فی الحال بھی ہو سکتا ہے اگر چہ اس کفیل کا امیل ایک ایسا غلام ہے جس کو خرید و فرخت سے رد کردیا گیا ہے اور فی الحال اس سے قرض کا مطالبہ بھی نہیں کیا جاسکتا کیونکہ اس کے حق میں مانع موجود ہے اور کفیل سے مانع زائل ہو چکا ہے
The deceased bankrupt (muflis) is not valid (for kafalah). Imam Abu Hanifa said: Kafalah for the debt of a deceased muflis is not valid when no guarantor remained during his life, because kafalah is linking one dhimma to another. So when the dhimma of the deceased is no longer valid, how can the surety's dhimma be attached to it? In contrast, if during his life he had property or had a guarantor, then because his dhimma is complete, kafalah on his behalf is valid. On the contrary, if a person made a tabarru' (gratuitous payment) on behalf of the deceased without kafalah, it is valid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Kafalah for a deceased muflis is valid because death is not legislated to void debts. If the deceased were discharged, then taking the debt from the donor would not be valid, nor would there be any right to demand in the Hereafter. Unlike the interdicted slave ('abd mahjur) who acknowledges a debt, then someone stands surety for him – it is valid, even though the slave cannot be demanded before his emancipation, because his dhimma is inherently complete due to life and reason. Demand is established in some sense, because it is possible that the master may confirm or emancipate him, so demand can be made immediately. Since demand on his behalf is valid, kafalah on his behalf is valid. But the difference is that the debt can be demanded from the surety immediately, even if the surety's principal (the slave) is one who is restricted from buying and selling and cannot be demanded immediately because there is a barrier in his case, while the barrier has been removed from the surety.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents a fiqh ruling regarding surety (kafalah) for a deceased person who died insolvent. Abu Hanifa holds that such kafalah is invalid because kafalah requires a valid dhimma (legal personality) to which the surety's dhimma is attached. Upon death, the dhimma of a muflis (bankrupt) is considered non-existent for matters of liability, as he left no estate. However, if he had property or a guarantor during life, his dhimma is considered complete, and kafalah is valid. The Sahibayn disagree, arguing that death does not eliminate debts; otherwise, gratuitous payments (tabarru') on his behalf would be meaningless, and there would be no accountability in the Hereafter. The author then contrasts the case of an interdicted slave (who cannot be sued for debts during his restriction) but whose dhimma is intact due to life and reason. Kafalah for such a slave is valid because the slave's dhimma is complete, and demand can be made upon emancipation. The surety can be demanded payment immediately because the barrier (the slave's restriction) does not apply to the surety. This ruling is based on rational analysis of the nature of dhimma and the purposes of kafalah. It falls under the category of fiqhi ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
كفالة (kafalah): Linking one dhimma to another for a debt
ذمة (dhimma): Legal personality/capacity entailing obligations
مفلس (muflis): A bankrupt person with no property to pay debts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is kafalah invalid for a deceased bankrupt?
A) Because the deceased is no longer alive
B) Because the deceased lacked a valid dhimma
C) Because the Sahibayn opposed it
D) Because tabarru' is not valid

Key Takeaway
Kafalah requires a valid and attachable dhimma; a deceased muflis lacks this, rendering suretyship void unless he had property or a guarantor during life.
